- [x] BadStateRootSignature evidence verification: `consensus::state_root_sig_pre_image` (canonical FALCON pre-image per Ch 6 ¬ß12); two contradictory roots, both sigs verify under accused's pubkey ‚Äî PR [#26](https://github.com/pyde-net/engine/pull/26)
- [x] BadAnchorAttestation evidence verification (self-contained `honest_majority: Vec<Vertex>` payload; 85+ distinct-member witnesses must agree on a different prior anchor; ~290 KiB per evidence under 4 MiB gossipsub cap) ‚Äî PR [#27](https://github.com/pyde-net/engine/pull/27)
- [x] BadDecryptionShare evidence verification: self-contained payload (`share`, `ciphertext`, `share_pubkey`); `verify_evidence` gains `&dyn DkgProtocol` parameter; checks signer match ‚Üí FALCON sig over `share_signature_pre_image` ‚Üí `verify_decryption_share` returns false. Caller pre-validates `share_pubkey` against chain state. **Safety-offense evidence catalog is now complete.** ‚Äî PR [#53](https://github.com/pyde-net/engine/pull/53)
- [x] Evidence-to-escrow pipeline: `process_evidence(evidence, stake, verifier, slasher, escrow) ‚Üí ProcessOutcome` ‚Äî verify ‚Üí slash ‚Üí escrow in one call, plus convenience builders for the three verified Safety payloads + `preview_slash` for RPC dry-runs. Resolution of `InsertOutcome::Equivocation` ‚Üí Vertex stays in node binary (Œ≥.5) ‚Äî slashing doesn't observe consensus state directly. ‚Äî PR [#32](https://github.com/pyde-net/engine/pull/32)
- [x] **BadStateRootSignature detector ‚Üí slashing pipeline** ‚Äî Œ≥.slashing.bad-state-root-sig: closes the wire that `StateRootSigBuffer`'s `InsertOutcome::Equivocation` had set up but nothing was consuming. State-root-sig double-signs now flow into the slashing pipeline the same way vertex equivocations do via Œ≥.mc2 #145. **Buffer surface change:** `InsertOutcome::Equivocation` upgraded from a unit variant ‚Üí `{ prior: StateRootSig, new: StateRootSig }` so consumers can build evidence directly from the outcome. New `equivocation_sink: RwLock<Option<UnboundedSender<...>>>` + `set_equivocation_sink` / `clear_equivocation_sink` mirroring `VertexStore::set_equivocation_sink`. Sink emits `StateRootSigEquivocationDetected { signer_id, commit_id, prior, new }`. Receiver-drop silently swallowed (send-or-drop) so a slow consumer can't hold up subsequent inserts. **New `BadStateRootSigConsumer` (mirrors `EquivocationConsumer`):** drains the buffer's equivocation channel, builds evidence via `pyde_engine_slashing::build_bad_state_root_sig_evidence`, runs through `process_evidence` ‚Üí `Slasher` + `Escrow`, persists slasher + escrow snapshots after each successful slash via `with_persistence` (Œ≥.slashing.persistence + escrow-persistence pattern from #160 + #161). v1 stubs identical to the `EquivocationConsumer`: `AcceptingVerifier`, `MockDkg`, `DEFAULT_EPOCH`, `DEFAULT_STAKE` ‚Äî the buffer's own slot-collision detection is the meaningful gate at v1; tightening lands with the committee registry. **Validator wiring:** spawns a new `bsrs_task` alongside the equivocation consumer + joins on shutdown. Two new metrics: `bad_state_root_sig_consumer_processed` + `bad_state_root_sig_consumer_rejected`. **7 new tests:** 3 buffer (sink fires on equivocation / sink swallows receiver-drop / no-sink-attached still surfaces outcome to caller); 4 consumer (happy-path slash / matching-roots rejection via `verify_evidence`'s defensive check / run-drains-then-exits / run-exits-on-shutdown). 1687 workspace tests passing (was 1680; +7). All 4 CI gates green. **Detector status update:** of the 9 offenses in the catalog, 2 now have running detectors in the validator binary ‚Äî `Equivocation` (vertex double-sign, #145) + `BadStateRootSignature` (this PR). The remaining 7 (`BadAnchorAttestation`, `InvalidVertexStructure`, `BadDecryptionShare`, `DkgParticipationFailure`, `DecryptionShareWithholding`, `ExtendedDowntime`, `BadBatchAttestation`) need detectors using the same `with_persistence`-style pattern; several depend on subsystems that haven't shipped yet (DKG production protocol, threshold-decryption ceremony, downtime tracking). ‚Äî PR [#164](https://github.com/pyde-net/engine/pull/164)
- [x] **InvalidVertexStructure detector ‚Üí slashing pipeline** ‚Äî Œ≥.slashing.invalid-vertex-structure: 3rd of 9 catalog offenses to get a running detector. Vertices that gossip in with `DuplicateBatchRefs` or `InsufficientParentQuorum` (the two members of `StructuralViolation`'s slashable subset) are now dropped from the local DAG and the producer is slashed through the same pipeline as `Equivocation` (Œ≥.mc2 #145) + `BadStateRootSignature` (Œ≥.slashing #164). **Consensus crate:** new `detect_slashable_structural_violation(vertex, quorum) -> Option<ConsensusError>` ‚Äî pure check, no DAG / verifier / committee table needed; returns the first slashable violation found. Cheap enough for the receive-path hot loop. **Node crate:** new `crates/node/src/invalid_vertex_structure_consumer.rs` mirrors `EquivocationConsumer` + `BadStateRootSigConsumer` pattern. Drains detection events ‚Üí `build_invalid_vertex_structure_evidence` ‚Üí `process_evidence` ‚Üí slasher + escrow ‚Üí snapshot persistence. Same v1 stubs as peer consumers (`AcceptingVerifier`, `MockDkg`, default epoch + stake). New `InvalidVertexStructureDetected { accused, vertex, code, reporter }` event type ‚Äî carries the bad vertex itself in the payload so the consumer can build evidence without going back to the (now-empty) store. **Mainloop wiring:** `ValidatorMainLoop` gains optional `set_invalid_vertex_structure_sink` (mirrors `VertexStore::set_equivocation_sink` discipline ‚Äî drop-on-no-receiver, fire-and-forget). `dispatch` gains a 9th param threading the sink through. `handle_vertex_bytes` calls `detect_slashable_structural_violation` BEFORE insert; on violation ‚Üí emit event + drop vertex (no insert). **Detection is gated on the sink being attached** ‚Äî tests that pass `None` skip the check, preserving pre-slashing semantics for the 30+ existing dispatch tests that build vertices without 85 parents. **Validator binary:** constructs the channel BEFORE the mainloop task spawns so the first dispatch sees `Some(tx)`. Joins the new consumer on shutdown alongside the other consumers. **3 new metrics:** `invalid_vertex_structure_detected` (gossiped vertices dropped by the pre-check) + `invalid_vertex_structure_consumer_processed` + `invalid_vertex_structure_consumer_rejected`. **12 new tests:** 5 detector helper (clean / duplicate / insufficient parents / genesis-no-parent-check / duplicate-takes-precedence); 5 consumer (happy-path dup-batch-refs / happy-path insufficient parents / clean-vertex rejected by `verify_evidence`'s defensive check / run drains-and-exits / run exits on shutdown); 2 mainloop (dup-batch-refs gets dropped + routed to sink / no-sink-attached skips detection entirely). 1699 workspace tests passing (was 1687; +12). All 4 CI gates green. **Detector status update:** 3/9 catalog offenses have running detectors now ‚Äî `Equivocation` (#145) + `BadStateRootSignature` (#164) + `InvalidVertexStructure` (this PR, #165). Remaining 6 mostly block on subsystems not yet shipped (DKG production protocol, threshold-decryption ceremony, downtime tracking, Œ≤'s batch validation). `BadAnchorAttestation` is the only one whose dependencies are already in tree ‚Äî consensus subsystem exists, detector wire pending. ‚Äî PR [#165](https://github.com/pyde-net/engine/pull/165)
- [x] **BadAnchorAttestation detector ‚Üí slashing pipeline** ‚Äî Œ≥.slashing.bad-anchor-attestation: 4th of 9 catalog offenses to wire a running detector. New `crates/node/src/anchor_attestation_buffer.rs` tracks per-round `prev_anchor_attestation` claims keyed by `(round, attested_anchor)`. When some bucket crosses QUORUM (= 85 distinct members) it locks the majority for that round; every other attester is flagged as a slashable minority and emitted on a detection sink via `BadAnchorAttestationDetected { accused, disputed, honest_majority }` (the full majority vertices are snapshotted so the consumer can build evidence without re-querying any store). The buffer also handles late-arriving minorities (post-`MajorityReached`) via `InsertOutcome::LateMinorityFlagged`. New `BadAnchorAttestationConsumer` mirrors the IVS/BadStateRootSig consumer pattern: drains the channel, calls the new `build_bad_anchor_attestation_evidence` slashing-crate builder, runs `process_evidence`, persists slasher + escrow snapshots to RocksDB. Unlike `InvalidVertexStructure`, the disputed vertex is structurally well-formed (dispute is purely about its attestation content, not its parent quorum or batch refs), so it stays in the local DAG ‚Äî the wave-committer can still use it; only the producer is slashed. Wired into `ValidatorMainLoop` alongside the IVS sink; spawned in the validator binary alongside the equivocation / bad-state-root-sig / invalid-vertex-structure consumers. Remaining 5 of 9 offenses (BadDecryptionShare, DkgParticipationFailure, DecryptionShareWithholding, ExtendedDowntime, BadBatchAttestation) block on subsystems not yet shipped (DKG production protocol, threshold-decryption ceremony, downtime tracking, Œ≤ batch validation). ‚Äî PR [#166](https://github.com/pyde-net/engine/pull/166)
- [x] **Slasher snapshot to RocksDB** ‚Äî Œ≥.slashing.persistence: closes the slasher half of the roadmap "Persistence: Slasher + Escrow to RocksDB" line. Validators now resume their offense log + jail map across restarts instead of losing slashing state on every node bounce. **Design:** new `SlasherSnapshot { offenses: Vec<((u64, u32), Vec<Offense>)>, jail_until: Vec<(u32, u64)> }` borsh-serialisable + sorted by `(epoch, accused)` / `accused` ascending so byte output is deterministic regardless of HashMap iteration order. New `Slasher::snapshot()` + `Slasher::restore(snap)` inverses. **Layout:** `ConsensusStore` gains `CF_SLASHER` with `SLASHER_SNAPSHOT_KEY = b"snapshot"` ‚Äî v1 has rare slashing events so "rewrite whole snapshot on every record" is negligible; future versions can shard by epoch if needed. New `ConsensusStore::put_slasher_snapshot` / `get_slasher_snapshot`. **Runtime resume:** `ValidatorRuntime::build()` calls `get_slasher_snapshot()` at startup and `Slasher::restore` if `Some`; falls back to fresh `Slasher` with a `warn` log on read failure (same "better to lose the resume than crash the node" discipline as `BeaconStore::resume_from_store` from Œ≥.mc2 #147). **Consumer wiring:** new `EquivocationConsumer::with_persistence(consensus_store)` builder. On `Ok(_)` from the detector, snapshot is taken + put to disk. Persist failure logs at `error` + bumps new `slasher_persistence_failures` metric; in-memory state already reflects the slash so the failure is bounded by "one event lost on subsequent crash". 12 new tests: 6 slasher (empty / offense-log roundtrip / jail_until roundtrip / byte-determinism / borsh roundtrip / clear_jail propagates), 3 consensus_store (empty / put+get / overwrite), 1 runtime (restart resume), 2 consumer (with/without persistence). 1663 workspace tests passing (was 1651; +12). All 4 CI gates green. **Out of scope (next slice):** Escrow persistence (in-flight slash records during dispute window) ‚Äî same snapshot pattern fits cleanly; lands separately. Slasher writes from non-equivocation paths (BadStateRootSignature, BadAnchorAttestation, DecryptionShareWithholding, ExtendedDowntime, etc.) ‚Äî each needs a similar `with_persistence`-style attachment when those detectors land. ‚Äî PR [#160](https://github.com/pyde-net/engine/pull/160)
- [x] **Escrow snapshot to RocksDB** ‚Äî Œ≥.slashing.escrow-persistence (closes the second half of the original "Persistence: Slasher + Escrow to RocksDB" line; pairs with #160): same snapshot pattern as the slasher, now for the dispute-window escrow. Validators resume in-flight slash records across restarts so a crash during the dispute window doesn't double-enqueue or lose matured payouts. **Slashing crate:** `SlashBreakdown` + `EscrowStatus` + `EscrowEntry` gain `BorshSerialize`/`BorshDeserialize` derives; new `EscrowSnapshot { dispute_window_epochs, next_id, entries }` is borsh-serialisable + sorted by `EscrowId` for deterministic bytes; `Escrow::snapshot()` / `Escrow::restore(snap)` inverses. **Critical:** `Escrow::restore` preserves `dispute_window_epochs` from the snapshot (NOT a separate constructor arg) so a future refactor can't silently shift pending entries' effective maturity ‚Äî that would be a data-integrity hazard worse than crashing. **Node crate:** `ConsensusStore` gains `CF_ESCROW` + `put_escrow_snapshot` / `get_escrow_snapshot` under `ESCROW_SNAPSHOT_KEY` single-key layout. `ValidatorRuntime::build()` calls `get_escrow_snapshot` at startup; `Escrow::restore` if `Some`, `Escrow::new(config.dispute_window_epochs)` otherwise. `EquivocationConsumer::new` takes `escrow: Arc<Escrow>` as new param; on `Ok(_)` from the detector (after `process_evidence` enqueued the entry), BOTH slasher snapshot AND escrow snapshot persist. New `escrow_persistence_failures` metric for the latter. 9 new tests: 6 escrow snapshot/restore (empty / entries preserved with Pending+Voided status retained / next_id continuity for fresh enqueue / byte-determinism / borsh roundtrip / dispute_window preserved); 2 consensus_store (empty store ‚Üí None / put+get roundtrip); 1 runtime restart-resume test that asserts dispute_window_epochs is preserved from the snapshot. Existing slasher persistence test extended to also assert the escrow snapshot is persisted on the same dispatch. 1672 workspace tests passing (was 1663; +9). All 4 CI gates green. **Closes** the original roadmap line: with #160 (Slasher half) + #161 (Escrow half), validators now resume the full slashing state machine across restarts end-to-end. ‚Äî PR [#161](https://github.com/pyde-net/engine/pull/161)
- [x] Reward distribution math: `distribute_rewards(pool, entries)` pure function (pool √ó stake √ó uptime, sum-invariant bit-exact, u128-overflow-safe fallback, 6-decimal `UPTIME_PRECISION`) ‚Äî PR [#31](https://github.com/pyde-net/engine/pull/31)
- [ ] Reward distribution wiring: `UptimeTracker` from consensus attestation events + `RewardPool` epoch-accumulator (depends on Œ≥.1 attestation surface)

#### Œ≥.5 `node` crate `[SEQ within Œ≥] ‚Üí Œ≥.1 + Œ≥.2 + Œ≥.4` ‚Äî owned by Œ≥; integration point
- [x] `EquivocationDetector` ‚Äî node-level wiring between consensus's `InsertOutcome::Equivocation` and slashing's `process_evidence`. Composes Arc'd `VertexStore` + `Slasher` + `Escrow`; `handle_equivocation` looks up the prior, builds Evidence, runs the slash pipeline. Closes the resolution side noted in slashing.12. ‚Äî PR [#56](https://github.com/pyde-net/engine/pull/56)
- [x] `ValidatorRuntime` composition: holds disk-backed libp2p `Keypair` + Arc'd `VertexStore` + `Slasher` + `Escrow` + `ValidatorRegistry` + `EquivocationDetector` + `NetworkHandle`. `ValidatorRuntime::build(config)` returns `{ runtime, network_runner, network_events }` so caller controls tokio spawn; main loop consumes the event stream + uses the runtime. Foundation for the validator binary. ‚Äî PR [#58](https://github.com/pyde-net/engine/pull/58)
- [x] `ConsensusVertexProvider` + `BatchCache` + `BatchCacheProvider`: adapters that satisfy `pyde_engine_net::VertexProvider` / `BatchProvider` from `Arc<VertexStore>` + an in-memory `Arc<BatchCache>`. `ValidatorRuntime::build` wires real providers through `NetworkProviders` instead of the `new_null` placeholder; inbound vertex-fetch / batch-fetch requests now answer out of the runtime's authoritative storage. ‚Äî PR [#60](https://github.com/pyde-net/engine/pull/60)
- [x] `ValidatorMainLoop` + `dispatch()` + `MainLoopMetrics`: long-running tokio task that drains `NetworkEventStream` into the runtime's `VertexStore` + `BatchCache`. Routes vertices (gossip + fetch responses ‚Üí `VertexStore::insert`, counting `New` / `Duplicate` / `Equivocation`) and batches (gossip ‚Üí cache by decoded hash; fetch response ‚Üí cache by requested hash). 10 atomic counters surfaced via `MainLoopMetrics`. `tokio::select!` biased on a `watch::Receiver<bool>` shutdown signal. `NetworkEventStream::channel()` constructor added so tests drive the loop without a real libp2p swarm. Equivocation evidence dispatch deferred to follow-up (needs committee/DKG/stake oracle). ‚Äî PR [#63](https://github.com/pyde-net/engine/pull/63)
- [x] `VertexProducer` solo-validator task ‚Äî the chain's heartbeat. tokio task that ticks at a configurable interval (default 250 ms, `--producer-tick-ms <MS>`; `0`/omit = disabled), builds a fresh signed `Vertex` for the local validator's slot via `pyde_engine_consensus::VertexBuilder` + `select_parents`, FALCON-signs via the runtime's `FalconKeypair`, inserts into local `VertexStore`, publishes on `pyde/vertices/1`. `tokio::interval` with `MissedTickBehavior::Skip` so paused validators don't burst; `tokio::select!` biased on shutdown. Publish failures (no peers) bump a counter and the task keeps ticking. 2 new `MainLoopMetrics` counters (`vertices_produced`, `vertex_publish_failures`). End-to-end verified: `pyde validator --producer-tick-ms 100 ‚Ä¶` produces ~10 vertices/sec observable via `pyde_getMetrics`. Anchor selection + wave-commit walking + threshold decryption + DKG + committee rotation all land in follow-ups. ‚Äî PR [#93](https://github.com/pyde-net/engine/pull/93)
- [x] `WaveCommitter` task ‚Äî **the chain commits + replicates**. tokio task that ticks at a configurable interval (default 125 ms, `--committer-tick-ms <MS>`; `0`/omit = disabled), scans the local `VertexStore` for new anchor rounds, walks the causal sub-DAG via `pyde_engine_consensus::walk_subdag`, calls `assemble_wave_commit_record` with empty Œ≤-side inputs (state_root, events, included_txs all empty for now ‚Äî `StateMutator::commit_wave` populates these once Œ≤.3 ships), and persists via `consensus_store.put_wave`. `pick_anchor` selects the deterministic anchor for the round ‚Äî among honest slots (single vertex per `(round, member_id)`), the lowest `member_id` wins; equivocating slots are skipped. `committed: HashSet<VertexHash>` excludes prior-wave ancestors from each new walk; `prior_anchor_round` threads through correctly. Transient missing-anchor (peer vertex still propagating) waits for the next tick without advancing state; hard failures (assemble overflow, store IO) advance to avoid spinning. 3 new `MainLoopMetrics` counters (`wave_commit_attempts`, `waves_committed`, `wave_commit_failures`). End-to-end verified solo (PR [#97](https://github.com/pyde-net/engine/pull/97)): `pyde validator --producer-tick-ms 100 --committer-tick-ms 50` produced 13 vertices + committed 12 waves in 2s with 0 failures; `pyde_getWave(0..N)` returns real `WaveCommitRecord`s. Multi-validator (PR [#100](https://github.com/pyde-net/engine/pull/100)): `--validator-id <N>` (default 0; range `[0, 128)` enforced) threads through to `VertexProducerConfig::member_id`; two `pyde validator` instances with distinct ids that dial each other share a DAG and commit identical wave records (deterministic anchor selection makes both sides agree without VRF). VRF anchor selection wired in Œ≥.15 PR-2 (PR [#112](https://github.com/pyde-net/engine/pull/112)); N/3+1 quorum vote threshold + skip rules wired in Œ≥.16 (PR [#120](https://github.com/pyde-net/engine/pull/120)); sentry pattern still pending.
- [x] `pyde` binary ‚Äî validator mode shipped: `pyde validator --keypair <path> [--listen <addr>]‚Ä¶ [--dial <addr>]‚Ä¶ [--dispute-window-epochs N]` builds a `ValidatorRuntime`, spawns the libp2p runner + `ValidatorMainLoop`, waits for Ctrl+C, drains, exits. `run_validator(config, shutdown: F)` takes the shutdown future as a parameter so tests drive the lifecycle without installing a real signal handler. Prints a stable post-shutdown summary (PeerId hex, listen/dial addrs, all 10 mainloop counters). Full-node + light-client modes wire in later. ‚Äî PR [#67](https://github.com/pyde-net/engine/pull/67)
- [x] **`pyde devnet` long-running mode + prefunded accounts + banner** ‚Äî surfaced by otigen Phase 1 integration brief A4: foundation slice of the single-process devnet that contract authors hardcode against. `pyde devnet` (without `--smoke`) now launches a long-running single-validator loop. **Deterministic seed**: `devnet_secret(i) = Blake3("pyde-devnet-v1/" || i.to_le_bytes())` ‚Äî same 10 addresses + secrets every run on every machine. The `v1` prefix locks the algorithm for v1 mainnet (rotating requires a deliberate `v2` constant). **Genesis prefund**: each account credited via `DevnetState::credit` (default 10,000 PYDE = 10,000,000,000 quanta, configurable via `--prefund-amount`). **Startup banner**: chain_id (default `31337` ‚Äî the widely-recognised "don't replay on mainnet" dev-chain sentinel), prefund summary, copy-paste-friendly addresses + secrets ‚Äî stable format for downstream tests to grep. **Long-running wave loop**: `Devnet::run_one_wave` ticks on a configurable interval (`--tick-ms`, default 1000) so `wave_id` advances even with no pending txs. **Graceful Ctrl-C shutdown**: final report prints chain_id + prefund count + waves committed. **Out of scope (follow-up PR)**: JSON-RPC handlers wired to `DevnetState` (`pyde_sendRawTransaction` / `pyde_getBalance` / `pyde_getNonce` / `pyde_getReceipt` / `pyde_call`) ‚Äî the existing RPC scaffold is wired to the validator's `ConsensusStore`, so the devnet needs a parallel `DevnetState`-backed `RpcContext`. The banner currently shows `RPC server: (not yet wired ‚Äî follow-up PR)` to set expectations. The `--fork <RPC>` flag (brief A6) is blocked on the state-snapshot protocol shipping. **Test surface**: 8 new runner tests in `devnet::runner::tests` (seed stability + distinctness + banner-hex helper + prefund-state credit + shutdown-signal exit + idle-tick wave progress) + 2 new CLI tests (defaults + custom flags parsing). Node lib total: 355 ‚Üí 364. Live binary smoke verified: `cargo run --bin pyde -- devnet --tick-ms 100 --prefund-count 3` prints banner + 3 deterministic accounts + runs until Ctrl-C. ‚Äî PR [#172](https://github.com/pyde-net/engine/pull/172)
- [x] **`pyde devnet` JSON-RPC server + `--rpc-listen` flag** ‚Äî closes the otigen Phase 1 A4 unblock kicked off by #172. The long-running devnet now binds a JSON-RPC 2.0 server backed by `DevnetState` so `otigen deploy` against `pyde devnet` works end-to-end. **New flag**: `pyde devnet --rpc-listen 127.0.0.1:8545` (port matches the de-facto Ethereum-RPC port that wallet libraries already target so they work without reconfig); omit for banner-only mode. **5 methods**: `pyde_chainId` (hex u64), `pyde_sendRawTransaction` (borsh-encoded `Tx` hex ‚Üí tx hash hex; submits + commits one wave so receipt is queryable immediately), `pyde_getBalance` (hex u128), `pyde_getTransactionCount` (hex u64 next nonce derived from `NonceWindow.base + bitmap.trailing_ones()`), `pyde_getTransactionReceipt` (receipt JSON or null). Names mirror the `eth_*` JSON-RPC shape with the `pyde_` prefix so wallet libs port over by string substitution. **Wire format**: `0x`-prefixed lowercase hex throughout, JSON-RPC 2.0 single + batch + notification handling, standard error codes (`-32700` parse, `-32600` invalid request, `-32601` method not found, `-32602` invalid params, `-32603` internal); notifications get `204 No Content` per spec. **Receipt persistence**: `DevnetState` now stores receipts indexed by `TxHash` (`receipts: HashMap<TxHash, Receipt>` on `Inner`); `commit_wave_with_resolved_txs` inserts as it builds; `get_receipt(&tx_hash)` accessor serves the RPC. **Lifecycle**: RPC server binds up-front (port-conflict errors surface before the banner prints), serves alongside the tick loop under the same shutdown watch, drains cleanly on Ctrl-C; banner shows the live RPC URL when bound, falls back to "(disabled ‚Äî pass --rpc-listen to enable)" otherwise; final report adds `RPC bound: <addr>`. **Out of scope (separate follow-up PRs)**: `pyde_call` (view calls via `WasmExecutor` ‚Äî needs a separate context-build path), `pyde_getLogs` (event index), `pyde_blockNumber` (easy add once otigen exercises it), `--fork <RPC>` (brief A6; blocked on snapshot protocol). **Test surface**: 12 new RPC dispatch + handler tests in `devnet::rpc::tests` including an end-to-end `sendRawTransaction ‚Üí receipt ‚Üí balance` round trip + error paths (malformed JSON, missing `jsonrpc`, unknown method, bad hex, unknown tx hash) + batch requests + notifications; 1 new runner integration test (`run_devnet_with_rpc_listen_binds_and_reports_addr`) binding `127.0.0.1:0` and asserting on the OS-assigned port. Node lib total: 364 ‚Üí 377. **Live-verified**: `pyde devnet --rpc-listen 127.0.0.1:8547` responds to `pyde_chainId` with `0x7a69` (31337) and `pyde_getBalance` with `0x2540be400` (10,000,000,000 quanta default prefund). ‚Äî PR [#173](https://github.com/pyde-net/engine/pull/173)
- [x] **`pyde_waveId` RPC method (devnet)** ‚Äî Pyde's analogue of EVM `eth_blockNumber`. Pyde uses **wave** not block per the DAG-Mysticeti consensus model (HOST_FN_ABI ¬ß7.3 `wave_id`); the RPC method follows. New `DevnetState::current_wave_id()` accessor over `Inner.current_wave` (updated by every `commit_wave_with_resolved_txs`); `pyde_waveId` handler returns hex u64. **2 new tests** ‚Äî `wave_id_starts_at_zero_before_any_commits` + `wave_id_advances_after_send_raw_transaction` (proves the end-to-end send ‚Üí commit ‚Üí query cycle). **Live-verified**: `pyde devnet --rpc-listen 127.0.0.1:8548 --tick-ms 200` returns hex-encoded wave id that advances over idle ticks. Node lib total: 377 ‚Üí 379. **The other two A4 RPC extras (`pyde_call` view calls, `pyde_getEvents` event index) remain blocked on devnet WASM-contract deploy support** ‚Äî the devnet currently uses `DevnetExecutor` (native pre-flight only), so there are no deployed contracts to call against and no events emitted by `pyde::emit_event`. Documented as deferred-with-reason in `devnet/rpc.rs` module docs. Unblocks when devnet swaps in `WasmExecutor` + contract deploy plumbing (its own future workstream ‚Äî not on the immediate roadmap). ‚Äî PR [#174](https://github.com/pyde-net/engine/pull/174)
- [x] **wasm-exec: revert `pyde::emit_event` to `-> i32` per spec restoration (A11)** ‚Äî closes engine ask A11 from the otigen Phase 1 brief. Pyde-book commit b816592 (2026-05-28, doc-cleanup) tightened the spec's `emit_event` return type from `-> i32` to `-> ()` as a drive-by along with the (deliberate) variable-length storage redesign. The reclassification wasn't called out in the commit message + wasn't motivated by the storage redesign (events were always variable-length). Reverting restores the deliberate design + preserves the option for v2 (event ordinal, byte count, etc.) without a hard fork + stays consistent with `transfer` which is also a mutating op and `-> i32`. Spec restored (¬ß3.1 imports example + ¬ß3.4 return-shape table ‚Äî ¬ß7.5 was never drifted) in paired [pyde-book#211](https://github.com/pyde-net/pyde-book/pull/211). Engine: 4 inline WAT test fixtures pick up `(result i32)` + trailing `drop`; closure returns `Ok(0)` after the existing event push; module-doc updated to reflect `-> i32` + the reservation rationale. Unblocks 10+ otigen example contracts (counter-token, erc20-token, simple-multisig, vesting, merkle-claim-airdrop, etc.) that hadn't migrated. All 223 wasm-exec lib tests green. ‚Äî PR [#176](https://github.com/pyde-net/engine/pull/176)
- [x] **devnet now uses the production validator runtime (no parallel impl)** ‚Äî closes a deep architectural concern surfaced during the A4 follow-up review: the MC-2 spike's `Devnet` composer + `DevnetExecutor` + `run_smoke` scenario were parallel implementations that diverged from mainnet code paths, and a partial RPC migration was building on top of that divergence. **Fix**: deleted the spike orchestration (`composer.rs`, `executor.rs`, `smoke.rs`, `rpc.rs`, `tests/devnet_smoke.rs` + the `--smoke` CLI mode) and rewrote `devnet/runner.rs` to drive the **production validator runtime** in solo mode. Same `WasmExecutor` (via `WasmExecutorAdapter`), same `DevnetState` mutator (production validator already uses it as StateMutator substitute until the state crate's `commit_wave` lands), same `PydeMempoolView`, same `WaveCommitter`, same `Driver`, same `FalconBeaconScheme` (real PQ FALCON-512 beacon, ephemeral keypair, solo committee = `[self_pk]`). Only the network layer is stubbed: libp2p binds to ephemeral loopback, `producer_quorum = 1`, no peers, no mDNS. **Mainnet-side, non-breaking extension**: new `ValidatorPreRunHook` type (generic `Box<dyn FnOnce(&ValidatorRuntime) + Send>`) + `run_validator_with_hook` / `run_validator_until_ctrl_c_with_hook` variants. The hook fires once between `ValidatorRuntime::build` and task spawn. Production passes `None` ‚Äî zero behavior change. Future non-devnet uses include A6 state-snapshot loading at boot, integration-test state seeding, monitoring installation. Devnet uses it to pre-fund genesis accounts via `runtime.state.credit(addr, amount)` ‚Äî pre-funding now rides the production code path, not a devnet-specific side door. **Why this matters**: contract deploy + call + events + everything mainnet supports works on devnet automatically because devnet IS the mainnet flow minus consensus replication + networking. As mainnet matures (DKG ceremony, threshold-decryption execution, remaining 5 of 9 slashable offenses), devnet inherits with no devnet-side work. **Kept (production-load-bearing despite the "devnet" module name)**: `devnet/state.rs` (`DevnetState` ‚Äî used by `ValidatorRuntime`, `WaveCommitter`, mainloop), `devnet/wallet.rs` (`Wallet` ‚Äî vertex-producer test + devnet runner). **Devnet glue** (in `crates/node/src/devnet/runner.rs`): tempdir for libp2p keypair + FALCON keypair + ConsensusStore (auto-cleaned on drop, fresh chain per `pyde devnet` start); deterministic devnet validator FALCON secret from `Blake3("pyde-devnet-v1/validator")` (distinct domain from wallet secrets via the `/validator` suffix) so the validator pubkey is stable across restarts; pre-fund closure built from the deterministic wallet seeds, fed through `ValidatorPreRunHook`. **Banner unchanged externally**; internal flow now boots the real validator stack. **CLI**: `--smoke` flag removed; all other devnet flags unchanged (`--prefund-count`, `--prefund-amount`, `--chain-id`, `--tick-ms`, `--rpc-listen` ‚Äî `--rpc-listen` is a stub this PR, follow-up rewires devnet RPC against the production stack handles so contract deploy + call work end-to-end). **Live-verified**: `pyde devnet --tick-ms 200 --prefund-count 1` boot log shows `devnet: genesis pre-fund applied` (hook fired) + `validator: bound + dialing` (production validator runtime now drives the devnet) + `beacon scheme: FalconBeaconScheme committee_size=1 keypair=ephemeral committee=solo` (real PQ beacon running). 340 node-crate tests pass (was 379 ‚Äî dropped 39 with the removed spike modules: smoke + composer + executor + rpc + the integration test). ‚Äî PR [#175](https://github.com/pyde-net/engine/pull/175)
- [x] **devnet RPC now wired against the production validator runtime (A4 PR2)** ‚Äî closes the second half of the A4 follow-up that #175 explicitly deferred. New `devnet/rpc.rs` introduces `DevnetRpcContext` holding `Arc`-cloned production handles: `Arc<DevnetState>` (production state mutator + view), `Arc<PydeMempoolView>` (production mempool with full Œ≤.5 validation pipeline), and `Arc<ConsensusStore>` (production RocksDB-backed receipt store). 6 methods land: `pyde_chainId`, `pyde_waveId`, `pyde_sendRawTransaction`, `pyde_getBalance`, `pyde_getTransactionCount`, `pyde_getTransactionReceipt`. RPC server bound inside the `ValidatorPreRunHook` when `--rpc-listen` is supplied ‚Äî no mainnet-side surface change; the hook is the generic post-build / pre-spawn extension point added in #175. Uses `tokio::signal::ctrl_c` for its own shutdown ‚Äî same signal the validator binary listens for, so both shut down together. **Production-flow semantics**: unlike the deleted spike's `Devnet::submit_and_commit` ("instant-commit" per call), the production-stack path is async + tick-paced: `PydeMempoolView::insert(tx).await` runs the full validation pipeline (FALCON sig + balance + nonce + chain_id + structural + per-sender rate limit + dedupe) then returns immediately with the canonical tx hash; the production producer task picks up the tx on its next tick (~250 ms) and packs it into a vertex; the committer commits the wave on its next tick (~125 ms); the receipt is queryable via `pyde_getTransactionReceipt` once the wave commits (~250-500 ms after `sendRawTransaction`). otigen + similar clients should poll with ~100 ms backoff ‚Äî an "instant-commit" UX is a property of a single-process synchronous executor; Pyde's production stack is event-driven + tick-paced, so devnet inherits that timing. **Why this matters**: contract deploy + call + events automatically work because they go through the production execution path. As mainnet matures (DKG ceremony, threshold-decryption execution, remaining slashable offenses), devnet inherits with no devnet-side work. **Live-verified end-to-end**: `pyde devnet --rpc-listen 127.0.0.1:8549 --tick-ms 200 --prefund-count 1`: `pyde_chainId` ‚Üí `0x7a69` (31337), `pyde_waveId` ‚Üí `0x0` (idle ticks haven't committed yet), `pyde_getBalance` ‚Üí `0x2540be400` (10,000,000,000 quanta = prefund applied via the production `DevnetState::credit` path). Boot log: `devnet: rpc server bound addr=127.0.0.1:8549` + `validator: bound + dialing` + `beacon scheme: FalconBeaconScheme committee_size=1 keypair=ephemeral committee=solo`. ‚Äî PR [#177](https://github.com/pyde-net/engine/pull/177)
- [x] **contract execution gap close ‚Äî PR1/4: wire `StateStore` + `AccountStore` + `WasmExecutor` into `ValidatorRuntime`** ‚Äî first of a four-PR workstream that closes the contract-execution gap left by #177 (which wired the RPC against `DevnetState` but couldn't deploy + call contracts because `DevnetState` had no executor wiring). `ValidatorRuntime` gains three new fields ‚Äî `state_store: Arc<StateStore>` (RocksDB-backed, opened at `consensus_store_path.join("state_store")` so consensus + execution state share a directory parent + lifetime), `accounts: Arc<AccountStore>` (production account store wrapping the `StateStore`), `executor: Arc<WasmExecutor>` (singleton wasmtime engine + module cache per `WASM_ENGINE_DESIGN`). - [x] **contract execution gap close ‚Äî PR3/4: `DevnetState` handles `TxType::Deploy` + contract-targeted `Standard` via executor** ‚Äî wires the `WasmExecutor` into `DevnetState::commit_wave_with_resolved_txs` so contract deploys actually persist code + contract calls actually dispatch through wasmtime. Two new optional fields on `DevnetState` ‚Äî `executor: Option<Arc<WasmExecutor>>` + `state_store: Option<Arc<StateStore>>` ‚Äî set together via the new `with_contract_support(executor, state_store)` builder; `None` keeps the transfer-only behavior for tests. New `derive_contract_address(deployer, nonce)` derives contract addresses as `Blake3("pyde-contract-v1/" || deployer.bytes || nonce.le_bytes)`. - [x] **contract execution gap close ‚Äî PR4/4: `pyde_call` + `pyde_getEvents` RPC** ‚Äî closes the four-PR workstream. `pyde_call` binds the production `WasmExecutor` for view-mode contract calls against committed state. Builds a transient `HostContext` + `TxOverlay` over the production `AccountStore`; `view_mode=true` so any mutating host fn (`sstore`, `sdelete`, `transfer`, `emit_event`) traps with `ERR_FORBIDDEN` per HOST_FN_ABI ¬ß3.7 Layer 3. - [x] **wasm-exec: align `pyde::falcon_verify` return to spec (A9)** ‚Äî closes otigen Phase 1 follow-up A9. [HOST_FN_ABI ¬ß7.7](https://book.pyde.network/companion/HOST_FN_ABI_SPEC.html#77-cryptographic-primitives) declares `pyde::falcon_verify` returns `0` for valid + `ERR_SIGNATURE_INVALID` (`-17`, ¬ß4) for invalid ‚Äî the 0-is-success convention every other status-code-returning host fn uses. Engine returned the inverted `1`/`0` boolean. **Impact**: any contract following the spec convention (`falcon_verify(...) == 0` to authorize) silently treated invalid signatures as authorized. Concretely: `simple-multisig`, `dao-governance`, every otigen example contract that calls `pyde::falcon_verify` and checks `== 0` for success. Fix: 3 LOC change in `host_fns/crypto.rs` plus import of `pyde_engine_types::error::ERR_SIGNATURE_INVALID`; module doc reframed. Two existing end-to-end tests in `executor.rs` updated to assert spec-aligned values: `host_fn_falcon_verify_real_keypair_returns_zero` (was `_returns_one`, WAT traps if return != 0 ‚Äî uses `if unreachable end` directly on the return value), `host_fn_falcon_verify_tampered_sig_returns_err_signature_invalid` (was `_returns_zero`, WAT compares to `i32.const -17`). Trap semantics for malformed inputs (pubkey/sig rejected by pyde_crypto, oversize msg/sig) unchanged. All 223 wasm-exec lib tests green. Otigen-side follow-up: revert the temporary `"1"` expectation in `runner_engine::tests::phase_e_falcon_dsl_signs_and_verifies_end_to_end` back to `"0"` per the A1 unblock pattern. ‚Äî PR [#182](https://github.com/pyde-net/engine/pull/182)

- [x] **node: propagate configured `chain_id` through to mempool admission** ‚Äî closes the second of the two devnet drift surfaces flagged from the otigen deploy-loop integration test. - [x] **node: devnet prefund registers the wallet's FALCON pubkey as `auth_keys`** ‚Äî closes the last of the otigen deploy-loop integration drift surfaces. The devnet wallet has signed against real FALCON-512 since A16 part 1, but the prefund hook only ran `state.credit(addr, amount)` and never registered the corresponding pubkey on-chain. The mempool's admission check short-circuits on `AuthKeys::None` with "no auth keys; submit RegisterPubkey first" *before* the FALCON sig verify step ever runs, so every prefunded sender's first tx was rejected ‚Äî defeating the "ten ready-to-use wallets" devnet promise. The prefund flow now does both `state.credit(addr, amount)` and `state.set_auth_keys(addr, AuthKeys::Single(pubkey))` for every prefunded account; freshly-booted devnets accept signed txs from prefunded senders immediately. The combined step lives in a new `apply_prefund` helper so a unit test can drive it without spinning up the full `ValidatorPreRunHook` closure. **Test**: `devnet::runner::tests::apply_prefund_credits_and_registers_auth_keys` builds a real `DevnetState` over a tempdir-backed `StateStore` + `AccountStore`, applies prefund for three deterministic wallets, and asserts both `get_balance` and `get_auth_keys` return the expected values for each. Workspace all-green (1801 passed, 0 failed, 7 ignored); clippy clean. ‚Äî PR [#210](https://github.com/pyde-net/engine/pull/210)
- [x] **node: devnet wave-committer commits on solo committee size 1** ‚Äî closes engine ask A22. The wave-committer hardcoded the spec constants `COMMITTEE_SIZE = 128` + `QUORUM = 85` for anchor selection + support resolution. The devnet runs a single producer at slot 0; anchor selection lands at `Hash(beacon, round, prev_state_root) mod 128` which almost never picks slot 0, and even when it does the support stage waits forever for 85 supporters that no one ever produces. Every round resolved `AnchorResolution::Pending` and `pyde_waveId` stayed at zero indefinitely. **Fix**: threads `committee_size: u32` + `quorum: usize` through `WaveCommitterConfig` and `ValidatorRunConfig`, defaulting to the spec constants for mainnet but overridden to `(1, 1)` by `pyde devnet`'s `build_validator_config`. Production resolver now reads from config; the `resolve_anchor_with` helper subsumes the old `resolve_anchor_for_testing` (renamed, ungated). Startup info-logs land for the producer + committer spawn paths so the boot sequence is observable. `DevnetRunReport` gains a `final_wave_id` field driven by a state-capture handle the prefund hook fills. **Tests**: `wave_committer::tests::resolve_anchor_commits_in_solo_committee_size_one` asserts the resolver returns `Commit` against the local producer's own R+1 + R+2 vertices when `(committee_size, quorum) == (1, 1)`; `devnet::runner::tests::devnet_wave_id_advances_under_normal_tick` boots devnet at `tick_ms = 50`, sleeps 1500 ms, and asserts `report.final_wave_id >= 1`. - [x] **node: wire `SlashSubmitter` into the validator runtime** ‚Äî closes the runtime-side wiring deferred from #199. The submitter existed and `EquivocationConsumer` accepted one via `with_slash_submitter()`, but the runtime never called it at startup ‚Äî every spawned validator ran the equivocation detector without ever submitting a slash, so detected equivocations stayed paper tigers and `ValidatorRecord.stake` never reduced on-chain. The runtime now constructs a `SlashSubmitter` at startup with the local validator's signing keypair, the local mempool + account store + vertex store, and a v1-solo `StaticCommitteeLookup` populated with the local vertex-signing pubkey at `config.validator_id`. `EquivocationConsumer` receives the submitter before its task spawns; detected equivocations now flow through `submit_equivocation_slash ‚Üí mempool ‚Üí wave producer ‚Üí committer` end-to-end on solo devnet. The lookup stays a solo-only `StaticCommitteeLookup` for now; multi-validator runs need an on-chain `CommitteeLookup` that resolves `member_id` via `ValidatorRecord.pubkey` from chain state ‚Äî separate follow-up. BSRS / `InvalidVertexStructure` / `ExtendedDowntime` consumers still need their own `submit_*` evidence-builders on `SlashSubmitter` before they can be wired the same way (PR-3b / PR-3c follow-ups). Workspace all-green (1803 passed, 0 failed, 7 ignored); clippy clean. ‚Äî PR [#212](https://github.com/pyde-net/engine/pull/212)
- [x] **node: `BadStateRootSig` consumer auto-submits on-chain Slash (PR-3b/I)** ‚Äî second of the safety-detector wirings, mirroring #212 for the state-root-sig path. - [x] **tx + node: `handle_slash` dispatches structural evidence; IVS auto-slash wired** ‚Äî third of the safety-detector wirings. The on-chain `handle_slash` previously decoded `tx.data` as raw `SafetyEvidence` (two distinct FALCON-sig pairs), which fits Equivocation + BadStateRootSignature but excludes `InvalidVertexStructure` where the offender only signs ONE thing (the malformed vertex itself). This PR introduces a top-level `SlashEvidence` enum at the `tx.data` layer with discriminants `0x00 Safety(SafetyEvidence)` + `0x01 Structural(StructuralEvidence)`; the handler dispatches on variant. The structural verification: load offender record + status check, verify `vertex.falcon_sig` under `record.pubkey` over `vertex_sig_pre_image`, re-run `detect_slashable_structural_violation(&vertex, QUORUM)`, and confirm the resulting `ConsensusError` matches the declared kebab-case `reason`. Slots `0x02` (BadAnchor ‚Äî needs multi-validator `CommitteeLookup`), `0x03` (Liveness ‚Äî distinct evidence variant), and `0x04` (BadDecryptionShare ‚Äî needs DKG ceremony) are reserved on the enum. **SlashSubmitter** gains `submit_invalid_vertex_structure_slash` + `build_invalid_vertex_structure_slash_tx`. **InvalidVertexStructureConsumer** gains `with_slash_submitter()`; `dispatch` becomes async; successful in-memory records auto-submit the on-chain Slash; outcome lands on `invalid_vertex_structure_consumer_slash_tx_{submitted,failed}` metrics. The validator runtime passes the same `SlashSubmitter` to the IVS consumer. **Wire-format break**: existing `SafetyEvidence`-encoded `tx.data` is no longer valid; callers wrap in `SlashEvidence::Safety`. Pre-mainnet so no external consumers affected; chain-side tests + the two existing `SlashSubmitter` methods (equivocation + BSRS) updated accordingly. **Tests**: `tx::handlers::slash::tests::structural_evidence_*` (5 ‚Äî real violation slashes, invalid sig rejected, unknown reason rejected, clean-vertex rejected with `VertexIsActuallyValid`, mismatched-reason rejected with `ViolationMismatch`); `slash_submitter::tests::build_invalid_vertex_structure_slash_tx_produces_chain_verifiable_evidence` builds a real FALCON-signed malformed vertex and asserts the produced evidence verifies under the offender's pubkey via real `pyde_crypto::falcon::falcon_verify`; `..._rejects_unknown_offender` asserts `UnknownOffender` when the committee table lacks the slot. Workspace all-green (1812 passed, 0 failed, 7 ignored); clippy clean. ‚Äî PR [#215](https://github.com/pyde-net/engine/pull/215)
- [x] **node: devnet receipts indexed under canonical `tx_hash` (A23)** ‚Äî closes engine ask A23. `DevnetState::tx_hash` was computing `blake3(borsh(Tx including signature))` ‚Äî a sig-inclusive hash ‚Äî while the producer + RPC + `consensus_store` key transactions under the canonical sig-excluded hash from `pyde_engine_tx::tx_hash`. So `commit_wave_with_resolved_txs` successfully applied each admitted tx (sender nonce + balance updated via `AccountStore`) but stored the receipt under the wrong key. Every `pyde_getTransactionReceipt` call returned null even though the tx had committed; otigen's deploy loop hit `InclusionTimeout` because the canonical hash it returned to the caller never matched the receipt store's index. **Fix**: `DevnetState::tx_hash` delegates to `pyde_engine_tx::tx_hash`, bringing the receipt index into alignment with the canonical hash the rest of the chain uses. A test-only helper `run_devnet_until_shutdown_with_taps` lets integration tests observe the live `DevnetState` + mempool via shared `OnceLock`s populated by the pre-run hook, so the populated-mempool ‚Üí tx-included-in-wave path can be exercised without an RPC server. **Tests**: `devnet::runner::tests::devnet_includes_admitted_standard_tx_in_committed_wave` admits a signed Standard transfer via the captured mempool, ticks producer + committer ~30 times, and asserts the sender's nonce_window advances + balance drops; `devnet::runner::tests::devnet_includes_admitted_deploy_tx_in_committed_wave` admits a `TxType::Deploy` with a real `DeployData` envelope and asserts the canonical tx_hash resolves to a persisted receipt ‚Äî the specific failure mode from the A23 ask. Workspace all-green (1814 passed, 0 failed, 7 ignored); clippy clean. ‚Äî PR [#216](https://github.com/pyde-net/engine/pull/216)
- [x] **node: proptest locks `DevnetState::tx_hash` against `pyde_engine_tx::tx_hash`** ‚Äî A23 hardening. The original A23 fix (#216) corrected the receipt-index drift but nothing in the codebase would have stopped someone reintroducing a divergent local hash six months from now. Two proptest-style invariants now run across an arbitrary `Tx` generator that varies tx_type / addresses / payload / signature / chain_id: `devnet_tx_hash_matches_canonical` requires the two hash functions return byte-identical 32 bytes (so a regression shrinks to the simplest failing case); `devnet_tx_hash_ignores_signature` requires the canonical hash to stay stable when only the signature is varied (the gossip invariant a producer relies on so remote validators rebuild the same receipt index). Workspace all-green (1816 passed, 0 failed, 7 ignored); clippy clean. ‚Äî PR [#217](https://github.com/pyde-net/engine/pull/217)
- [x] **node: live JSON-RPC integration test for devnet send + receipt path** ‚Äî A23 hardening companion to #217. - [x] **node: devnet UX hardening ‚Äî bind failures + admission + commit logs** ‚Äî three pain points from the A24 saga, now surfaced in stdout where operators actually see them. (1) RPC bind failures broadcast via `eprintln!` to stderr in addition to `tracing::error!` ‚Äî the previous tracing-only path let `Address already in use` silently mask a stale process for hours; the eprintln gives the operator a clear prompt with an `lsof -nP -iTCP:<port>` hint. (2) Each successful `pyde_sendRawTransaction` admission logs `devnet: tx admitted tx_hash=‚Ä¶ kind=‚Ä¶ mempool_depth=N` at info ‚Äî combined with the existing `producer: drained txs into pending batch` line (#219), drain + apply progression is visible without curling. (3) Wave-committer emits a one-line `devnet: wave committed with txs wave_id=N anchor_round=R tx_count=M gas_used=G` per non-empty commit; idle ticks stay silent so an idle chain doesn't drown stdout at the 1Hz default tick rate. **Manual smoke-verified** against the release binary: squatter on port 9933 produces the eprintln on stderr; submitted Deploy tx logs `tx admitted` immediately and `wave committed with txs` ~3s later with matching canonical hash + counts. - [x] **wasm-exec + types: typed-storage substrate ‚Äî 12 host fns √ó scalar/map1/map2/map3 keyed by `state_schema`** ‚Äî closes the "raw `sstore(slot, value)` only" footgun that survived strict-ABI by introducing a chain-side schema-driven slot derivation, paired with per-field type checks at write + read time. **`ContractAbi` extension** (`crates/types/src/abi.rs`): `state_schema: Vec<StateFieldAbi>` added at `V1_1 = 0x0001_0001`, each `StateFieldAbi { name: String, ty: StorageType, key_arity: u8 }` carrying a closed-vocabulary `StorageType` enum (`U8..U128`, `I8..I128`, `Bool`, `Address`, `Hash32`, `Bytes`, `String`, `Vec(Box<StorageType>)`) plus arity 0/1/2/3 for scalar / `Map<K, V>` / `Map<K1, Map<K2, V>>` / `Map<K1, Map<K2, Map<K3, V>>>`. Variable-arity `Vec<_>` storage fields rejected at deploy via `DeployError::VariableLengthVecInStateField { field }` ‚Äî variable Vecs only legal as function args or return values, never as a settled storage value (would silently grow gas per slot). 12 new host fns under `pyde::` registered by `host_fns/state.rs`: `sstore`, `sstore_map1`, `sstore_map2`, `sstore_map3`; `sload`, `sload_map1`, `sload_map2`, `sload_map3`; `sdelete`, `sdelete_map1`, `sdelete_map2`, `sdelete_map3`. Slot derivation is host-side: scalar key = `Blake3(self_address ‚Äñ field_name)`; map1 key = `Blake3(self_address ‚Äñ field_name ‚Äñ k1)`; etc. ‚Äî contract never sees raw slot bytes for typed paths. `HostContext.schema: Arc<HashMap<String, StateFieldAbi>>` plumbed via `WasmExecutor::execute_call_with_schema` from the cache's loaded `ContractAbi`; on field-name mismatch, arity mismatch, or value-byte-length mismatch with declared `StorageType` width the host fn returns `ERR_BAD_STATE_FIELD` / `ERR_BAD_STATE_KEY_ARITY` / `ERR_BAD_STATE_VALUE_WIDTH` (negative `i32`, per HOST_FN_ABI ¬ß4) rather than trapping ‚Äî contract-side macros translate to revert; hand-rolled callers can branch. Pre-existing untyped `pyde::raw::sstore` / `sload` / `sdelete` kept under the explicit `raw` namespace for authors who want bypass; the strict gate is per-call, not per-contract. **`pyde::transfer` payouts from a contract's own balance** kept on the existing untyped extern; not gated on `schema` since transfers never touch the JMT under field names. **Tests**: 18 new ‚Äî schema decode round-trip, declared-but-unused-key-arity reject, value-width mismatch reject across U/I-widths, Address vs Hash32 disambiguation (both 32 bytes; rejection by declared `StorageType` not byte width), `Vec<U64>` permitted, `Vec<Vec<U8>>` rejected at deploy. Workspace all-green, clippy clean. ‚Äî PRs [#228](https://github.com/pyde-net/engine/pull/228), [#229](https://github.com/pyde-net/engine/pull/229), [#230](https://github.com/pyde-net/engine/pull/230), [#231](https://github.com/pyde-net/engine/pull/231)
- [x] **wasm-exec: reentrancy lock applied to top-level entry frames + cleared on outer-frame exit** ‚Äî closes the symmetry gap A5 (PR #184) left at the top of the call stack. The cross-call paths (`cross_call` / `cross_call_static` / `delegate_call`) all enforced the `#[reentrant]` opt-in via `HostContext.call_stack`-driven precheck per HOST_FN_ABI ¬ß3.5.2, but the TOP-LEVEL `execute_contract_call` entry never pushed its own `(self_address, entry_name)` frame ‚Äî so a contract that ENTERED via `tx.data` and then cross-called BACK into itself reached the precheck with an empty stack + the re-entry was permitted even when the outer entry was NOT `#[reentrant]`. The lock is now applied symmetrically: top-level dispatch pushes `(self_address, entry_name)` onto the stack BEFORE the function body executes, the cross-call precheck reads it via the same `is_on_stack` check, the frame is popped on outer-frame exit (success + revert + trap paths all release it via a guard struct using `Drop`). `delegate_call` reentrancy key remains `(caller.self_address, entry_name)` ‚Äî delegated code runs in the caller's frame, so the lock targets the caller's slot, not the target contract's. **Tests**: 3 new e2e ‚Äî `top_level_reentry_through_cross_call_blocks_when_non_reentrant` (self-call cross-call from outer entry returns `ERR_REENTRANCY_BLOCKED = -9`); `top_level_reentry_through_cross_call_succeeds_when_outer_is_reentrant` (same shape, outer attribute flipped on); `outer_revert_releases_lock_for_next_tx` (consecutive standalone txs to the same `(self_address, fn)` are independent ‚Äî the second tx sees an empty stack). 4 pre-existing cross-call e2e tests in `executor.rs` exercised the lock on inner frames and still pass unchanged. ‚Äî PR [#227](https://github.com/pyde-net/engine/pull/227)
- [x] **wasm-exec + node: receipt events surfaced from `HostContext.events` ‚Üí `CallOutcome.events` ‚Üí `Receipt.events`** ‚Äî the `pyde::emit_event` host fn was writing into `HostContext.events: Vec<EventRecord>` cleanly since A5, the dispatch flow was returning them up to `WasmExecutor::execute_call` as `CallOutcome.events`, and the wave-committer was even building a `Vec<EventRecord>` per receipt ‚Äî but `executor_impl::handle_standard_contract_call` + `handle_deploy` were both throwing them away with `events: Vec::new()` before the receipt assembled. Same for `receipt_to_json` which had no `events` field in its serialised form, so even if the receipt CARRIED them they wouldn't have shown up in `pyde_getTransactionReceipt`. This PR closes both halves: `handle_standard_contract_call` + `handle_deploy` map `outcome.events` straight through to the receipt; `receipt_to_json` now emits `events: [{address, topics, data, log_index}, ...]` where `topics: Vec<Hash32>` are hex-encoded + `data: String` is `"0x..."` for the per-topic 32-byte words + arbitrary trailing data bytes. **Smoke** against the release binary: deploy `erc20-token` + `transfer(alice, 1000)` returns a receipt whose `events: [{topics: [Blake3("Transfer(address,address,u128)"), alice_addr_padded, bob_addr_padded], data: "0x...1000-as-le"}]` exactly ‚Äî usable by any indexer or wallet poll loop without re-decoding the WASM-side internal `EventRecord` struct. ‚Äî PR [#232](https://github.com/pyde-net/engine/pull/232)
- [x] **types: `TypeAbi` + ABI version bump to `V1_2 = 0x0001_0002` for custom-types in calldata + returns + state fields** ‚Äî closes the "structs and enums round-trip through the ABI but the schema can't describe them" gap. New `TypeAbi { name: String, kind: TypeKind }` + `TypeKind { Struct { fields: Vec<TypeField> }, Enum { variants: Vec<EnumVariant> } }` + `TypeField { name, ty: StorageType }` + `EnumVariant { name: String }` (deliberately **unit-only** for cross-language portability ‚Äî Borsh-shaped tuple + struct variants are powerful but every non-Rust SDK author then has to map them into their own type system, which kills the "any-language WASM target" thesis). `ContractAbi.types: Vec<TypeAbi>` populated by `otigen-toml::parse_types_section` from `[types.MyStruct]` / `[types.MyEnum]` declarations in `otigen.toml`. Parser allows reference to user-defined type names anywhere a `StorageType` is legal (function args, return type, state fields, nested in `Map<_, MyStruct>` or `Vec<MyStruct>`). Deploy-time validation extended: `validate_deploy` walks all referenced type names through `ContractAbi.types` + rejects undeclared references via `DeployError::UndefinedType { name, referenced_in }`; cyclic struct definitions rejected via `DeployError::CyclicStructDefinition`; duplicate variants in an enum rejected as `DeployError::DuplicateEnumVariant`. `MAX_SUPPORTED_ABI_VERSION` advances `V1_1 ‚Üí V1_2`. **Tests**: 12 new ‚Äî happy-path round-trip, nested struct in map value, cyclic A‚ÜíB‚ÜíA rejection, undefined type rejection, duplicate variant rejection, version-bound pin updated. Workspace all-green. ‚Äî PR [#233](https://github.com/pyde-net/engine/pull/233)
- [x] **wasm-exec: per-frame `caller_address` ‚Äî `pyde::caller` returns the immediate caller, not `tx.from`** ‚Äî closes the EVM-style `msg.sender` semantics gap A5 left open. The `pyde::caller` host fn was returning `HostContext.tx.from` unconditionally ‚Äî fine at the top-level frame, but every cross-call sub-frame ALSO saw `tx.from`, breaking the canonical authorization pattern `require(caller == self_address)` whenever a contract called another contract. Specifically: an NFT marketplace cross-calling `nft.transfer_from(seller, buyer, id)` expected `nft.caller()` to be the marketplace contract; the contract instead saw the original `tx.from` (the bidder) + the transfer reverted with `NotApproved` because the bidder didn't have approval ‚Äî the marketplace did. **Fix**: `HostContext.caller_address: Address` field added, defaulting to `tx.from` for top-level frames via the `with_caller` builder; cross-call sub-frames are constructed with `sub_ctx.caller_address = parent.self_address`; `delegate_call` preserves the PARENT'S `caller_address` (delegated code runs as the caller ‚Äî EVM `msg.sender` semantics: when proxy delegate-calls into logic, `msg.sender` inside the logic is the entity that called the proxy, NOT the proxy itself). The `caller` host fn now writes `caller.data().caller_address` to the contract's output buffer. **Tests**: 3 new e2e ‚Äî `caller_at_top_level_is_tx_from`; `caller_in_cross_call_sub_frame_is_parent_self_address`; `caller_in_delegate_call_sub_frame_preserves_parent_caller_not_proxy_address`. End-to-end verified against the nft-marketplace acceptance contract: bidder calls `marketplace.fill(id)` ‚Üí marketplace cross-calls `nft.transfer_from(seller, bidder, id)` ‚Üí `nft.transfer_from` sees `caller = marketplace_address` + passes the approval check (marketplace was pre-approved by the seller via `setApprovalForAll`) ‚Üí NFT transfers. Pre-fix the same flow reverted with `NotApproved`. ‚Äî PR [#234](https://github.com/pyde-net/engine/pull/234)
- [x] **node: `pyde_call` accepts `borsh(CallPayload)` ‚Äî unify view + standard dispatch** ‚Äî closes the two-wire-formats-for-one-thing wart that the strict-ABI smoke (engine#225) exposed. The chain had two contract-dispatch routes carrying different wire shapes: `TxType::Standard` routed via `WasmExecutorAdapter::handle_standard_contract_call` (engine#223) which decoded `tx.data` as `borsh(CallPayload { function: String, calldata: Vec<u8> })` and dispatched by function name via `WasmExecutor::execute_call(&hash, &name, ctx)`; `pyde_call` RPC routed via the legacy `execute_contract_call` path which interpreted `data` as `[selector(4), args...]` and dispatched by the 4-byte selector via `resolve_dispatch`. Same contract, two wire formats depending on whether the caller was mutating or viewing ‚Äî and the engine's design memo (`address-naming-collision`) had already locked in name-based dispatch as canonical specifically to spare contract authors from selector-table boilerplate. The selector path was a Solidity-shape leftover the view RPC never migrated out of. This PR aligns the view path with the standard one. `pyde_call`'s `data` is now the same `borsh(CallPayload)` envelope `tx.data` carries; the handler decodes the envelope, looks up `payload.function` by name in the contract's ABI via `cache.get_with_abi`, runs the same attribute pre-checks the standard path applies (constructor lockout, payable-vs-value), then dispatches via `WasmExecutor::execute_call(&cache_key, &function_name, host_ctx)`. The `HostContext.input` is `payload.calldata` (NOT the raw `data` field ‚Äî the borsh envelope is unwrapped before the contract sees it, same as the standard path). View-mode is still set unconditionally on the host context so mutating host fns (`sstore`, `sdelete`, `transfer`, `emit_event`) trap with `ERR_FORBIDDEN` regardless of whether the called function is `view`-attributed ‚Äî a non-view fn invoked via `pyde_call` is honest dry-run simulation: the contract sees `view_mode=true` and any state mutation traps. Empty `data` is rejected upfront as `InvalidParams` with the explicit "missing `data` ‚Äî must be borsh-encoded CallPayload" message (was: silently fell through to fallback dispatch with a less informative downstream error). **Tests**: 4 unit tests rewritten / added in `devnet::rpc::tests` ‚Äî `pyde_call_empty_data_rejects_with_invalid_params` (envelope-missing path); `pyde_call_unknown_address_returns_invalid_params` (the address-resolution check still fires before the executor sees the call; the test now passes a real `borsh(CallPayload)` envelope so the new wire shape is exercised on the rejection path too); `pyde_call_against_deployed_contract_returns_empty_data` (canonical happy path against `build_contract_wasm("foo")` with a real `borsh(CallPayload { function: "foo", calldata: [] })` envelope ‚Äî empty `return_data` is right since the test fixture is void-void and doesn't call `pyde::return`); `pyde_call_unknown_function_name_rejects_with_invalid_params` (locks the "function 'X' not found in ABI" error message so otigen / wallets can surface it to authors ‚Äî mirrors the equivalent revert path in `handle_standard_contract_call`). **End-to-end smoke** against the release binary: boot `pyde devnet`, deploy `counter-rust`, `otigen call counter-rust increment` (sets the counter to 1 via a state-mutating Standard tx ‚Äî nonce 0 ‚Üí 2 since deploy + call), then `pyde_call` with `data = borsh(CallPayload { function: "get", calldata: [] })` returns `result = "0x0000000000000001"` ‚Äî the BE-u64-encoded counter value the contract surfaced through `pyde::return`. Sender nonce stays at `0x2` ‚Äî the view call did NOT bump it, did NOT cost gas, did NOT persist a receipt. This is the wire shape the otigen-side fix (otigen#196) will consume to route view-attributed function calls via `pyde_call` instead of submitting them as `pyde_sendRawTransaction` ‚Äî which today turns every view read into a full tx with gas charge + nonce bump + ledger receipt, breaking UX for any real DApp's read-heavy paths. Workspace all-green (1837 passed, 0 failed); clippy clean. ‚Äî PR [#226](https://github.com/pyde-net/engine/pull/226)
- [x] **wasm-exec: enforce `() -> ()` entry-point signature** ‚Äî locks the HOST_FN_ABI ¬ß3.5.2 contract that Pyde entry points are uniformly void-void at the WASM-function-boundary level: args flow through the `pyde.calldata_size` / `pyde.calldata_copy` host fns, return data flows through `pyde.return_with_data`. Before this PR a natural Rust contract that wrote `extern "C" fn increment() -> i64` (the shape `otigen new` was emitting in `examples/counter-rust`) would deploy fine, get dispatched fine, then trap at the first call with wasmtime's `expected 1 results, got 0` ‚Äî surfaced to the caller as a shape-less `Reverted` receipt with no actionable reason. The same hole applied symmetrically to `extern "C" fn foo(amount: i32)` style params: WASM-level args bypass the calldata convention and the chain has no honest default value to pass. **Fix** is two layers + a UX glue change. **Deploy-time gate** in `validate_deploy`: a new `extract_exported_func_signatures` walks the WASM type + import + function + export sections, resolves the function index space correctly (imports live at `[0..import_func_count)`, locally-defined functions at `[import_func_count..)`, each function carrying a type-index into the type section), and produces a map `export_name ‚Üí (param_count, result_count)`. The new `check_entry_point_signatures` step in the validation pipeline then walks every ABI-declared function and rejects any whose WASM type isn't `() -> ()` with `DeployError::InvalidEntryPointSignature { fn_name, params, results }`. **Call-time defense-in-depth** in `WasmExecutor::execute_call`: same gate applied right after `instance.get_func` resolves the entry ‚Äî rejects with `ExecutorError::Runtime` carrying a message that points the contract author at `pyde.calldata_*` for args and `pyde.return_with_data` for return data. The call-time layer catches anything that slipped past deploy (older deploys, raw-bytes-upload bypass that skips `validate_deploy`). **UX glue alongside the strict gate**: the deploy + standard-call revert helpers (the two `let reverted = |reason: &str| -> Receipt { ... }` closures) now put the rejection reason into `receipt.return_data` as UTF-8 bytes ‚Äî previously empty bytes, which surfaced to the caller as a shape-less `TxReverted: reverted` with no debuggable signal. The accompanying tracing log is bumped from `debug` to `info` so devnet operators see rejections without enabling debug. **Tests**: 7 new ‚Äî 5 in `deploy::tests` (`validate_deploy_accepts_void_void_entry_point`, `validate_deploy_rejects_entry_with_wasm_level_result`, `validate_deploy_rejects_entry_with_wasm_level_param`, `validate_deploy_rejects_entry_with_both_param_and_result`, `validate_deploy_signature_check_resolves_function_index_space_correctly` ‚Äî the last one specifically locks the index-space walker against off-by-import bugs by planting one `pyde.sload` import + a void-void entry at func_idx=1 and asserting it validates cleanly); 2 in `executor::tests` (`execute_call_rejects_entry_with_wasm_level_result`, `execute_call_rejects_entry_with_wasm_level_param`). A new `build_wasm_with_wat` helper lets signature-validation tests declare non-void shapes (the cookie-cutter `build_wasm_with_abi` only emits void-void). **Breaking for contract authors**: any contract with WASM-level params or results now fails deploy. otigen's `counter-rust` example as currently shipped (the `extern "C" fn increment() -> i64` + `extern "C" fn get() -> i64` shape) will fail deploy with a clean error: `validate_deploy: entry point 'get' has WASM signature (0 params, 1 results); Pyde entry points must be \`() -> ()\`. Args via \`pyde.calldata_*\` host fns, return data via \`pyde.return_with_data\`.` The otigen-side update to `counter-rust` (drop `-> i64`, use `return_with_data` for outputs), the `#[pyde::entry]` Rust proc macro (inline-template via `otigen new` so the calldata-decode + return-wrap boilerplate stays hidden), the `otigen call` / `otigen deploy` change to decode `receipt.return_data` as UTF-8 on revert, and the pyde-book documentation of the `() -> ()` ABI contract + community contribution pathway for non-Rust language macros all ship separately. **End-to-end smoke** against the release binary: `pyde devnet` + `otigen deploy --bundle counter-rust.bundle` now reverts cleanly with `receipt.return_data` carrying the readable rejection reason ‚Äî clear, actionable, fixable from the author side. Workspace all-green (1835 passed, 0 failed); clippy clean. ‚Äî PR [#225](https://github.com/pyde-net/engine/pull/225)
- [x] **consensus + node: solo validator combines beacon for next epoch** ‚Äî closes the silent-stall a solo `pyde devnet` start hit at the end of every epoch (wave 99 ‚Üí wave 100, default `epoch_length = 100`). Two layers conspired to make the next-epoch beacon unreachable. (1) The wave-committer's `maybe_emit_share_for_next_epoch` published the validator's own share to the gossip mesh but never inserted it into the local `BeaconShareBuffer`. The receive-side path (`mainloop::handle_beacon_share`) only fires on shares that arrive from peers ‚Äî a multi-validator committee survives this because peers echo, but a solo `pyde devnet` has zero peers and the buffer's `count(next_epoch)` stayed at 0 forever. (2) Even with the local share buffered, both `MockBeaconScheme::combine` and `FalconBeaconScheme::combine` hard-coded the spec `BEACON_THRESHOLD = 85`, returning `BeaconError::InsufficientShares` for any count below 85. The `WaveCommitterConfig::beacon_combine_threshold` field was honoured at the outer count-gate that decided WHEN to invoke `combine`, but the scheme itself had no knob ‚Äî so a committer configured for threshold=1 still bottomed out at 85 inside `combine`. The committer ticked happily through wave 0 ‚Üí 99 (epoch 0), then trace-logged `wave committer: beacon not derived for epoch yet, waiting epoch=1 round=100` forever. **Fixes**: `BeaconScheme::combine` is now per-instance threshold-driven ‚Äî `MockBeaconScheme::with_threshold(usize)` and `FalconBeaconScheme::with_threshold(local_member_id, secret, committee, usize)` let the construction site set it explicitly; the existing `::new()` constructors keep `BEACON_THRESHOLD = 85` so multi-validator + spec-shaped tests stay unchanged. `maybe_emit_share_for_next_epoch` now inserts the locally-generated share into the local `beacon_buffer` alongside the network publish (`BeaconShareBuffer::insert` dedups by `(epoch, member_id)`, so a peer-echoed duplicate is a no-op + bumps `beacon_share_duplicates` metric). The validator boot path computes `beacon_combine_threshold = min(committee_size, QUORUM)` + `beacon_combine_target_count = min(committee_size, COMMITTEE_SIZE)` and threads them through both `WaveCommitterConfig` AND `FalconBeaconScheme::with_threshold` ‚Äî solo `pyde devnet` runs at threshold=1 (one share = one beacon), small dev clusters at `threshold = committee_size`, production-shape clusters at the spec 85. `WaveCommitter::for_test` now constructs the mock scheme with the same threshold the outer config gates on so unit tests exercising the solo path don't trip a misleading `InsufficientShares` from the inner scheme. **Tests**: `share_emit_buffers_local_share_so_solo_validator_can_combine` locks the local-insert invariant in isolation (uses `beacon_combine_threshold = 2` + 1-hour wait window so the local share lands + sticks, prevents the immediate-combine-then-prune that would erase the buffer state the test wants to assert on); `solo_validator_combines_beacon_for_next_epoch_from_own_share_alone` drives the full vertical ‚Äî `beacon_combine_threshold = 1`, `target_count = 1`, one commit ‚Üí share emitted + buffered + combined + stored under epoch N+1 ‚Äî without the fix the `beacon_store.get(1)` assertion fails because combine never fires; `combine_fires_when_buffer_reaches_quorum_and_stores_beacon` rewritten to match its name (the pre-PR body asserted the negative ‚Äî `beacons_combined == 0` ‚Äî with an explanatory comment about the hardcoded 85 making the test name's positive claim impossible to verify; post-PR with `beacon_combine_threshold = 3` + 3 buffered shares + scheme threshold=3 it actually does what the name says). **End-to-end smoke** against the release binary: `pyde devnet` + `otigen deploy --bundle counter-rust.bundle --from devnet-0` printed `‚úì Deployed.` with a receipt status of `"success"` ‚Äî otigen polled the receipt over real HTTP, got a non-null body with status field success, and exited 0. Pre-fix the same flow hit `InclusionTimeout` after the chain ticked past wave_id = 99 and the committer stalled. The `otigen call` step still reverts with `expected 1 results, got 0` on the release binary ‚Äî that's the separate `() -> ()` ABI strictness follow-up (engine + otigen + macro coordination), not part of this PR. Workspace all-green (1828 passed, 0 failed); clippy clean. ‚Äî PR [#224](https://github.com/pyde-net/engine/pull/224)
- [x] **node + wasm-exec: standard contract-call dispatch via `WasmExecutorAdapter`** ‚Äî closes the gap where `TxType::Standard` txs targeting a deployed contract were drained from the mempool into a pending wave batch but never actually executed. otigen's `call` command admitted the tx successfully (admission log + canonical hash returned), the producer's `drained=1` log fired, and then nothing ‚Äî no `devnet: tx applied` line, no receipt, sender nonce stuck at 1 after the prior deploy bumped it. The legacy `DevnetState::apply_contract_call` was a parallel implementation that read `tx.data` as a 4-byte selector + dispatched through `WasmExecutor::execute_contract_call`, while the production `WasmExecutorAdapter::handle_standard_contract_call` (#205) already implemented the canonical `CallPayload { function, calldata }` borsh decode + name-based ABI lookup. The chain saw the borsh `function.len()` u32 LE prefix as a non-matching selector, silently dropped the tx, and otigen `call` hit `InclusionTimeout`. **Fix** mirrors the A25 deploy-side shape: `WasmExecutorAdapter::handle_standard_contract_call` is now `pub`; `DevnetState::apply_contract_call` delegates to it by constructing a per-wave adapter (cheap ‚Äî `WasmExecutor` is `Clone` and Arc-shares its `Engine` + module cache). The devnet's local copy preserves the chain's replay-protection invariant: on a Reverted receipt from the adapter's pre-execution checks (decode failure, unknown function name, bad signature, nonce out of window, insufficient balance), the sender's nonce is committed + gas charged up to balance on the DevnetState side; on Success the contract address is added to `touched_addresses` so the wave's `state_root` recompute includes the storage writes. **`pyde_getStorageSlot` RPC** is now exposed in the devnet RPC catalog so wallets + the `otigen inspect` flow can read a contract's storage slot directly from chain state via `StateStore::read_slot` ‚Äî the only path through which a step-6 acceptance can verify a call actually changed state. Slot key is the full 32-byte slot the contract supplies at sstore time per HOST_FN_ABI ¬ß7.6; callers that want a `(contract, index)` shape derive the key themselves. **Tests**: `call_payload_borsh_roundtrip` + `call_payload_bytes_are_not_raw_wasm` proptests across an arbitrary `CallPayload` generator (symmetric to the DeployData proptests ‚Äî the second locks the same wire-confusion footgun); `devnet_deploy_then_call_lands_storage_slot_via_live_json_rpc` ‚Äî boots devnet with `--rpc-listen 127.0.0.1:0`, deploys a counter contract whose `increment` function writes `0x01` to slot `[0x42; 32]` via `pyde.sstore`, calls it as a `TxType::Standard` tx over real HTTP, polls the call receipt, then asserts the full vertical: deploy receipt status=success + `return_data == contract_name_address(name)`, call receipt status=success, `pyde_getTransactionCount(sender) == 0x2` (nonce 0 ‚Üí 2 across deploy + call), and `pyde_getStorageSlot([0x42;32])` returns a non-null hex string with at least one non-zero byte. `devnet_deploy_then_unknown_function_call_reverts_via_live_json_rpc` ‚Äî same shape but calls a function name not in the ABI; asserts receipt status=reverted, nonce still advances 0 ‚Üí 2, and `pyde_getBalance(sender)` is strictly less than the prefund amount (replay-protection invariant + no-refund gas charge intact). - [x] **node + wasm-exec: A25 ‚Äî `apply_deploy` delegates to `handle_deploy`** ‚Äî closes engine ask A25. Before this PR the devnet had two Deploy implementations that diverged: the chain's `commit_walked_subdag` dispatched through `DevnetState::apply_deploy` (which read `tx.data` as raw wasm and used CREATE-style `(sender, nonce)` addressing) while the production `WasmExecutorAdapter::handle_deploy` (#203/#204) already implemented the spec-correct flow ‚Äî borsh-decode `DeployData`, derive `Poseidon2("pyde-contract:" || name)`, validate the wasm bundle, run the constructor with `init_calldata`, register the name in the on-chain registry. All four A25 sub-asks (`DeployData` decode, name-based address, `init_calldata` to constructor, duplicate-name rejection) come along simultaneously. The Reverted branch on the DevnetState side preserves the chain's replay-protection invariant by charging gas + committing the nonce on the sender even when the adapter's pre-execution revert (decode / invalid name / duplicate / wasm validation failure) doesn't write state; the Success branch tracks the new contract address in `touched_addresses` so the wave's `state_root` recompute includes it. **Tests**: `deploy_data_borsh_roundtrip` + `deploy_data_bytes_are_not_raw_wasm` proptests across an arbitrary `DeployData` generator ‚Äî the second specifically asserts the borsh envelope never starts with WASM magic bytes (the A25 confusion footgun); `deploy_with_contract_support_succeeds_and_returns_address` updated to assert the name-based address; `deploy_with_raw_wasm_in_tx_data_reverts_cleanly` ‚Äî the exact A25-confusion shape (raw wasm in `tx.data`) now produces a Reverted receipt + advanced nonce + gas charge; `deploy_rejects_duplicate_name` ‚Äî second deploy at same name reverts; `devnet_deploy_succeeds_with_real_pyde_abi_bundle_via_live_json_rpc` ‚Äî boots devnet with `--rpc-listen 127.0.0.1:0`, POSTs a `TxType::Deploy` whose `tx.data` is the canonical `borsh(DeployData)` envelope with a wasm bundle that has a `pyde.abi` custom section, polls `pyde_getTransactionReceipt` over real HTTP, and asserts `status: "success"` + `return_data == contract_name_address(name)` ‚Äî the exact wire path the acceptance doc's step 4 drives. `deploy_tx` helpers in both `state.rs` and `rpc.rs` tests updated to ship `borsh(DeployData{name, wasm_bytes, ‚Ä¶})` per A25 ask #5. - [x] **types + tx + wasm-exec: `TxType::Unjail` handler closes the validator-jail loop** ‚Äî completes the validator-lifecycle consolidation slice that started with the `Status::Jailed` variant + `handle_slash` jail-vs-exit branch + the auto-submit slash bridge. Validators slashed into `Status::Jailed` can now return to `Active` after their jail period elapses; without this they were stuck in jail forever. **`TxType::Unjail = 0x0E`**: new variant in `pyde_engine_types::TxType`, wire-pinned by an explicit borsh-discriminant test; envelope shape per spec (`tx.to == ZERO`, `tx.data` empty, `tx.from = validator's address` ‚Äî validator-self-signed like `StakeWithdraw`/`ClaimReward`). Helper `force_jailed()` mirrors what `handle_slash` does for a Safety offense without needing the full slash pipeline. Tx-crate tests: 231 ‚Üí 241.
