- [x] **wasm-exec + tx: `handle_standard` contract-call dispatch** ‚Äî closes the gap where Standard txs targeting contracts (`tx.to` has code) were rejected with `HandlerError::ContractCallDeferred` and never reached the WASM runtime. otigen-test deploy-loop integration test #236 is unblocked end-to-end now. **`CallPayload` wire type**: new `pyde_engine_types::call::CallPayload { function: String, calldata: Vec<u8> }` is the borsh-encoded payload `Tx::data` carries for contract-targeting Standard txs. The chain dispatches by function name (not by 4-byte selector); calldata is the function's args, no selector prefix. **`handle_standard_contract_call`** is the new method on `WasmExecutorAdapter` that owns the contract-call execution ‚Äî pre-routed from the dispatcher when `accounts.code_hash(&tx.to)` returns `Some`, so the tx-crate's `handle_standard` never sees a contract target in the production path. **Flow** (12 steps): decode `CallPayload` ‚Üí load + verify sender (auth + nonce + balance) ‚Üí ensure module cached (`load_from_persistent` for cold-restart from a snapshot) ‚Üí find function in ABI by name ‚Üí attribute checks (`CONSTRUCTOR` lockout, non-`PAYABLE` refuses value) ‚Üí pre-debit sender + commit nonce ‚Üí build `TxOverlay` + credit value to contract via overlay ‚Üí build `HostContext` with `self_address = tx.to`, `input = payload.calldata` ‚Üí `execute_call(&code_hash, &payload.function, ctx)` ‚Üí on clean exit finalise overlay; on trap/revert/OOG drop overlay (no state changes persist) ‚Üí Receipt with the call's `return_data`. **Failure model**: pre-execution rejects charge `MIN_GAS_LIMIT` (the intrinsic floor); post-execution reverts charge `tx.gas_limit` (no refund per PIP-4). The sender's pre-debit at step 6 stays forfeit on any post-execution revert. **`handle_standard` cleanup**: removes the `ContractCallDeferred` short-circuit (the dispatcher's pre-route handles contract targets upstream); the tx-crate handler now sees only the value-transfer path. Removes the `HandlerError::ContractCallDeferred` variant entirely; the old `contract_call_path_returns_deferred` test becomes `contract_target_treated_as_plain_value_transfer` (direct callers of the handler get pure value-transfer semantics when they bypass the dispatcher). **Tests**: `standard_call_into_no_op_function_succeeds` (deploy + call happy path); `standard_call_to_unknown_function_reverts` (function not in ABI); `standard_call_to_constructor_at_runtime_reverts` (`CONSTRUCTOR` lockout); `standard_call_with_value_to_non_payable_function_reverts` (`PAYABLE` attribute enforcement); `standard_call_contract_revert_charges_full_gas_and_keeps_pre_debit` (`(unreachable)` trap; full gas_limit charged; pre-debit stays); `contract_target_treated_as_plain_value_transfer` (direct callers of tx-crate handle_standard). - [x] **wasm-exec: wire constructor execution into `handle_deploy`** ‚Äî completes the deploy slice. `handle_deploy` now invokes the contract's constructor function via `WasmExecutor::execute_call` when the ABI declares one, with full rollback semantics on revert / trap / OOG. **Flow change**: step 8 is now a pre-debit + overlay-stage (writes the contract account into a `TxOverlay` rather than directly to `AccountStore`). Step 9 invokes `execute_call(&code_hash, constructor_name, ctx)` if `abi.constructor_index` is `Some`; on constructor failure the overlay is dropped (contract account vanishes, sstore writes vanish, `tx.value` is forfeited per PIP-4's no-refund policy) and the receipt carries the full `gas_limit` as `gas_used` (constructor ran). The handler still returns a `Reverted` Receipt with floor gas charged for any pre-execution failure (decode, name validation, wasm validation, balance check, sender not found). Contracts with no constructor (`abi.constructor_index == None`) skip the constructor call entirely; `init_calldata` in the envelope is silently ignored in that case (the wasm couldn't observe what it didn't import). **HostContext for the constructor**: built with `self_address = derived contract address`, `tx.input = deploy.init_calldata`, `tx.value = tx.value`; the overlay handle is threaded in for storage host fns, and the executor handle for `cross_call`; `wave_timestamp = 0` (orchestrator patches in prod). `execute_call` is the right entry point ‚Äî `execute_contract_call` explicitly rejects `CONSTRUCTOR`-attributed functions with `ERR_CONSTRUCTOR_LOCKOUT` (callable only at deploy time). **Tests**: `deploy_runs_no_op_constructor_to_success` (empty-body constructor runs cleanly + commits the contract + registers the name); `deploy_constructor_revert_rolls_back_contract_account_and_name` (constructor uses `(unreachable)`; receipt is `Reverted` with full `gas_limit` charged; the contract account never persists + the name registry stays empty); `deploy_no_constructor_path_still_succeeds` (regression gate on the existing test against the constructor-execution change); all existing deploy tests pass unchanged. - [x] **account + wasm-exec: name-based contract addresses + `DeployData`-driven `handle_deploy`** ‚Äî closes the spec drift in the deploy flow where the existing `handle_deploy` decoded `tx.data` as raw WASM bytes and derived the contract address via CREATE-style `Poseidon2(deployer || nonce)`. - [x] **node: `SlashSubmitter` bridges equivocation detection to on-chain slash (validator lifecycle PR-3)** ‚Äî third PR in the consolidation slice. **Closes the "safety detectors are paper tigers" gap.** Until now the slashing-detector consumers (`EquivocationConsumer`, `BadStateRootSigConsumer`, etc.) called `Slasher::record()` which only updated the in-memory offense log + jail map. The on-chain `ValidatorRecord.stake` reduction happens only via `TxType::Slash` ‚Äî and nothing was submitting one automatically. So safety detectors were detection-only: equivocations were observed and logged locally, but no validator ever lost stake on-chain. **`SlashSubmitter`** closes that gap for `EquivocationConsumer`. After each successful in-memory record, the consumer looks up the offender's FALCON pubkey via the injected `CommitteeLookup` (v1: `StaticCommitteeLookup` ‚Äî position-indexed `Vec<Option<FalconPubkey>>` built from genesis-committee config), pulls the prior equivocating vertex from `VertexStore` by hash, builds a `SafetyEvidence` with both vertices' pre-image bytes + FALCON sigs, signs a `TxType::Slash` with the local validator's `FalconKeypair` (setting itself as `reporter` ‚Äî collects 20% reporter share per `Offense::Equivocation.spec().distribution.reporter_bps`), and inserts into the local mempool via `PydeMempoolView::insert`. The chain-side `handle_slash` (PR-2) then reduces stake + transitions the offender to `Status::Jailed`. **Wiring + opt-in**: `with_slash_submitter(submitter)` is an opt-in builder so older consumer tests that don't spin up a mempool keep working in detection-only mode; two new `MainLoopMetrics` counters (`equivocation_consumer_slash_tx_submitted` / `_failed`). **Newly public**: `consensus::vertex_sig_pre_image` (was `pub(crate) pre_hash_bytes`) ‚Äî exposes the canonical FALCON pre-image bytes so the submitter routes both ends of the evidence through one encoding source; the chain-side `handle_slash` hashes the same bytes via `verify_hash_signature`. **Out of scope (PR-3b/c follow-ups)**: same shape for `BadStateRootSig` / `BadAnchorAttestation` / `InvalidVertexStructure` (PR-3b); Liveness consumers like `ExtendedDowntime` need a distinct `LivenessEvidence` variant since the auto-detected liveness pipeline has no per-event FALCON sig pair (PR-3c); validator runtime wiring that passes the submitter into the consumer at startup needs the genesis-committee ‚Üí lookup build path (deferred to a runtime-side PR that doesn't touch consumer logic). **Tests**: 6 new on `slash_submitter` ‚Äî 3 on `StaticCommitteeLookup` resolution paths; `build_equivocation_slash_tx_produces_chain_verifiable_evidence` (end-to-end build with real FALCON-signed vertices, asserts the produced evidence verifies under real `falcon_verify` ‚Äî the chain-side invariant); `build_equivocation_slash_tx_rejects_unknown_offender` (defensive guard on missing committee mapping); `build_equivocation_slash_tx_surfaces_missing_prior_vertex` (defensive guard on pruned `VertexStore`). Existing `EquivocationConsumer` tests migrated from `#[test]` to `#[tokio::test]` (dispatch is now async). Node-crate lib tests: 377 ‚Üí 383. Workspace all-green; clippy clean. ‚Äî PR [#199](https://github.com/pyde-net/engine/pull/199)
- [x] **tx: `handle_slash` reads `Offense` from evidence + branches jail vs exit (validator lifecycle PR-2)** ‚Äî second PR in the consolidation slice. `handle_slash` previously hardcoded a 10% slash + `Status::Exited` transition for every Safety offense, ignoring the per-offense penalties in the slashing crate's catalog. This PR wires the catalog through end-to-end. **Changes**: `SafetyEvidence` gains an `offense: Offense` field; new `HandlerError::SlashOffenseClassMismatch` rejects Liveness offenses via the Safety shape (Liveness evidence ships in PR-3 alongside the auto-submit pipeline); slash amount now reads `record.stake √ó spec.first_instance_bps / 10_000` (Equivocation/BadStateRootSig stay at 10%; BadAnchorAttestation/InvalidVertexStructure/BadDecryptionShare move to their catalog 5%); distribution reads from `spec.distribution` ‚Äî `SAFETY_DEFAULT` (50% burn / 30% treasury / 20% reporter) now credits both reporter AND treasury via `treasury_address()`, while `ALL_BURN` (InvalidVertexStructure) trivially zeros both shares; status transition branches on `spec.jail_epochs` ‚Äî `> 0` ‚Üí `Status::Jailed` with `jail_until_wave = wave + jail_epochs √ó EPOCH_LENGTH_WAVES`, `== 0` leaves status unchanged (warning-only path, currently unreachable from SafetyEvidence but kept for future Safety additions); `TOTAL_ACTIVE_STAKE_WEIGHTED` decrements only on `Active ‚Üí Jailed` since Unbonding already decremented at StakeWithdraw time (re-decrementing would cause saturating-sub underflow); `REPORTER_REWARD_BPS` bumped 1000 ‚Üí 2000 to match `SAFETY_DEFAULT`. **Spec evolution**: SLASHING.md treats Safety as 1-epoch jail with fractional slash, not the original "100% + permanent ban" baseline ‚Äî the latter is v2 hardening (correlation multiplier + repeat-offense scaling). **Tests**: 229 ‚Üí 231 (+2 net). - [x] **tx: add `Status::Jailed` variant + `jail_until_wave` field to `ValidatorRecord` (validator lifecycle PR-1)** ‚Äî first PR in the validator-lifecycle consolidation slice. - [x] **node: validator `FalconKeypair` uses real FALCON-512 (A16 part 2)** ‚Äî closes the validator-side half of otigen Phase 1 follow-up A16. #195 migrated the devnet `Wallet` (tx signing) to real FALCON via `consensus::FalconSigner`; this PR migrates the disk-backed `FalconKeypair` (vertex signing) so the validator producer / mainloop / beacon hot paths all run on the same crypto end-to-end. Removes the last `MockSigner`-backed signing surface on the validator binary. **File format v1 ‚Üí v2**: on-disk shape changes from `(version: u8 = 1, secret: 32 bytes mock seed, pubkey: 897 bytes Blake3-extended mock)` to `(version: u8 = 2, secret: 32 bytes FALCON keygen seed, pubkey: 897 bytes real FALCON-512)`. v1 mock keypairs are rejected with `MismatchedVersion` ‚Äî operators with v1 keypairs regenerate (the old keypair never reached production validators, so the upgrade path is "delete the file"). Persisting a 32-byte seed (not the 1281-byte FALCON secret key bytes) keeps the on-disk footprint small + leans on `pyde_crypto::falcon::falcon_keygen_deterministic` to re-derive the keypair on every load; the persisted pubkey is then cross-checked against the freshly-derived one as the integrity gate. **`FalconKeypair::from_seed(seed) -> Result<Self, FalconKeypairError>`**: deterministic constructor mirroring `FalconSigner::from_seed` (#195) ‚Äî same seed ‚Üí same `(pk, sk)` across restarts. New `FalconKeypairError::Keygen(String)` variant surfaces the (effectively unreachable) upstream-keygen failure. The old `from_mock_secret` name is retained as a thin panicking shim that delegates to `from_seed` so existing devnet-runner call sites compile through the migration; it'll be retired in the follow-up renaming pass. **Sig non-determinism**: real FALCON-512 sigs are non-deterministic per the FN-DSA spec (fresh randomness per sign ‚Äî guards against fault-injection attacks). Tests that previously asserted byte-equality of two sigs over the same pre-image (`save_and_load_round_trip_preserves_pubkey_and_signature`, `from_mock_secret_is_deterministic`) now assert under-pubkey verification instead via `pyde_crypto::falcon::falcon_verify` ‚Äî verifier contract is what matters, not byte-identical outputs. The runtime sig-length assertion in `runtime::tests::falcon_keypair_signs_through_signer_trait` widens from a 666-byte exact match to the `[500, 1000]` FALCON wire-format range. Old `signer_impl_matches_mock_signer_with_same_secret` test is replaced with `signer_impl_produces_real_falcon_verifiable_sigs` since the keypair no longer wraps `MockSigner` ‚Äî the verifier contract is what's load-bearing. The `derive_mock_pubkey` Blake3-stretching helper goes away with the migration. **Test counts**: 17 `falcon_keypair::tests` (was 14 ‚Äî added `from_mock_secret_alias_matches_from_seed`, replaced two sig-equality tests with verify-under-pubkey shapes); 377 node-crate lib tests pass total (was 376). Workspace all-green, clippy clean. **Otigen unblocks**: validator binary now uses real FALCON across every signing surface (vertex via `FalconKeypair`, beacon via `BeaconKeypair`, devnet wallet via `Wallet` from #195) ‚Äî `pyde devnet` no longer surfaces any mock-vs-real split internally. Closes the A16 work-stream end-to-end. ‚Äî PR [#196](https://github.com/pyde-net/engine/pull/196)
- [x] **node + consensus: devnet `Wallet` uses real FALCON-512 + Poseidon2 address (A16 part 1)** ‚Äî closes the wallet-side half of otigen Phase 1 follow-up A16. Pyde's principle is "same crypto everywhere across mainnet / testnet / devnet" ‚Äî internal mock-vs-real-FALCON splits must never surface as user-facing choices. Current state violated that: chain verification was already real FALCON (`pyde_engine_tx::verify_tx_signature` ‚Üí `pyde_crypto::falcon_verify`) but the devnet wallet signed with `MockSigner` (Blake3 counter-rehash) and derived addresses as `Blake3(secret)` not `Poseidon2(falcon_pubkey)`. built via `FalconSigner::from_seed(&[u8; 32])` which calls `falcon_keygen_deterministic`; `sign` delegates to `pyde_crypto::falcon::falcon_sign`; falls back to a representative-length zero signature on the impossible upstream failure path so the chain verify rejects deterministically rather than panicking. **`devnet::wallet::Wallet`**: `signer: MockSigner` ‚Üí `signer: FalconSigner`; secret stays full 32 bytes so otigen-wallet's `--from-devnet` import can re-derive the full keypair via the same `falcon_keygen_deterministic` API. **Tests**: 4 new `FalconSigner` unit tests in `consensus::signer` (deterministic pubkey across calls; - [x] **wasm-exec: invoke `_initialize` after `instantiate` per WASI Preview 1 (A14)** ‚Äî closes otigen Phase 1 follow-up A14. Per Pyde's no-SDK multi-language design (the `no_sdk_parachain_approach` memory: "Authors compile their own WASM in any wasm32-target language"), the engine must honour the WASI Preview 1 reactor / command-module contract: any module that exports `_initialize` expects it to run BEFORE any other export is called. The hook sets up the toolchain's runtime state (heap base, globals, schedulers) that later exports depend on. Engine's `execute_call` previously only invoked the named entry-point. Bare rustc `wasm32-unknown-unknown` modules don't export `_initialize` so they worked fine; every other supported toolchain (TinyGo `wasm-unknown`, C/Zig with libc, AssemblyScript) trapped at the first runtime-managed access inside the entry call. **Not an otigen accommodation** ‚Äî this is the WASI Preview 1 standard the wider WASM ecosystem follows; without honouring it Pyde silently restricted the contract-author toolchain matrix to bare-rustc, contradicting the documented "any wasm32 language" support. **Change**: 4 LOC in `WasmExecutor::execute_call` between `linker.instantiate(...)` and `instance.get_func(entry)` ‚Äî `instance.get_func(&mut store, "_initialize")` is called if present, mapped to `ExecutorError::Runtime("_initialize trapped: ‚Ä¶")` on failure. Init fuel charges against the same gas budget as the entry call. Cross-call / `delegate_call` / `cross_call_static` paths route through `execute_call` itself so they inherit the fix without extra changes. **Tests**: 3 new ‚Äî `execute_call_invokes_initialize_when_exported` (module sets a global in `_initialize`; `main` reads it back, traps if zero), `execute_call_skips_initialize_when_absent` (bare module without `_initialize` must not surface "missing export"), `execute_call_surfaces_initialize_trap_as_runtime_error` (`_initialize` `unreachable`s, surfaces as `ExecutorError::Runtime` with "_initialize trapped" in the message). `cargo test -p pyde-engine-wasm-exec --lib` green ‚Äî 242 passed (was 239). Workspace all-green. Clippy clean. Otigen-side: `counter-go` (was 0/3) and `counter-token-go` (was 0/7) under `--engine` flip from failing to passing without contract changes. **Adjacent A15 declined**: parachain host fns in the linker ‚Äî per `v2_roadmap_and_room`, parachains are explicit v2 / post-mainnet; engine has no parachain runtime, no parachain state, no parachain semantics defined; building stubs now would freeze interface decisions before v2 design exists. Otigen's legacy runner has working mocks for parachain host fns so `--engine`-mode parachain testing is the only thing actually blocked, and the legacy fallback unblocks the same workflow. Same shape as the `--fork` detour. ‚Äî PR [#194](https://github.com/pyde-net/engine/pull/194)
- [x] **node: `DowntimeDetector` task + validator wiring (Œ≥.slashing.extended-downtime, PR2/2)** ‚Äî second PR closes the two-PR slice for offense #8. #192 shipped the pure-logic `DowntimeAccumulator` + `ExtendedDowntimeConsumer`; this PR adds the chain-side observer task + spawns the detector/consumer pair at validator startup. **`DowntimeDetector`** is a long-running tokio task that periodically scans the `VertexStore` for completed rounds and feeds the `DowntimeAccumulator`. Architecture differs from the safety detectors (which are event-driven, one per vertex/sig insert): downtime is *absence-driven* ‚Äî we have to look at what's NOT in the DAG, which requires a periodic sweep. **Per-tick flow**: for each round `R in (last_scored, highest - lag]`: (1) `vertices = dag.vertices_at_round(R)`; (2) `present = vertices.iter().map(|v| v.member_id).collect()`; (3) **partition guard** ‚Äî if `present.len() < min_active_count` skip (advance `last_scored` without observing; honest validators shouldn't be punished for inability to communicate through a network split); (4) `missing = committee - present`; (5) `emissions = accumulator.observe_round(epoch, R, missing)`; (6) forward each emission to the consumer's channel. **Config knobs**: `tick_interval = 125 ms` (matches wave-committer cadence); `completed_round_lag = 8` (safety margin for late-arriving vertices); `min_active_count = 86` (= `MAX_BYZANTINE + 1` per the catalog); `committee = vec![0..128]` (static for v1; per-epoch membership lands with DKG); `epoch = 0` (v1 stub matching `DEFAULT_EPOCH`). **Validator startup** spawns the detector + consumer pair as long-running tokio tasks alongside the 4 existing safety-offense consumers, sharing the same shutdown signal. The consumer uses `runtime.consensus_store` for slasher + escrow snapshot persistence. Solo / small-committee devnets get the partition guard for free (active count always below 86 ‚Üí detector skips every round in observe mode); multi-validator mainnet detects normally once ‚â•86 members are present at a round. Three new `MainLoopMetrics` counters: `downtime_detector_rounds_scanned`, `downtime_detector_rounds_skipped_partition`, `downtime_detector_emitted`. **Tests**: 6 detector unit tests covering empty-DAG no-op, full-attendance quiet, missing-member-below-threshold counter-freezing behaviour (single emit per epoch), partition-guard skip, completed-round-lag holding back recent rounds, and re-scan idempotency. `cargo test -p pyde-engine-node --lib` green ‚Äî 376 passed (was 370). Workspace all-green. Clippy clean. **Slashing-detector catalog after this PR**: ‚úÖ #1 Equivocation, ‚úÖ #2 BadStateRootSignature, ‚úÖ #3 BadAnchorAttestation, ‚úÖ #4 InvalidVertexStructure, üö´ #5 BadDecryptionShare (blocked on DKG), üö´ #6 DkgParticipationFailure (blocked on DKG), üö´ #7 DecryptionShareWithholding (blocked on threshold decryption), ‚úÖ #8 **ExtendedDowntime**, ‚è≠Ô∏è #9 BadBatchAttestation (unblocked; operational-tier), üö´ #10 Censorship (v2). ‚Äî PR [#193](https://github.com/pyde-net/engine/pull/193)
- [x] **slashing + node: `ExtendedDowntime` accumulator + consumer (Œ≥.slashing.extended-downtime, PR1/2)** ‚Äî offense #8 from the slashing rules catalog. First PR of a two-PR slice; this one is pure-logic + slashing-pipeline wiring. The detector task that scans `VertexStore` for missing per-round producers, the validator startup wiring, and the network-partition guard land in PR2. **`slashing::downtime::DowntimeAccumulator`**: per-(epoch, member_id) missed-round counter. `observe_round(epoch, round, missing)` increments the counter for each missing member; when a member crosses the threshold (`DEFAULT_DOWNTIME_EMISSION_THRESHOLD = 100` = 5% slash at 0.05%/round per the catalog) ONE `DowntimeDetected` event emits for that `(epoch, member_id)` pair. Subsequent observed misses in the same epoch silently skip (the slash + jail consequence is already in flight; further duplicates would just generate noise). Round-idempotent: repeat observations at rounds ‚â§ `last_scored_round` are dropped, so a detector restart doesn't double-count. `reset_epoch(epoch)` drops per-epoch state on an epoch boundary. **`build_liveness_evidence(offense, accused, epoch)`**: shared builder for the four Liveness-class offenses ‚Äî auto-detected shape (`reporter: None`, `payload: Liveness`). **`node::extended_downtime_consumer::ExtendedDowntimeConsumer`**: mirrors the four existing safety-offense consumers (`Equivocation`, `BadStateRootSig`, `BadAnchorAttestation`, `InvalidVertexStructure`). - [x] **node: devnet `--fork` accepts an RPC URL (Phase 2)** ‚Äî A6 Phase 2 close-out. #186 + #187 + #189 shipped the producer (`Snapshotter`), loader (`SnapshotLoader`), wave-numbering parity, + the validator-side `pyde_getSnapshot` RPC. - [x] **wasm-exec: `pyde::falcon_verify` returns `ERR_SIGNATURE_INVALID` on undecodable bytes (A13)** ‚Äî closes otigen Phase 1 follow-up A13. [HOST_FN_ABI ¬ß7.7](https://book.pyde.network/companion/HOST_FN_ABI_SPEC.html#77-cryptographic-primitives) says "0 if signature is valid, `ERR_SIGNATURE_INVALID` otherwise" ‚Äî "otherwise" is unconditional, covering bytes that don't decode as the FALCON-512 wire shape, not just bytes that decode but fail verification. Engine trapped on undecodable pubkey or sig bytes via `return Err(wasmtime::Error::msg(...))`, making the canonical defensive idiom `if rc != 0 { revert(...) }` **uncatchable** for user-supplied bad sigs (multi-sig, oracle proofs, attestation, threshold-decryption requests). Same class as A9 (return polarity inverted, #182) and A12 (transfer return polarity inverted, #188). **Fix**: two `from_bytes() ‚Üí None` sites in `host_fns/crypto.rs::register_crypto` now `return Ok(ERR_SIGNATURE_INVALID)` instead of trapping. Module doc reframed ‚Äî the trap-vs-return-code boundary now spells out the spec literal: oversize input traps (¬ß4 host-fn-invariant violation = DoS guard against gigantic buffer allocations before the gas check fires); undecodable-but-within-cap input returns `ERR_SIGNATURE_INVALID`. **Tests**: existing `host_fn_falcon_verify_rejects_malformed_sig_length` renamed `..._malformed_sig_returns_err_signature_invalid` + WAT asserts `i32.const -17` against the return rather than expecting a trap; new `..._malformed_pubkey_returns_err_signature_invalid` exercises the paired pubkey-decode path (zero-byte pubkey rejected by `pyde_crypto`, contract observes -17 + exits cleanly); existing oversize tests (`rejects_oversize_msg`, `rejects_oversize_sig`) unchanged. `cargo test -p pyde-engine-wasm-exec --lib` green ‚Äî 239 passed (was 238). Clippy clean. Otigen-side: `simple-multisig::malformed_signature_rejected` test under `--engine` flips from failing to passing **without contract changes** ‚Äî the contract's `if rc != 0 { fail(b"BadSignature") }` idiom is the canonical spec pattern; the engine's drift was what broke it. Per the otigen brief: A13 closes the last spec-drift surface in the ¬ß7 host fns. ‚Äî PR [#190](https://github.com/pyde-net/engine/pull/190)
- [x] **node: `pyde_getSnapshot` RPC method (unblocks devnet `--fork <RPC>`)** ‚Äî A6 Phase-2 enabler. Producer side (`Snapshotter`) was already shipped; loader side (`SnapshotLoader`) + devnet `--fork <FILE>` wiring landed in #186 + #187. The missing piece was a way for a remote consumer to **fetch** a snapshot from a running validator's RPC. **Method**: new `pyde_getSnapshot` on the validator-side JSON-RPC surface (same `axum` router that serves `pyde_getReceipt` / `pyde_getTx` / `pyde_getWave` ‚Äî production scope, not devnet). No params. Returns **standard-base64-encoded** borsh-encoded `SnapshotBundle { manifest, chunks }` at the state store's current `last_flushed_wave`. STANDARD alphabet (RFC 4648 ¬ß4, no URL-safe variant) so consumers don't worry about base64 dialect; ~25% smaller wire than hex on multi-MB payloads. Same byte shape `--fork <FILE>` consumes ‚Äî consumers base64-decode the result, borsh-decode into a `SnapshotBundle`, and pass to `SnapshotLoader::apply` whose per-chunk Blake3 + state-root gates verify transport integrity end-to-end. **Plumbing**: `RpcContext.state_store: Arc<StateStore>` added; constructor signature gains the new param; validator bind site (`run_validator_with_hook`) passes `runtime.state_store.clone()` through; `base64 = "0.22"` added at workspace + direct dep on `pyde-engine-node`. **Tests**: `get_snapshot_on_empty_state_returns_well_formed_bundle` decodes + asserts manifest shape for an unflushed store; `get_snapshot_round_trips_a_populated_state_store` commits 8 slots + flushes + fetches via RPC + feeds the decoded bundle through `SnapshotLoader::apply` against a fresh target store (the loader's state-root gate is the end-to-end integrity check); `get_snapshot_rejects_unexpected_params` confirms the method takes no params. `cargo test -p pyde-engine-node --lib rpc::` green ‚Äî 40 passed (was 37). Workspace all-green. Clippy clean. **Follow-up**: devnet `--fork <RPC>` becomes a small follow-up PR ‚Äî the runner adds a URL-vs-path code path that JSON-RPC-calls `pyde_getSnapshot`, base64-decodes, and hands the bytes to the same `SnapshotLoader::apply` the file path already feeds. No new spec surface. ‚Äî PR [#189](https://github.com/pyde-net/engine/pull/189)
- [x] **wasm-exec: align `pyde::transfer` return to spec (A12)** ‚Äî closes otigen Phase 1 follow-up A12. [HOST_FN_ABI ¬ß7.2](https://book.pyde.network/companion/HOST_FN_ABI_SPEC.html#72-account--balance-host-fns) declares `pyde::transfer` returns `0` on success + `ERR_INSUFFICIENT_BALANCE` (`-3`, ¬ß4) on insufficient caller balance ‚Äî the 0-is-success convention every other status-code-returning host fn uses (`sload`, `emit_event`, `cross_call`, `falcon_verify`, etc.). Engine returned the inverted `1`/`0` boolean. **Impact**: every contract following the spec convention (`if rc != 0 { fail }`) silently inverted transfer success + failure ‚Äî sufficient-balance transfers were reverted, insufficient-balance ones appeared successful. Concretely: otigen examples that route payouts through transfer (`simple-multisig`'s 4 transfer-reaching tests under `--engine`, plus `erc20-token`, `vesting`, anything implementing a disburse step). Fix: 4 LOC change in `host_fns/balances.rs` (`TRANSFER_OK` `1` ‚Üí `0`; `TRANSFER_INSUFFICIENT` `0` ‚Üí re-export of canonical `pyde_engine_types::error::ERR_INSUFFICIENT_BALANCE`); module doc reframed; `constants_match_spec` test updated; three existing end-to-end tests in `executor.rs` retargeted at the spec-aligned shape (`host_fn_transfer_self_returns_ok_no_state_change` + `host_fn_transfer_credits_recipient` use `if unreachable end` directly on the return; `host_fn_transfer_insufficient_returns_zero` renamed `..._returns_err_insufficient_balance` + WAT compares to `i32.const -3`). All 238 wasm-exec lib tests green. Otigen-side: the 4 of 9 `simple-multisig` tests under `--engine` (`two_of_three`, `three_of_three`, `replay_same_action_hash`, `malformed_signature`) flip from failing to passing **without contract changes** ‚Äî the contract idiom (`if rc != 0 { fail }`) is the canonical spec pattern; it was the engine's drift that broke it. Per the otigen brief: A12 is the last known spec-drift fix in the host-fn surface ‚Äî `--engine` should now run every otigen example known-good under legacy. ‚Äî PR [#188](https://github.com/pyde-net/engine/pull/188)
- [x] **node: wave-numbering parity for devnet `--fork`** ‚Äî A6 follow-up. After #186 loaded a snapshot at `manifest.wave_id = N`, `DevnetState.current_wave` stayed at 0 and the next committed wave landed at 1 ‚Äî `pyde_waveId` returned 0 immediately after boot of a forked devnet, breaking the "fork at wave N + new waves N+1..." semantic this PR closes. **Plumbing**: `ValidatorRunConfig.initial_wave_id: Option<WaveId>` + `ValidatorRuntimeConfig.initial_wave_id: Option<WaveId>` thread the seed through to two construction sites: `DevnetState::with_initial_wave_id(N)` seeds `Inner.current_wave`, and `WaveCommitterConfig.initial_wave_id_floor: Option<WaveId>` reaches `CommitterState::resume(store, floor)` which computes `next_wave_id = max(consensus_highest + 1, floor + 1)` ‚Äî honouring the fork seed without ever regressing waves already committed in consensus. **Devnet runner**: new `peek_fork_manifest_wave_id(path)` decodes the bundle's manifest **before** runtime build so the seed reaches both subsystems at construction time. The hook re-decodes the bundle to apply chunks; double-read is fine for the small file. **`--fork` now suppresses prefund**: prefund writes at wave 0 + snapshot apply at wave N would put extra leaves in the JMT at version 0 that the snapshot's `manifest.state_root` doesn't account for ‚Äî the loader's state-root verification gate would fail. Forked-chain users get their accounts from the forked state anyway. When `config.fork` is `Some`, the runner generates an empty `accounts` Vec and the prefund hook becomes a no-op. **Tests**: 2 unit tests on `DevnetState::with_initial_wave_id` (fresh state at 0; seeded state at N) + 3 unit tests on `CommitterState::resume(_, floor)` (empty store + floor ‚Üí floor+1; floor below consensus ‚Üí consensus wins; floor above consensus ‚Üí floor wins) + 2 unit tests on `peek_fork_manifest_wave_id` (decodes manifest wave_id from a real bundle; returns None for None input) + 1 e2e test updated to assert `prefunded_count == 0` (was 1) per the new --fork-suppresses-prefund semantic. `cargo test -p pyde-engine-node --lib` green ‚Äî 359 passed (was 352). Workspace all-green. Clippy clean. ‚Äî PR [#187](https://github.com/pyde-net/engine/pull/187)
- [x] **state + node: snapshot loader + devnet `--fork <FILE>` (A6)** ‚Äî closes otigen Phase 1 ask A6 (Phase-1 split). Producer side (`pyde_engine_state::Snapshotter`) was already shipped; this PR adds the consumer side (`pyde_engine_state::snapshot_loader::SnapshotLoader`) + wires it into the devnet's pre-run hook under a new `--fork` flag. **New types**: `SnapshotBundle { manifest, chunks }` is the borsh-encoded on-disk container ‚Äî same shape the future `pyde_getSnapshot` RPC will return; `SnapshotLoader::new(&store).apply(bundle)` runs the verification chain that mirrors [STATE_SYNC.md ¬ß"Verification Flow"](https://book.pyde.network/companion/STATE_SYNC) steps 1-4: (1) per-chunk Blake3 integrity vs `manifest.chunk_hashes[i]`, (2) coverage + ordering + `total_keys` sum, (3) apply via a **single** `StateCommitter::commit` at `manifest.wave_id` with all chunk entries flattened (multiple commits at the same JMT version queue overlapping node batches whose flush order produces divergent state roots ‚Äî discovered during round-trip testing), (4) state-root gate: `flush_once` then re-derive JMT root and compare to `manifest.state_root`. **Error taxonomy**: `SnapshotLoaderError::{ChunkCountMismatch, ChunkIndexOutOfOrder, ChunkHashMismatch, TotalKeysMismatch, StateRootMismatch}` + transparent `StateError` pass-through. The loader is **byte-source-agnostic** ‚Äî file / future RPC / peer streaming all feed into the same `apply` call. **Devnet `--fork <FILE>` wiring**: `DevnetRunConfig.fork: Option<PathBuf>` threads through to the pre-run hook which calls `load_snapshot_into_runtime` BEFORE prefund credits apply (the standard `--fork` semantic ‚Äî prefunds layer on top of the forked state). Load failure is fatal: `eprintln!` + `std::process::exit(1)` rather than serving a half-loaded chain. Banner surfaces the fork path. **Wave counter restarts at 0 locally** ‚Äî "fork at wave N + new waves N+1..." numbering is a follow-up requiring `DevnetState` to boot from a non-zero `wave_id`. **`--fork <RPC>` deferred** until the chain-side `pyde_getSnapshot` RPC ships; the loader's byte-source agnosticism means that's a pure RPC-plumbing PR. **Tests**: 9 new `pyde-engine-state` unit tests covering verify / apply / tamper rejection / borsh round-trip / round-trip JMT-root equality + 1 new `pyde-engine-node` end-to-end test booting a devnet with `--fork` pointing at a real `Snapshotter::build`-produced file. `cargo test --workspace --no-fail-fast` all-green (state 144 was 135, node 352 was 351, every other crate passing). Clippy clean. ‚Äî PR [#186](https://github.com/pyde-net/engine/pull/186)
- [x] **wasm-exec + node: rename `BlockContext` ‚Üí `WaveContext` (wave-terminology cleanup)** ‚Äî Pyde's consensus model is waves, not blocks. The host-fn ABI surface contracts call has been spec-aligned at `pyde::wave_id` + `pyde::wave_timestamp` since otigen Phase 1 ‚Äî but the surrounding execution-context struct + its timestamp field were still named `BlockContext` + `block_timestamp` per the deferred note at `crates/wasm-exec/src/host_fns/context.rs` ("internal struct field stays `block_timestamp` until a broader rename of the surrounding context struct"). This is that broader rename ‚Äî **purely internal, no wire-format impact** (the host fn surface names contracts depend on are already `wave_*`). Renames: `BlockContext` ‚Üí `WaveContext`, `BlockContext.block_timestamp` ‚Üí `WaveContext.wave_timestamp`, `HostContext.block` ‚Üí `HostContext.wave`, `HostContext::new(block, ‚Ä¶)` ‚Üí `HostContext::new(wave, ‚Ä¶)`, `DevnetState::build_block_context` ‚Üí `build_wave_context`, `DevnetState::block_context_for_view_call` ‚Üí `wave_context_for_view_call`, local var/param names `block`/`block_ctx` ‚Üí `wave`/`wave_ctx`, test names `..._returns_block_wave_id` etc. ‚Üí `..._returns_wave_context_wave_id` etc. Stale doc comments mentioning "Block-level" / "block timestamp" / "BlockContext" updated throughout. **Verification**: `cargo test --workspace --no-fail-fast` all-green (wasm-exec 238, node 351, + every other crate passing in lockstep), `cargo clippy -p pyde-engine-wasm-exec -p pyde-engine-node --lib --tests -- -D warnings` clean, `cargo check --workspace` clean. No behavioral change ‚Äî otigen / contract authors observe no diff. ‚Äî PR [#185](https://github.com/pyde-net/engine/pull/185)
- [x] **wasm-exec: cross-call attribute enforcement + REENTRANT guard (A5)** ‚Äî closes otigen Phase 1 ask A5. [HOST_FN_ABI ¬ß3.5.2](https://book.pyde.network/companion/HOST_FN_ABI_SPEC.html#352-per-call-dispatch-flow) says the per-call dispatch flow applies to "top-level tx or cross_call" ‚Äî same constructor lockout, payable check, view-mode flip, and reentrancy guard at both entry points. Top-level dispatch already enforced these (#180); cross-call paths (`cross_call`, `cross_call_static`, `delegate_call`) called `execute_call` directly, bypassing the dispatcher, so: internal helpers (non-`ENTRY` fns) were reachable; `#[payable]` was not enforced on sub-call value; `#[constructor]` was reachable post-deploy; `#[view]` attribute wasn't flipped on the sub-frame; `#[reentrant]` was not enforced ‚Äî re-entry was unrestricted. **Fix**: new `resolve_cross_call(target_abi, fn_name, value, parent_view_mode, caller_call_stack, target_address)` in `dispatch.rs` returns either `Ok(CrossCallResolution { entry_name, callee_view_mode, attrs })` or `Err(CrossCallPrecheckError::{InvalidFunctionName, ValueTransferNotPayable, ReentrancyBlocked})`. All three cross-call host fns route through it + surface the precheck errors as the canonical negative `i32` codes per HOST_FN_ABI ¬ß4 (`-13`, `-12`, `-9`). `HostContext` gains `call_stack: Vec<(Address, String)>`; `execute_contract_call` pushes the entry frame; each cross-call clones the caller's stack + pushes the sub-frame, so re-entry into any frame already on the stack (direct or transitive) returns `ERR_REENTRANCY_BLOCKED` unless the target is `#[reentrant]`. `delegate_call`'s reentrancy key is `(caller_self_addr, entry_name)` because delegated code runs as the caller. **Spec-drift fixes folded in**: `ERR_INVALID_FUNCTION_NAME` -7 ‚Üí -13, `ERR_CROSS_CALL_FAILED` -8 ‚Üí -10, `ERR_CALLEE_NOT_FOUND` (impl-defined -10 colliding with spec's `ERR_CROSS_CALL_FAILED`) removed (delegate_call's no-code-target case collapses into `ERR_INVALID_FUNCTION_NAME`; cross_call's no-code is still pure value-transfer + `Ok(0)`), `ERR_CROSS_CALL_DEPTH_EXCEEDED` (impl-defined -9 colliding with `ERR_REENTRANCY_BLOCKED`) removed (depth-exceeded traps per ¬ß4's StackOverflow class), cache-miss for a known code_hash now traps (was silent `ERR_CALLEE_NOT_FOUND` collision). **Tests**: 12 new dispatch unit tests covering every precheck path + 4 new end-to-end cross-call tests through `execute_contract_call` (REENTRANT self-reentry blocks; same with `#[reentrant]` attribute allows; PAYABLE precheck returns -12 without debiting the caller; unknown-fn precheck returns -13) + 4 existing cross-call e2e tests updated to inject `pyde.abi` custom sections into their callee/target fixtures. `cargo test -p pyde-engine-wasm-exec --lib` green ‚Äî 238 passed (was 234). `cargo test -p pyde-engine-node --lib` green ‚Äî 351 passed. Clippy clean. **Otigen follow-up**: example contracts (`simple-multisig`, `dao-governance`, `vesting`, etc.) now get spec-correct cross-call enforcement. Pre-A5 contracts that happened to depend on the old non-enforcement (e.g., reaching internal helpers via cross-call by name) surface `ERR_INVALID_FUNCTION_NAME` and need either `#[entry]` on the helper or a structural change. ‚Äî PR [#184](https://github.com/pyde-net/engine/pull/184)
- [x] JSON-RPC server (per `HOST_FN_ABI_SPEC ¬ß15.4-15.5` + chapter 17 method list) ‚Äî **scaffold + five read methods shipped**: spec-compliant JSON-RPC 2.0 dispatcher over axum 0.7 (single + batch, notifications excluded from responses, five standard error codes, HTTP 204 for all-notification batches), `RpcContext` with peer_id / falcon_pubkey / listen_addrs / agent_version (`pyde/<CARGO_PKG_VERSION>`) / protocol_version (`pyde/1`) / `Arc<MainLoopMetrics>` / `Arc<ConsensusStore>`, `bind_rpc_server` returns resolved `SocketAddr` synchronously so port-conflicts surface immediately, graceful shutdown via `watch::Receiver<bool>`. Wired into `pyde validator --rpc-listen <addr>` (optional; default disabled ‚Äî no auth in v1). Methods: identity/telemetry ‚Äî `pyde_getNodeInfo` + `pyde_getMetrics` (PR [#73](https://github.com/pyde-net/engine/pull/73)); persistent-store reads ‚Äî `pyde_getReceipt(hash)` + `pyde_getTx(hash)` + `pyde_getWave(wave_id)` (PR [#79](https://github.com/pyde-net/engine/pull/79); hex hash params with or without `0x` prefix; misses return `null`; raw serde wire format until chapter 17 finalises). The remaining chapter-17 method set (`pyde_call`, `pyde_sendRawTransaction`, `pyde_getLogs`, etc.) lands in follow-up PRs as state + execution layers wire up.
- [x] `consensus_store` with `WriteOptions::set_sync(true)` (per Ch 16 ¬ß16.12) ‚Äî **storage skeleton shipped**: `ConsensusStore` wraps `Arc<rocksdb::DB>` (cheap clone, thread-safe), opens three column families on first run (`receipts_cf` TxHash ‚Üí Receipt, `txs_cf` TxHash ‚Üí Tx, `waves_cf` WaveId BE ‚Üí WaveCommitRecord ‚Äî BE keys so iter ordering matches numeric order for future range scans). Every write builds a fresh `WriteOptions { sync: true }` so callers never accidentally share a non-sync handle. Typed helpers per CF + `highest_wave_id` (reverse iterator) + `flush`. `ConsensusStoreError` taxonomy (RocksDb / Decode / Encode / MissingColumnFamily). Wired into `ValidatorRuntime` + `pyde validator --consensus-store-path <dir>`. Main-loop write-through lands in a follow-up once the execution layer hands us wave-commit records. ‚Äî PR [#76](https://github.com/pyde-net/engine/pull/76)
- [ ] `panic = "abort"` on persist failure
- [x] Validator role ‚Äî FALCON-512 keypair management: `FalconKeypair` (disk-backed, atomic tmp‚Üírename persistence, integrity-checked on load via re-derived pubkey, secret redacted in Debug). `impl Signer` for direct use in vertex production. Borsh-encoded `FalconKeypairFile` with `version: u8` so swapping in real `pyde-crypto` FALCON-512 bumps the version. v1 ships a deterministic mock that matches `MockSigner`'s Blake3-extension pattern; production crypto swaps in when `pyde-crypto` ships. Wired into `ValidatorRuntime` + `pyde validator --falcon-keypair <path>`. ‚Äî PR [#70](https://github.com/pyde-net/engine/pull/70)
- [ ] Validator role ‚Äî attestation + key rotation (depends on production `pyde-crypto` FALCON-512)
- [x] Persistence ‚Äî **txs_cf write-through shipped**: validator main loop routes `pyde/mempool/1` gossip to `consensus_store.put_tx(canonical_tx_hash(tx), tx)`. New `pyde-engine-tx::canonical_tx_hash` ships ahead of Œ≤.3 ‚Äî `TxHash = Blake3(canonical_pre_image(tx))` per Ch 11 ¬ß11.6, same bytes the producer FALCON-signs (Œ≤.3 will adopt the same function for mempool admission, receipt indexing, execution-side lookups, so the keys remain interoperable). 4 new `MainLoopMetrics` counters (received / persisted / decode-failures / persist-failures). Operator can now publish a tx on gossip and read it back via `pyde_getTx(hash)`. ‚Äî PR [#88](https://github.com/pyde-net/engine/pull/88)
- [ ] Persistence ‚Äî receipts_cf + waves_cf write-through (lands when execution layer commits waves)

**Œ≥ BAR:** `cargo test` clean on `consensus-side` branch; consensus loop runs end-to-end with `MockStateView` + `MockMempool` + `MockNetwork`; vertex production + anchor selection + commit work in isolation.

---

## MC-2 ‚Äî INTEGRATION `[SEQ] ‚Üí MC-1 all streams` ‚Äî Œ≥-owned

Merge `execution-side` and `consensus-side` branches to `main`. Bring up a local devnet.

### MC-2 spike ‚úÖ shipped (precedes full MC-2)

A **single-validator** devnet running the real consensus driver end-to-end with stubbed crypto / network / persistence. The "Pyde transfers value, today" demonstration ‚Äî real Mysticeti 3-stage commit, real BFS subdag walk, real `WaveCommitRecord` assembly, real `HardFinalityCert` collection, for a real transfer transaction.

- [x] `DevnetState` ‚Äî `StateMutator` impl with real transfer + fee + nonce-window logic ‚Äî PR [#15](https://github.com/pyde-net/engine/pull/15)
- [x] `DevnetExecutor` ‚Äî pure pre-flight `Executor` impl ‚Äî PR [#16](https://github.com/pyde-net/engine/pull/16)
- [x] `Devnet` composer + `Wallet` ‚Äî full single-validator commit loop ‚Äî PR [#17](https://github.com/pyde-net/engine/pull/17)
- [x] `run_smoke` scenario + 8 integration tests ‚Äî PR [#18](https://github.com/pyde-net/engine/pull/18)
- [x] `pyde devnet --smoke` CLI subcommand ‚Äî PR [#19](https://github.com/pyde-net/engine/pull/19)
- [x] README "Try the demo" + bench baseline link ‚Äî PR [#20](https://github.com/pyde-net/engine/pull/20)

Reproduce: `cargo run --bin pyde -- devnet --smoke`. Full bench baseline: [`crates/consensus/benches/baseline.md`](https://github.com/pyde-net/engine/blob/main/crates/consensus/benches/baseline.md).

### Full MC-2 (ahead ‚Äî needs real Œ≤ + real Œ≥ libs wired)

The MC-2 spike (single-validator, stubbed crypto/network/persistence) proved the consensus + execution shape works end-to-end. **Full MC-2 swaps the stubs for the real Œ≤ + Œ≥ crates** that landed in MC-1. The work is mechanical wiring, NOT new design ‚Äî every component is already shipped; node-binary assembly is the last mile.

#### Merge gates
- [x] Œ≤-stream ‚Üí `main` ‚Äî execution PR [#130](https://github.com/pyde-net/engine/pull/130) (Œ≤.1 state + Œ≤.2 account + Œ≤.3 tx + Œ≤.4 wasm-exec + Œ≤.5 mempool, all rolled up)
- [ ] Œ≥-stream ‚Üí `main` ‚Äî Œ≥ owns; final Œ≥.X PRs land first, then a `consensus-side ‚Üí main` milestone PR mirroring Œ≤'s pattern

#### Node binary (`crates/node`) ‚Äî currently a 34-line scaffold; needs to grow into the integration crate

**Persistence wiring (replaces `DevnetState` stub from spike)**
- [ ] Construct `StateStore::open(StateConfig::new(data_dir))` at boot ‚Äî owns RocksDB handle, 7 column families, all PIP-4 caching
- [ ] Wrap as `AccountStateView::new(state_store)` ‚Äî the production `StateView + StateMutator` impl (Œ≤.2 PR-5 / PR [#69](https://github.com/pyde-net/engine/pull/69))
- [ ] Wire `StateMutator::commit_with_events(wave_id, updates, events) ‚Üí WaveCommitRecord` into the consensus commit path; this is what closes the Œ≤.1 PR-9 `NotImplemented` stub on `commit_wave`
- [ ] Wire `Deploy` tx handler to call `WasmExecutor::compile_and_persist(state, bytes)` so the WASM blob lands in `code_cf` atomically with the receipt (PR [#115](https://github.com/pyde-net/engine/pull/115) shipped the storage primitive ‚Äî the handler wire-up is still placeholder)
- [x] `receipts_cf` / `txs_cf` ‚Äî landed in the state crate (not the node) via PR [#132](https://github.com/pyde-net/engine/pull/132). `StateStore::store_receipt` / `get_receipt` / `store_tx` / `get_tx` (`TxHash`-keyed, borsh-encoded). Append-only with overwrite-on-re-org semantics aligned to the 1-epoch bounded rollback policy. The `consensus_store` (separate Œ≥-owned CF for vertex/round persistence) still needs `WriteOptions::set_sync(true)` per Ch 16 ¬ß16.12 ‚Äî Œ≥-side task

**Executor wiring (replaces `DevnetExecutor` stub from spike)**
- [ ] Construct `WasmExecutor::new()` (or `with_cache_config(...)` for tuned nodes) once at boot ‚Äî the singleton holds the wasmtime `Engine` + `ModuleCache` with the LRU+TTL policy from PR [#119](https://github.com/pyde-net/engine/pull/119)
- [ ] Wrap as `WasmExecutorAdapter::new(executor, accounts)` (Œ≤.4 PR-17 / PR [#114](https://github.com/pyde-net/engine/pull/114)) ‚Äî the `Executor` trait impl that dispatches by `tx.tx_type` into Œ≤.3 handlers
- [ ] Hand `WasmExecutorAdapter` to the consensus `Driver` (Œ≥.1) as the `Arc<dyn Executor>` it expects
- [x] `WasmExecutorAdapter` interior mutability ‚Äî `wave_id` + `base_fee` are `Arc<AtomicU64>` so the node updates them post-commit through the shared `Arc<dyn Executor>` reference. `update_wave_id(&self, ...)` + `update_base_fee(&self, ...)` ship in PR [#133](https://github.com/pyde-net/engine/pull/133). Per-tx dispatch snapshots both atomics once.
- [ ] Cold-restart path: on boot, scan `state.list_all_code_hashes()` (shipped via PR [#135](https://github.com/pyde-net/engine/pull/135) ‚Äî iterates code_cf, returns `Vec<Blake3Hash>` in RocksDB-natural order) and call `WasmExecutor::load_from_persistent` for each to warm the ModuleCache to its target hot-set size. Caller-orchestration still pending (lands in the node binary).

**Mempool wiring (replaces stub from spike)**
- [ ] Construct `Mempool::new(MempoolConfig::default().with_chain_id(genesis.chain_id))`
- [ ] Wrap as `PydeMempoolView::new(mempool, account_state_view, initial_base_fee)` (Œ≤.5 PR-6 / PR [#129](https://github.com/pyde-net/engine/pull/129))
- [ ] Validator-loop wiring: when Œ≥'s `WaveCommitter` produces a batch, call `view.drain_for_batch(MAX_BATCH_BYTES)` (FIFO-per-sender; priority-fee ordering is a follow-up if MEV metrics demand it)
- [ ] Post-commit cleanup: for each tx in the committed wave, `mempool.remove(tx_hash)` to drop included txs

**Network wiring (Œ≥.2 `net` crate) ‚Äî the most-novel Œ≤‚ÜîŒ≥ surface**
- [x] Tx-gossip topic on Gossipsub ‚Äî `topics::MEMPOOL = "pyde/mempool/1"` (parallel to `VERTICES` + `BATCHES` + `BEACON_SHARES` + `STATE_ROOT_SIGS` constants that Œ≥.2 already ships).
- [x] Inbound: `mainloop.rs` routes `pyde/mempool/1` gossip through `Mempool::admit_gossiped` (signature, nonce, balance, chain_id, structural, dedupe). Per-source counter increments under `admitted_gossiped`.
- [x] **Outbound tx publish on local admission (closes the loop)** ‚Äî `NetworkView::publish_tx(tx: Tx)` added to the trait surface (this PR DID change `pyde-engine-interfaces` ‚Äî the trait grew one method; row updated below). `NetworkHandle::publish_tx` impl borsh-serialises + publishes on `topics::MEMPOOL`. `DevnetRpcContext` gains `network: Option<Arc<dyn NetworkView>>` + `with_network(...)` builder; `handle_send_raw_transaction` clones the tx before `mempool.insert` (which consumes it), and on successful insert publishes via `network.publish_tx(cloned)`. Publish failures log at `warn` but do NOT fail the RPC ‚Äî the tx is already in the local mempool and will be included in a future wave even if no peer sees the gossip; solo devnet returning "no peers" is expected + benign. `MockNetwork` gains the impl + `published_tx_count` counter + `published_txs()` snapshot accessor. `devnet/runner.rs` wires `runtime.network_handle.clone()` into the RPC context at the only RPC-bind site so every devnet boot publishes. Result: a tx submitted to validator A via `pyde_sendRawTransaction` now reaches validator B's mempool through the existing inbound `pyde/mempool/1` ‚Üí `admit_gossiped` pipeline. Multi-validator mempools actually converge. ‚Äî PR [#246](https://github.com/pyde-net/engine/pull/246)
- [x] **Update to "NetworkView left untouched" assumption** ‚Äî the trait DID grow `publish_tx` in PR [#246](https://github.com/pyde-net/engine/pull/246). All implementations (`NetworkHandle`, `MockNetwork`, `RecordingNetwork` + `FailingNetwork` test doubles in `vertex_producer.rs`) updated in the same PR. The `pyde-engine-interfaces` crate is no longer fully frozen at the `NetworkView` surface ‚Äî the outbound tx-publish path required it.

**Beacon + DKG wiring**
- [ ] `BlockContext.beacon` (used by Œ≤.4 `pyde::beacon_get` host fn ‚Äî PR [#113](https://github.com/pyde-net/engine/pull/113)) sourced from Œ≥.15 PR-3 per-epoch beacon derivation flow (currently static all-zeros stub per PR [#112](https://github.com/pyde-net/engine/pull/112)); the node threads the real beacon through to `WasmExecutorAdapter.update_block_context()`
- [ ] DKG ceremony at epoch boundaries (Œ≥.3) ‚Äî node listens for DKG events, persists own threshold share

**RPC surface (HOST_FN_ABI ¬ß15.4‚Äì¬ß15.5 + Ch 17)** ‚Äî `pyde-engine-node::devnet::rpc` (full method catalog) + `pyde-engine-node::rpc` (validator-side sparse ‚Äî only `pyde_getSnapshot` today). Catalog lift onto the validator/full path is a follow-up workstream.
- [x] `pyde_sendRawTransaction(bytes)` ‚Üí borsh-decode ‚Üí `PydeMempoolView::insert` ‚Üí return tx_hash on Admitted; on success, republish via `NetworkView::publish_tx` for peer propagation (PR [#246](https://github.com/pyde-net/engine/pull/246)). Live on devnet RPC since the production wave-committer wave-commit work earlier in the milestone.
- [x] `pyde_getTransactionReceipt(hash)` ‚Üí DevnetState in-memory receipt map (the production `receipts_cf` read-through path is a follow-up).
- [x] `pyde_getBalance(addr)` / `pyde_getTransactionCount(addr)` ‚Üí `StateView` against the live `AccountStore`. **`pyde_getAccount(addr)`** + **`pyde_getContractCode(addr)`** added in PR [#247](https://github.com/pyde-net/engine/pull/247): `pyde_getAccount` returns the full account snapshot (address, account_type, balance, next nonce, code_hash, state_root) in one round-trip ‚Äî under-the-hood a single `accounts().get(addr, wave_id)` call with struct-field accesses (NOT four StateView trait round-trips that would each read + borsh-decode the same record). Missing addresses get a fresh-EOA-shaped snapshot (zeros) rather than a 404 ‚Äî wallets querying unseen addresses get sensible defaults. `pyde_getContractCode` returns `0x<wasm-hex>` for a contract or `"0x"` for an EOA / unseen / zero-hash address (inspectors / wallets / verifiers treat `"0x"` as "skip ABI work"). Both methods are documented as canonical in pyde-book Ch 17.4 and parallel to Ethereum's `eth_getAccount` / `eth_getCode`; otigen `inspect <addr>` is the first consumer. ‚Äî PR [#247](https://github.com/pyde-net/engine/pull/247)
- [x] `pyde_call(target, fn_name, calldata)` (view call) ‚Üí `borsh(CallPayload)` envelope; spins a fresh `Store`, `WasmExecutor::execute_call` with `view_mode=true`. Unified onto the same `CallPayload` wire shape as `TxType::Standard` dispatch via engine #226 (no separate selector path).
- [x] `pyde_chainId` + `pyde_waveId` + `pyde_getStorageSlot` + `pyde_getEvents` ‚Äî live on the devnet RPC surface.
- [x] **`pyde_getLogs(filter)`** ‚Äî Ethereum-style filtered + cursor-paginated event-log query. Mirrors `otigen-rpc::types::{LogFilter, LogPage, LogCursor, LogEntry}` so the wrapper deserialises round-trip. Filter semantics: `from_wave` / `to_wave` (inclusive, defaults 0 / latest); per-request wave-range cap `GET_LOGS_WAVE_RANGE_CAP = 5000` (oversize surfaces `{"error": "wave range exceeds cap (‚Ä¶)"}`); multi-contract OR; position-sensitive topics (AND across positions, OR within position, wildcard at any position via empty inner array; events with arity < filter depth filtered out, NOT errored); opaque `(wave_id, tx_index, event_index)` cursor for resumable pagination; limit clamped to `GET_LOGS_MAX_LIMIT = 5000` (default 500); ordering matches existing `pyde_getEvents` (`(wave_id, tx_index, event_index)` ascending). Live on the devnet RPC; lift onto the production rpc.rs catalog deferred to the broader devnet ‚Üî production handler dedup PR. ‚Äî PR [#250](https://github.com/pyde-net/engine/pull/250)
- [x] **`pyde_resolveName(name)`** ‚Äî chain-side name-registry lookup over `pyde_engine_account::names::resolve(store, name, wave_id)`. Returns `0x<addr-hex>` on a registered name; JSON `null` on unregistered; `{"error": "invalid name format: ‚Ä¶"}` on `validate_name` failure so callers can distinguish "bad name" from "unregistered." Lifted into both `devnet/rpc.rs` AND production `rpc.rs` catalogs in the same PR ‚Äî the handler is short enough that duplication is fine until the dedup PR. Unblocks the "target by name" surface across otigen subcommands. ‚Äî PR [#250](https://github.com/pyde-net/engine/pull/250)
- [x] **Bugfix: `pyde_getContractCode` returned empty for deployed contracts** ‚Äî `DevnetState::StateView::get_code` read `inner.code: HashMap<‚Ä¶>` which was **never populated** (dead field). Meanwhile the deploy flow wrote contract bytes via `WasmExecutor::compile_and_persist` ‚Üí `StateStore::store_code` into the authoritative `code_cf`. Fix: `DevnetState::get_code` now routes through `state_store.get_code`, matching the path `get_code_hash` already used. `inner.code` field + initializer deleted. The production-side `rpc.rs` handler (PR [#249](https://github.com/pyde-net/engine/pull/249)) already read from `state_store` directly so the bug never existed on the validator / `pyde full` path; this fix makes the devnet RPC agree. Locked by two new unit tests: deployed wasm bytes returned byte-identical after `commit_wave_with_resolved_txs`, and unknown hash still returns `None` (the EOA / unseen path the RPC surfaces as `"0x"`). ‚Äî PR [#250](https://github.com/pyde-net/engine/pull/250)
- [ ] Event subscription (WebSocket): on `commit_with_events` push matching events to subscribers; index against `events_by_topic_cf` / `events_by_contract_cf` for replay
- [x] **Validator-side RPC catalog lift** ‚Äî the production-side `pyde-engine-node::rpc` module exposed only `getNodeInfo / getMetrics / getReceipt / getTx / getWave / getSnapshot`. The read+write catalog (`pyde_chainId` / `pyde_waveId` / `pyde_getBalance` / `pyde_getTransactionCount` / `pyde_getAccount` / `pyde_getContractCode` / `pyde_sendRawTransaction`) now lives on the production dispatcher too, so `pyde validator` + `pyde full` serve the same catalog explorers / wallets / indexers actually want. `RpcContext` gained `state` + `mempool` + `network` + `chain_id` fields + a `with_network(...)` builder; the bind site in `validator.rs` wires `runtime.state / mempool / network_handle` through. `dispatch_value` + `call_method` became `async` so `sendRawTransaction` can `await mempool.insert` + `await network.publish_tx` (same shape as the devnet path ‚Äî on success republishes the tx on `pyde/mempool/1` so peers see it). `pyde_getAccount` uses the same single-fetch optimisation as engine #247's devnet implementation (one `accounts.get(addr, wave_id)` call, struct-field access, no four-round-trip waste). Live smoke against `pyde full --rpc-listen 127.0.0.1:18549`: every new method returns the documented shape; old methods (`getNodeInfo` etc.) keep working. Intentional follow-up (separate PR): both `rpc.rs` and `devnet/rpc.rs` now have a ~95% identical catalog ‚Äî lifting handlers into a shared `rpc_methods` module would cut ~250 lines from devnet/rpc.rs; held back to keep this PR focused on the catalog lift itself. ‚Äî PR [#249](https://github.com/pyde-net/engine/pull/249)

**Bootstrap sequence**
- [x] **Genesis manifest + `pyde genesis init / validate / hash` CLI** ‚Äî `pyde_engine_types::genesis::Genesis` covers every value the chain spec freezes at launch: chain_id, chain_name, genesis_timestamp_unix, genesis_beacon_seed, founding committee (FALCON pubkey + operator address + locked stake per member_id), prefund balances, treasury multisig (signers + threshold + initial balance), optional airdrop (Poseidon2 Merkle root + deadline + sum + pool balance), tunable economics (base_fee_start, dispute_window_epochs, epoch_length_waves). Canonical bytes are borsh; human-edited templates use TOML with hex serde for 32-byte fields (Address / FALCON pubkey / merkle_root / beacon_seed) + u128-as-decimal-string (TOML's i64 cap). `Genesis::genesis_hash_blake3` is the chain identity hash operators publish out-of-band. Validation covers 20 invariants (zero chain_id, name length / charset, zero timestamp, empty / oversize / non-consecutive committee, duplicate FALCON pubkey or operator, below-min-stake, zero operator_address, duplicate prefund address, treasury signers / threshold / dup checks, airdrop zero-root). `pyde genesis init [--out genesis.toml] [--chain-id N] [--chain-name S] [--committee-size N] [--overwrite]` writes a placeholder template the operator MUST edit; `pyde genesis validate <path>` loads (auto-detect TOML vs borsh) + invariant-checks + prints summary + identity hash; `pyde genesis hash <path>` prints just the identity hash for out-of-band publication. ‚Äî PR [#236](https://github.com/pyde-net/engine/pull/236)
- [x] **First-boot path: `seed_state_from_genesis` + `GenesisRecord` on-disk marker** ‚Äî six-phase orchestrator in `pyde-engine-node::genesis_seed`: (1) validate genesis, (2) first-boot detection via `consensus_store.get_genesis_record` (`AlreadyInitialised` no-op on matching chain identity; `IdentityMismatch` refusal on divergent), (3) prefund (each `GenesisAccount` becomes an `Account { balance, auth_keys }` in `AccountStore`; `AuthKeys::Programmable` rejected per the v2-reserved tag), (4) treasury (`bootstrap_treasury` seeds the account at `treasury_address()` + `multisig::bootstrap_state` installs signers + threshold at the multisig system slots), (5) committee (per member: create / load operator account funded with `stake_quanta` ‚Üí `bootstrap_validator` locks the stake + writes `ValidatorRecord` to `VALIDATOR_REGISTRY` + appends to `OPERATOR_VALIDATORS`), (6) optional airdrop (`bootstrap_airdrop` seeds pool + the three system slots). `GenesisRecord` (in new `CF_GENESIS` column family at `GENESIS_RECORD_KEY`) carries `chain_identity_blake3` + denormalised chain_id + chain_name + `seeded_at_unix` + `seed_wave_id` + canonical bytes ‚Äî written LAST so absence on next boot is the "redo seeding" signal. Cross-DB atomicity is honest: state_store + consensus_store are separate RocksDB instances, so the full sequence isn't one transaction (same constraint the wave-commit invariant lives under); `GenesisRecord` being the last write makes partial-seed crashes converge to a full re-seed on the next attempt. Idempotent against re-runs because every step is last-write-wins per key/address. 9 unit tests cover end-to-end seed, no-op restart, identity mismatch, invalid genesis early-reject, programmable-authkeys rejection, validator registry shape, airdrop seeded / skipped, treasury credited. ‚Äî PR [#237](https://github.com/pyde-net/engine/pull/237)
- [x] **`pyde validator --genesis <path>` genesis-gate wired into boot** ‚Äî `run_validator_with_hooks` gains a phase-1a-pre gate between runtime build and the pre-run hook. Behaviour matrix: `skip_genesis_gate=true` ‚Üí devnet bypass; `Some(path) + no record` ‚Üí load + validate + seed; `Some(path) + matching record` ‚Üí log "already initialised" no-op; `Some(path) + mismatched record` ‚Üí `GenesisSeed(IdentityMismatch)` abort; `None + record present` ‚Üí log identity + proceed (restart of seeded chain); `None + no record` ‚Üí `FreshChainWithoutGenesis` abort. `ValidatorRunConfig` gains `genesis_path: Option<PathBuf>` + `skip_genesis_gate: bool` (devnet sets `true`, CLI default `false`). New `ValidatorRunError` variants: `GenesisLoad`, `GenesisSeed`, `FreshChainWithoutGenesis { data_dir }`. CLI surfaces a `--genesis <PATH>` flag on `pyde validator` with full doc. 4 integration tests cover refuse-fresh-no-genesis, fresh-with-genesis-seeds, restart-matching-genesis-no-op, restart-mismatched-genesis-refuses. All 14 pre-existing validator tests get `skip_genesis_gate=true` (gate isn't what those tests exercise). ‚Äî PR [#238](https://github.com/pyde-net/engine/pull/238)
- [x] **Cold-restart recovery walker + production wire-up** ‚Äî three-PR slice closing the kill-9 story. **PR [#240](https://github.com/pyde-net/engine/pull/240)** ships the pure orchestrator `recovery_walker::walk_chain_log(state_store, consensus_store, executor) ‚Üí Result<RecoveryReport, RecoveryError>`: loops `(state_high, log_high]`, for each wave reads the `WaveCommitRecord`, fetches every `Tx` from `consensus_store.txs_cf`, delegates execution to a caller-supplied `WaveExecutor` closure, verifies the produced state_root matches the recorded one byte-for-byte, runs a trailing `flush_once_up_to(log_high)`. 6 failure-mode variants (`StateAheadOfLog`, `MissingWaveRecord`, `MissingTx`, `ExecutorFailed`, `StateRootMismatch`, `ConsensusStore`/`StateFlush` pass-through). 7 unit tests including the canonical kill-9 reproduction. **PR [#241](https://github.com/pyde-net/engine/pull/241)** wires the walker into the validator boot via `ValidatorRecoveryHook = Box<dyn FnOnce(&ValidatorRuntime) -> Result<RecoveryReport, String> + Send>` + `run_validator_with_hooks(config, pre_run_hook, recovery_hook, shutdown)`. `ValidatorRunConfig.refuse_on_recovery_gap: bool` controls the no-hook path: state lags log + no hook + flag set ‚Üí `RecoveryGapUnhandled { state, log }` refusal; flag unset (devnet) ‚Üí log warning + proceed. **PR [#245](https://github.com/pyde-net/engine/pull/245)** ships the production wire-up ‚Äî `recovery_executor::devnet_recovery_hook()` factory + `DevnetWaveExecutor` adapter, wired into both devnet entry points so every `pyde devnet` boot installs the recovery hook. ‚Äî PRs [#240](https://github.com/pyde-net/engine/pull/240), [#241](https://github.com/pyde-net/engine/pull/241), [#245](https://github.com/pyde-net/engine/pull/245)
- [x] **State_root semantics + recovery proof ‚Äî JMT-authoritative + kill-9 test green** ‚Äî three-PR slice that aligns devnet state_root with the recovery walker's strict check. **PR [#242](https://github.com/pyde-net/engine/pull/242)** ships `StateCommitter::peek_root(version)` + `StateStore::peek_root(wave_id)`: read-only JMT root lookup via `jmt::JellyfishMerkleTree::get_root_hash_option` through the cache-aware reader, returns the all-zero `EMPTY_TREE_ROOT` sentinel when no root node exists at the version. 4 tests pin the contract (deterministic + idempotent on empty store, matches `commit.state_root` byte-for-byte after a real commit, zero side effects on cache + queue, cache-aware reader sees unflushed-wave writes). **PR [#243](https://github.com/pyde-net/engine/pull/243)** replaces `DevnetState::recompute_state_root` (a lossy Blake3-over-touched-accounts shortcut that ignored slot writes + auth_keys + code_hash + storage_root + system slots) with `StateStore::peek_root` output ‚Äî `WaveCommitInputs.state_root.blake3` is now the authoritative JMT root. `Inner.touched_addresses` + `Inner.state_root` fields deleted; 8 `touched_addresses.insert` call sites removed; three `apply_*` functions lose the now-unused `inner: &mut Inner` parameter. **PR [#244](https://github.com/pyde-net/engine/pull/244)** ships `DevnetWaveExecutor { state: Arc<DevnetState> }` impl `WaveExecutor` that delegates re-execution to a shared `DevnetState` + the canonical kill-9 integration test: commits 5 waves through the production per-wave flush pattern, simulates crash by dropping all in-memory state with only waves 1+2 flushed, reopens both stores fresh, builds a new `DevnetState` + `DevnetWaveExecutor`, runs `walk_chain_log` ‚Üí 3 waves replayed, state catches up to 5, recipient balance reflects all 5 transfers (5000 quanta) ‚Äî recovery rebuilt the in-memory account state byte-perfectly through the walker. ‚Äî PRs [#242](https://github.com/pyde-net/engine/pull/242), [#243](https://github.com/pyde-net/engine/pull/243), [#244](https://github.com/pyde-net/engine/pull/244)

**Config + CLI**
- [ ] `node.toml`: `data_dir`, `chain_id`, `validator_keypair_path`, `rpc.bind_addr`, `p2p.bind_addr`, `p2p.peers[]`, `mempool.max_size`, `mempool.rate_per_sec`, `cache.max_modules`, `cache.ttl_secs` *(v1 surfaces these via the per-subcommand CLI flags; consolidated TOML config is a v2 ergonomics PR)*
- [x] **`pyde validator [--keypair PATH] [--falcon-keypair PATH] [--consensus-store-path DIR] [--genesis PATH] [--listen MA] [--dial MA] [--bootnodes PATH] [--rpc-listen ADDR] [--producer-tick-ms MS] [--producer-quorum N] [--committer-tick-ms MS] [--validator-id N] [--enable-mdns] [--dispute-window-epochs N] [--falcon-beacon] [--beacon-keypair PATH] [--genesis-committee PATH]`** ‚Äî full validator role: consensus participation (vertex producer + wave committer), libp2p + RPC, real FALCON beacon scheme (or `MockBeaconScheme` for solo/devnet), recovery hook + genesis gate wired through. ‚Äî PRs [#236](https://github.com/pyde-net/engine/pull/236) (genesis CLI) + [#238](https://github.com/pyde-net/engine/pull/238) (genesis-gate boot wiring) + earlier validator-binary scaffolding.
- [x] **`pyde full --keypair PATH --consensus-store-path DIR [--genesis PATH] [--listen MA] [--dial MA] [--bootnodes PATH] [--rpc-listen ADDR] [--enable-mdns] [--dispute-window-epochs N]`** ‚Äî read-only full node: same network + state + RPC as `pyde validator` but with consensus participation off (`producer_tick_ms = None`, `committer_tick_ms = None`). FALCON keypair generated ephemerally in /tmp and never used for signing because both producer + committer are off. Use case: explorers / indexers / RPC providers / bridge relayers that observe the chain without staking, without a committee slot, without operational FALCON key management. Boot smoke against the release binary: state store opens cleanly, genesis seeds chain on first boot, libp2p binds, RPC server listening. ‚Äî PR [#248](https://github.com/pyde-net/engine/pull/248)
- [x] **`pyde light [--rpc-listen ADDR]` ‚Äî v1 stub pointing at MC-3** ‚Äî light-client mode requires the MC-3 snapshot pipeline + weak-subjectivity checkpoints + state-sync RPC (see [STATE_SYNC](./companion/STATE_SYNC.md)). v1 ships a stub: invoking prints a helpful message pointing operators at `pyde full` (against a `pyde validator` peer) as the v1 alternative and exits 1. The `--rpc-listen` flag is accepted so post-MC-3 scripts targeting the future light-client RPC surface keep parsing unchanged ‚Äî when MC-3 lands, the implementation drops in without a CLI signature change. ‚Äî PR [#248](https://github.com/pyde-net/engine/pull/248)
- [x] **`pyde genesis init / validate / hash`** ‚Äî see the Bootstrap-sequence row above. ‚Äî PR [#236](https://github.com/pyde-net/engine/pull/236)
- [x] **`pyde keys generate / inspect / export-pubkey`** ‚Äî FALCON-512 validator keypair lifecycle on top of the existing `FalconKeypair` primitives. Enables the off-validator cold workflow: generate on an air-gapped machine, inspect to verify pubkey + derived address, export the public half for a genesis committee, move keypair file to the validator host. `generate --out PATH [--overwrite]` mints + saves (refuses to clobber by default; creates parent dirs); `inspect PATH` prints pubkey hex + EOA address derived via `pyde_engine_account::eoa_address`; `export-pubkey PATH [--format hex|borsh]` produces `0x‚Ä¶<1794 hex chars>` (for genesis.toml committee fields) or raw 897 bytes (for piping to shasum/hex). At-rest encryption is intentionally NOT in this PR ‚Äî v1 stores keypair in plaintext borsh; the encryption story (Argon2id + ChaCha20-Poly1305 or similar) earns its keep as a focused follow-up with its own threat model, not as a side feature. CLI banners the gap so operators know to encrypt at the FS layer (LUKS / FileVault / age) or via HSM until then. 9 unit tests pin the generate / inspect / export round-trip + the address derivation against the canonical eoa_address. ‚Äî PR [#239](https://github.com/pyde-net/engine/pull/239)
- [x] **FALCON validator keypair at-rest encryption** ‚Äî closes the deferral from the keys-lifecycle PR. `pyde keys generate --out PATH --password-stdin` reads a password from stdin (first line, trailing newline stripped) and wraps the borsh-encoded keypair file in an Argon2id (m=64 MiB, t=3, p=4 ‚Äî ~250 ms / attempt on 2024 commodity hardware, multi-second on weaker attacker hardware) + ChaCha20-Poly1305 envelope. `pyde validator --falcon-password-stdin` boots from the encrypted file via `FalconKeypair::load_from_encrypted`. A 15-byte `PYDE_KP_ENC_V1\n` magic header lets `load_from` detect encrypted-vs-plaintext without parsing ‚Äî encrypted files surface a typed `Encrypted` error from the plaintext loader, plaintext files surface a typed `NotEncrypted` from the encrypted loader; no silent fallback. KDF parameters live in the per-file header so defaults can be re-tuned later without rejecting files written by this build. Backward-compat preserved end-to-end: existing plaintext data_dirs keep booting without re-encryption. Threat model in scope: stolen disk / lost laptop / leaked backup / git-committed keypair / cold-boot on long-stopped machines; HSM integration remains the v2 path for production-grade key custody. 13 new unit tests pin the encryption round-trip, magic header, per-file salt freshness, bad-password rejection, cross-format refusals, and `pyde keys generate`'s encrypted-write path; 3 CLI parse-time tests on the new flags. ‚Äî PR [#251](https://github.com/pyde-net/engine/pull/251)
- [x] **Dedup the devnet + validator RPC dispatchers** ‚Äî collapses two near-identical dispatchers (the devnet-side `DevnetRpcContext` + `bind_devnet_rpc_server` and the validator-side `RpcContext` + `bind_rpc_server`) onto the single production dispatcher. Lifts the five devnet-only handlers (`pyde_getTransactionReceipt`, `pyde_call`, `pyde_getEvents`, `pyde_getStorageSlot`, `pyde_getLogs`) into the production `call_method` arm; retires the devnet RPC module entirely; reroutes the devnet pre-run hook to build an `RpcContext` from the runtime + call `bind_rpc_server`. Net **-1583 / +664** ‚Äî one context, one dispatcher, one handler set. Devnet now also serves `pyde_getNodeInfo` (real peer_id + FALCON pubkey from the runtime; empty listen_addrs since solo flow doesn't bind libp2p) + `pyde_getMetrics` (fresh default `MainLoopMetrics` because the pre-run hook fires before mainloop spawn ‚Äî devnet operators see zero counters, honest for the flow). 9 lifted-handler smoke tests pin the new arms at the router layer; live release-binary smoke against `pyde devnet --rpc-listen` confirms every lifted method returns canonical results. ‚Äî PR [#252](https://github.com/pyde-net/engine/pull/252)
- [x] **`pyde_subscribeLogs` push channel over WebSocket** ‚Äî closes the "Event subscription" open line. `GET /ws` upgrades to a JSON-RPC 2.0 WebSocket session that handles `pyde_subscribe(["logs", LogFilter])` ‚Üí hex subscription id, sends `pyde_subscription` push frames on matching just-committed events, and `pyde_unsubscribe([id])` ‚Üí bool. Every other catalog method (`pyde_chainId`, `pyde_call`, ‚Ä¶) falls through to the shared dispatcher so a single persistent WS connection covers polling + streaming consumers without protocol drift. `LogFilter` is the same shape `pyde_getLogs` consumes; `LogFilter::matches` is now the single shared matcher both surfaces route through, no behaviour drift between polling + streaming. Production discipline: bounded per-subscription channels (depth 256) with drop-on-full + slow-consumer telemetry, auto-prune of subscriptions whose receivers were dropped without an explicit unsubscribe, per-connection cleanup on close (clean or abrupt), single-mutex registry with no lock held across `try_send`. The `SubscriptionRegistry` lives on `ValidatorRuntime` so the wave-committer broadcast hook and the RPC server share one `Arc`. 16 module unit tests on the registry + matcher; 6 WebSocket end-to-end tests against a real tokio-tungstenite client through a real `bind_rpc_server` (subscribe round-trip, contract filter, position-sensitive topic filter, multiple subs per connection, connection-close drops every sub, param validation). ‚Äî PR [#253](https://github.com/pyde-net/engine/pull/253)
- [x] **Abort on durable `put_wave` failure instead of advancing past it** ‚Äî hardens the cross-DB log-then-flush invariant from PR [#235](https://github.com/pyde-net/engine/pull/235). The wave-committer previously bucketed every `CommitError` from `commit_one_wave_with_anchor` the same way: log a warn, bump `next_anchor_round`, continue. Correct for assemble-side failures (overflow, malformed vertex shape ‚Äî the in-memory state cache was never mutated) but unsound for `consensus_store.put_wave`: phase 1 (`commit_walked_subdag`) has already landed the wave's transfer / fee / slot effects in the state cache; if phase 2's durable log write then fails, the chain log carries no record while state-side memory believes the wave landed, and the next commit would build on a corrupted base the recovery walker can't reconstruct from. Single-site fix at the `put_wave` call site: replace the `?` with an explicit `Err` arm that `panic!`s naming the wave id, the underlying error, and the operator-facing remediation (restart triggers the recovery walker). Workspace `panic = "abort"` release profile turns this into a clean SIGABRT in production; tests under `panic = "unwind"` `catch_unwind` the message. Caller comment updates to note store-IO no longer reaches the recoverable branch. `#[cfg(test)]` `ConsensusStore::force_put_wave_failure()` hook flips an atomic flag that makes the next `put_wave` return Err without touching disk ‚Äî production code never sets it. Dedicated test asserts panic message names the durable-log failure + points at the recovery walker, AND that `next_wave_id` does NOT advance, AND that `waves_cf` has no record of the failed wave. ‚Äî PR [#254](https://github.com/pyde-net/engine/pull/254)
- [x] **`pyde stake` CLI + lifecycle RPC (PR 1 of validator-lifecycle scoping)** ‚Äî opens the operator-facing surface for the existing on-chain handlers (`handle_stake_deposit` / `handle_stake_withdraw` / `handle_claim_reward` / `handle_unjail` were already wired; nothing drove them from the validator host). Read RPC: `pyde_getValidator(addr)` ‚Üí full `ValidatorRecord` JSON (validator_address, operator, pubkey, stake, status, unbond_at_wave, jail_until_wave, last_claimed_rps, uptime_bps) or `null`; `pyde_getOperatorValidators(addr)` ‚Üí hex array of an operator's validator addresses. CLI: `pyde stake` parent + five sub-actions ‚Äî `status` (read-only query, derives address from `--falcon-keypair` when `--address` omitted), `register` (StakeDeposit 0x03 with `data = falcon_pubkey`, value = `--amount`), `unbond` (StakeWithdraw 0x04), `claim` (ClaimReward 0x06; lazily transitions Unbonding ‚Üí Exited after the unbond period), `unjail` (Unjail 0x0E). Every signed op shares the envelope: load FALCON keypair (supports `--falcon-password-stdin` for encrypted files), derive `validator_address = eoa_address(pubkey)`, query nonce via `pyde_getTransactionCount`, build `Tx`, hash via `pyde_engine_tx::tx_hash`, sign with FALCON, borsh + hex + submit via `pyde_sendRawTransaction`. Typed `StakeCliError` variants; no silent fallbacks. 11 new tests (4 stake_cli unit + 4 CLI parse + 3 RPC handler). Live release-binary smoke against `pyde devnet --rpc-listen`: `pyde stake status --rpc <URL> --address 0xdead‚Ä¶` correctly returns `(not a validator)` end-to-end. **Deferred to follow-up PRs:** `TxType::RotateValidatorKeys` + handler + CLI rotate; `MAX_VALIDATORS_PER_OPERATOR = 5` cap enforcement; `PENDING ACTIVATION` 1-epoch bonding period; jail escalation (1st = 24h / 2nd = 7d / 3rd = permanent); end-to-end lifecycle integration test against a running chain. ‚Äî PR [#255](https://github.com/pyde-net/engine/pull/255)
- [x] **`TxType::RotateValidatorKeys` + handler + `pyde stake rotate` CLI (PR 2 of validator-lifecycle scoping)** ‚Äî closes the deferred FALCON-key rotation from PR #255. New wire-frozen tx variant `0x0F` with the envelope shape `from = validator_address, to = ZERO, value = 0, data = new 897-byte FALCON pubkey, signed by the OLD key currently in account.auth_keys`. Tag added to canonical hashing (`tx_type_tag`), per-type shape validation (897-byte data via the shared `StakeDepositDataLen` arm), borsh wire test. `handle_rotate_validator_keys` in `pyde_engine_tx::handlers::staking` + dispatch in `wasm_exec::executor_impl`. Pipeline: structural checks ‚Üí load `ValidatorRecord` at `tx.from` ‚Üí require `Status::Active` (Unbonding/Exited/Jailed reject ‚Äî those states have higher-priority lifecycle work first; jailed must `Unjail` before rotating) ‚Üí reject no-op rotation to the same pubkey loudly so operators don't burn gas ‚Üí verify sig vs OLD `auth_keys` ‚Üí nonce + gas checks ‚Üí charge gas, commit nonce, set `record.pubkey = new_pubkey` AND `account.auth_keys = AuthKeys::Single(new_pubkey)` ‚Üí commit. `validator_address` stays the same ‚Äî rotation is a key swap, not an identity change; stake / operator binding / jail history all stay attached.
