CLI: `pyde stake rotate --rpc <URL> --falcon-keypair <OLD.kp> --new-falcon-keypair <NEW.kp> --chain-id <ID>` (each keypair can be plaintext or encrypted; passwords on stdin in order ‚Äî old then new). Prints a follow-up reminder that subsequent `pyde stake` calls MUST use the new keypair file. 10 new tests including the critical correctness check that after rotation the OLD key gets rejected (`BadSignature`) and the NEW key authorises further txs. **`KEY_ROTATION_INTERVAL = 1/epoch` rate limit deferred** to a follow-up PR (requires `last_rotation_wave` schema bump); no new attack vector opens since the OLD key already authorises rotation, so the rate limit is anti-griefing only. ‚Äî PR [#256](https://github.com/pyde-net/engine/pull/256)
- [x] **Free operator slot when validator exits (PR 3 of validator-lifecycle scoping)** ‚Äî closes a latent lifetime-vs-concurrent cap bug. `OPERATOR_CAP = 3` was correctly enforced at `handle_stake_deposit` / `bootstrap_validator` against `operator_validators_slot`, but nothing pruned that list when a validator transitioned to `Exited`. The cap effectively became "lifetime" instead of "concurrent": an operator who exited all three of their validators could never register a replacement, even though their concurrent footprint was zero. Per `staking-model-correction.md` and the lifecycle spec's `[WITHDRAWABLE]` state ("Returns to NOT REGISTERED, frees operator slot"), the cap is meant to be concurrent (Active + Unbonding + Jailed) ‚Äî exited validators must release their slot. Single-site fix in `handle_claim_reward`'s exit branch: when `should_exit = true`, read the operator's list, drop the exiting validator's address, and commit the new list alongside the validator record. The on-chain `ValidatorRecord` at `validator_registry_slot(addr)` stays as historical archive ‚Äî only the index that the cap reads from gets pruned. Tightened the `OPERATOR_CAP` doc to call out concurrent semantics explicitly so future contributors don't reintroduce the lifetime interpretation. 3 new tests including the headline correctness property: fill the cap, prove CAP+1 registration rejects, exit one via unbond + claim past window, prove that exact CAP+1 registration NOW succeeds. 57/57 staking tests + node-side regression (54 rpc + 4 stake_cli + 55 cli) green. **Slash-forced exit deferred**: when stake drops below `MIN_VALIDATOR_STAKE` via slashing ‚Üí forced unbond ‚Üí eventual Exit, the same removal hook needs to fire; tracked as a follow-up because the involuntary path goes through different state-machine transitions. ‚Äî PR [#257](https://github.com/pyde-net/engine/pull/257)
- [x] **Wire liveness slash submission end-to-end (mainnet-critical)** ‚Äî closes a real chain-security gap. Before this PR, `handle_slash` REJECTED all liveness evidence with `SlashOffenseClassMismatch`: `ExtendedDowntime`, `DkgParticipationFailure`, `DecryptionShareWithholding`, `BadBatchAttestation` were detected in-memory only. Absent validators faced zero on-chain consequence; the committee-security argument that misbehavior is economically punished was broken for every liveness offense. **Wire format**: new `SlashEvidence::Liveness(LivenessEvidence) = 0x03` variant ‚Äî tag was already reserved in the wire doc, now populated and borsh-frozen by a dedicated test. `LivenessEvidence` is `{offense, offender (Address), epoch}` with no cryptographic payload (the chain is the witness). **Handler pipeline**: `handle_slash` now decodes 3 variants; the Liveness path verifies offense class + validator existence + non-Exited status, then applies the slash via the shared `OffenseSpec`-driven path (stake reduction + jail; all liveness offenses use `Distribution::ALL_BURN` so reporter + treasury shares evaluate to 0). **The critical correctness primitive** ‚Äî new `SLASHED_LIVENESS_OFFENSES = 0x22` system slot keyed on `(epoch, accused, offense_tag)`. Liveness evidence is permissionlessly forgeable (any validator can build it); without dedup, N committee members detecting the same liveness event would over-slash by Nx. `handle_slash` reads the slot before applying, rejects with `LivenessOffenseAlreadySlashed` if a marker exists, writes the marker on success ‚Üí **first-tx-wins, identical resubmissions short-circuit cleanly**. New `offense_wire_tag` mapping (Equivocation 0x01 ‚Üí BadBatchAttestation 0x09) provides the stable per-offense discriminator; wire-frozen by test. **Submitter + consumer wiring**: `SlashSubmitter::submit_liveness_slash(offense, accused_member_id, epoch)` bridges detection ‚Üí on-chain; `ExtendedDowntimeConsumer::with_slash_submitter(submitter)` installs the bridge (consumer's dispatch becomes async, auto-submits after every successful in-memory record). `validator.rs` wires the submitter alongside the safety consumers. 11 new tests including the on-chain dedup correctness property (2nd identical submission gets `LivenessOffenseAlreadySlashed`, stake stays at first-slash level) + 2 SlashSubmitter chain-verifiability tests. 60+ tests across slash/submitter/consumer suites green; validator + safety-consumer regression clean. **Deferred follow-ups**: liveness DETECTION upstream (consensus-layer hook feeding DowntimeAccumulator), `DkgParticipationFailure` / `DecryptionShareWithholding` / `BadBatchAttestation` submission consumers (handler accepts all 4, only ExtendedDowntime has the consumer wired today; symmetric path ‚Üí each follow-up is just-add-consumer), escrow ‚Üí on-chain dispute window for governance VOID/REDUCE. ‚Äî PR [#258](https://github.com/pyde-net/engine/pull/258)
- [x] **Thread real epoch into downtime detector** ‚Äî closes a latent bug PR #258 created. The on-chain dedup gate (`slashed_liveness_offense_slot`) keys on `(epoch, accused, offense)`; the `DowntimeDetector` tagged every emission with `epoch: 0` (v1 stub), so once an `ExtendedDowntime` slash for a given validator landed on chain, the dedup gate blocked every subsequent submission for that validator across the entire process lifetime ‚Äî a validator could be slashed for downtime at most ONCE. Fix: shared `Arc<AtomicU64>` between the wave-committer (writer) and the downtime detector (reader). After every successful wave commit, the committer `store`s the just-committed wave's `epoch_for_wave(wave_id, epoch_length)` into the shared Arc with `Ordering::Release`. The detector `load`s with `Ordering::Acquire` on every scan tick + tags emissions with that epoch ‚Äî Acquire/Release pair guarantees a tick observing the new epoch sees a fully-committed wave at that boundary. The detector snapshots the epoch ONCE per scan pass so all rounds in the same pass bucket under the same epoch (avoids racing an epoch advance mid-scan, which would split a single pass's emissions across epochs and break the per-(epoch, accused, offense) idempotency model). Headline test: first scan at epoch=5 produces emissions tagged epoch=5; bumping the shared Arc to 6 between passes makes the next pass produce emissions tagged epoch=6. Without this thread, the dedup gate would reject every emission past the first. 2 new tests + 78 regression tests green. **Still deferred**: the static-128-member committee in the detector config doesn't shift with epoch boundaries (per-epoch dynamic membership lands with DKG / committee rotation); `DkgParticipationFailure` / `DecryptionShareWithholding` / `BadBatchAttestation` submission consumers ‚Äî handler accepts them but no detector emits. ‚Äî PR [#259](https://github.com/pyde-net/engine/pull/259)
- [x] **On-chain escrow dispute window for slashes (mainnet-critical)** ‚Äî closes the deferred 24h dispute path PR #258 called out. Before this PR, `handle_slash` was a foregone conclusion: evidence in ‚Üí stake reduced + reporter paid in the same transaction. A false-positive detector, a malicious coordinator forging structural evidence, or a transient network anomaly looking like equivocation knocked a validator out with zero recourse. **Split-transition design**: `handle_slash` now applies status + jail INSTANTLY (a confirmed equivocator gets removed from active duty immediately) but defers the stake reduction + reporter/treasury credit by 8 epochs (‚âà24h). The pending entry lives at a new PIP-2 slot `slashed_pending_slot(escrow_id)` keyed on a server-local autoincrement id, indexed via `slashed_pending_index_slot` for O(active-disputes) scan. Reporter is not yet credited; stake stays at pre-slash level. **New `TxType::DisputeSlash = 0x10`**: treasury multisig signs `canonical_msg(DisputeSlash, nonce, Poseidon2(borsh((escrow_id, action))))` and either VOIDs the entry (skip stake reduction; instant-jail stays in force as the spec intends ‚Äî the bad actor is already sidelined) or REDUCEs the bps (lower the magnitude; new_bps must be strictly less than the prior bps ‚Äî never escalation). Rejects entries that are `Applied` or `Voided`, post-maturity disputes, and below-threshold bundles. Domain-byte mapping + envelope-style validation + per-type shape rules wired alongside the existing multisig family. **Maturity scan**: `process_matured_escrows` runs in the wave-committer post-commit. Empty index pays one slot read (the common case at v1 traffic levels). At maturity: `Pending`/`Reduced` ‚Üí reduce stake, credit reporter + treasury, mark `Applied`, drop from index; `Voided` ‚Üí stake untouched, status stays `Voided` permanently as audit; validator-vanished ‚Üí promoted to `Applied` (no stake to reduce). The semantic fix matters: before this PR, the maturity scan over-wrote `Voided ‚Üí Applied` and lost the dispute decision; now the audit trail is preserved. **Dedup interaction with PR #258**: the `(epoch, accused, offense)` gate sets at enqueue time and stays set across the dispute outcome ‚Äî a Voided slash doesn't re-open the gate (governance has decided "this evidence doesn't count," and re-submission would just re-litigate). 9 new dispute-handler tests + 27 slash-handler tests rewritten to drive the new deferred semantics. 271 tx-lib tests + 279 wasm-exec + 509 node-lib all green; workspace check + clippy clean. **Out of scope**: SafetyEvidence's existing per-tx semantics stay identical at the handler level ‚Äî only the stake-reduction timing shifted; bundle-format expansion to allow REDUCE of safety vs liveness offenses with different reasoning paths can land as a v2 hardening. ‚Äî PR [#260](https://github.com/pyde-net/engine/pull/260)
- [x] **Devnet RPC server honors validator shutdown watch** ‚Äî closes a 5-test wedge in `runner::tests::*via_live_json_rpc`. The devnet prefund hook bound its own JSON-RPC server with a hook-private `ctrl_c`-based graceful-shutdown handler. That worked for the `pyde devnet` binary path (operator presses ctrl+c, hook flips its own `shutdown_tx`, server drains) but tests drive shutdown via the operator-supplied future and never deliver SIGINT, so the hook RPC server stayed alive holding a clone of `runtime.network_handle`. That clone kept the network runner's command channel open, so the validator's post-shutdown `network_task.await` blocked forever and the test process burned 40+ CPU seconds before hitting a `cargo test` timeout. The fix: extend the `ValidatorPreRunHook` signature to take a clone of the validator's own `shutdown_rx` watch, construct that watch channel earlier in `run_validator_with_hooks` so it's available before the hook fires, drop the in-hook ctrl_c spawn, and route the devnet RPC server's `with_graceful_shutdown` through the shared watch. Production semantics are unchanged: outer caller (`run_validator_until_ctrl_c`) handles SIGINT ‚Üí flips `shutdown_tx` ‚Üí axum sees the watch fire ‚Üí drains. Five previously-wedged tests now finish in ~6s combined; the full node-lib sweep is 514 passed without needing `--skip via_live_json_rpc`. ‚Äî PR [#262](https://github.com/pyde-net/engine/pull/262)
- [x] **Slash-forced exit when stake falls below `MIN_VALIDATOR_STAKE` (mainnet-critical)** ‚Äî closes a chain-security hole PR #257 deferred. Before this PR, when `process_matured_escrows` reduced a validator's stake below `MIN_VALIDATOR_STAKE` via slashing, NOTHING fired: the record sat at `Status::Jailed` with sub-minimum stake forever, holding an operator-cap slot, blocking the operator from registering a replacement. The concurrent-cap semantics from PR #257 (slot is `Active + Unbonding + Jailed`, not lifetime) effectively reverted to lifetime for every slash-driven sub-minimum validator ‚Äî a real economic-security gap that became more pressing once PR #260 made the maturity scan the authoritative apply path. **Fix in the maturity scan**: after computing `post_slash_stake = record.stake - actual_slash`, if it dropped below `MIN_VALIDATOR_STAKE` AND status isn't already `Exited`, force the auto-exit: set `record.stake = 0` + `record.status = Status::Exited`; credit the residual (`post_slash_stake`) back to the operator's account (same semantics as `handle_claim_reward`'s voluntary-exit branch ‚Äî the operator put up the bond, slashing takes its share, the rest returns); prune the operator's slot list at `operator_validators_slot` so they can immediately register a replacement; bump a new `EscrowMaturityResult.force_exited` counter for wave-committer logging. **Edge cases**: above-min stake post-slash leaves validator `Jailed` (no auto-exit) ‚Äî they can still `Unjail` once jail elapses; exact-MIN boundary (`post_slash_stake >= MIN_VALIDATOR_STAKE`) doesn't trigger; no-reporter slashes still credit operator residual; the validator-vanished branch unchanged; Voided / Reduced dispute outcomes interact correctly (Reduced uses the new bps, Voided skips the maturity stake reduction entirely). **Test ergonomics fix-up**: existing slash + dispute_slash tests that asserted per-bps stake math used MIN-stake deposits, which now trip the forced-exit path and zero-out the record before the math is observable. Added a `setup_active_validator_with_stake(stake)` helper across both test modules; pre-existing tests adapted to deposit 10√ó MIN so the assertions still measure what they were designed to measure (per-bps math) while the forced-exit-specific tests use MIN-stake deposits. 4 new headline tests: forced-exit + slot-freeing correctness, above-MIN no-auto-exit negative control, MIN-boundary preservation, no-reporter forced-exit residual credit. 275 tx-lib + 279 wasm-exec + 514 node-lib tests passing; workspace check + clippy clean. **Future**: emit a dedicated event log line on forced-exit so operators / monitoring can react (tracked separately; not blocking). ‚Äî PR [#263](https://github.com/pyde-net/engine/pull/263)
- [x] **DKG ceremony attestation gossip layer (testnet-critical)** ‚Äî opens the DKG ceremony surface area for the per-epoch committee rotation. PR #258 wired `handle_slash` to accept `DkgParticipationFailure` evidence but nothing emits it because no participation witness exists on chain; without DKG running, committee rotation at epoch boundaries can't happen and the chain is stuck on the genesis committee forever. **The architecture decision that mattered**: not Solana's votes-as-tx anti-pattern. Pyde's `BeaconShare` path (gossip ‚Üí per-epoch in-memory buffer ‚Üí wave-committer aggregation at epoch-boundary commits) is the precedent for validator-committee consensus messages; DKG attestations follow the same shape. Going tx-based would have charged validators gas for required protocol duty, polluted the receipt index with consensus noise, and put protocol-critical messages in competition with user txs for mempool slots ‚Äî the early scope I drafted that way was reverted before commit. **What ships**: `consensus::DkgAttestation { epoch, round, member_id, payload_digest, signature }` wire-frozen borsh struct (`DKG_ROUND_COUNT = 3` rounds, `payload_digest` is 32-byte commitment to the round's off-chain protocol artifact ‚Äî Pedersen commitment for Round 1, encrypted-share manifest for Round 2, verification proof for Round 3); `dkg_attestation_pre_image` canonical bytes carry a `pyde/dkg-attestation/v1` domain tag against cross-protocol sig replay. `net::topics::DKG_ATTESTATIONS = "pyde/dkg-attestations/1"` slots into the topic table between BEACON_SHARES and STATE_ROOT_SIGS. `node::DkgAttestationBuffer` mirrors `BeaconShareBuffer`'s parking_lot RwLock<HashMap<Epoch, HashMap<(member_id, round), DkgAttestation>>> shape with full insert/dedup/count/get/prune/clear API. `node::mainloop` dispatch gains a `pyde/dkg-attestations/1` route + `handle_dkg_attestation` function with full metrics (received / buffered / duplicates / decode_failures). `tx::system_slots::DKG_ATTESTATION = 0x26` discriminator + `dkg_attestation_slot(epoch, member_id, round)` helper land for the future wave-committer epoch-boundary snapshot to chain state ‚Äî the persistence-target slot family is in code now even though the snapshot wire-up is a separate follow-up. **Out of scope (each a clean follow-up)**: validator-side EMIT path (producer broadcasts after each ceremony round), sig verification on receive (needs live CommitteeRegistry ‚Äî same blocker as beacon-share verify), committee-membership filtering (same blocker), wave-committer snapshot to chain state at epoch boundaries, `DkgParticipationFailure` detector that reads the snapshot at end-of-round deadlines + emits slashes for missing members. 29 new tests (5 in `consensus::dkg_attestation` + 11 in `node::dkg_attestation_buffer` + 4 mainloop dispatch + 1 net topics pin); 1440 tests across consensus / net / node / tx / wasm-exec all green. ‚Äî PR [#264](https://github.com/pyde-net/engine/pull/264)
- [x] **Validator-side DKG attestation emit hook (testnet-critical)** ‚Äî closes the producer half of the gossip layer shipped in #264. On each commit that crosses into a new target epoch (`committed_epoch + 1`), the wave-committer fires a fresh round-set (`DKG_ROUND_COUNT = 3` attestations) FALCON-signed by the validator's keypair, buffers them locally so the validator's own work counts toward its tally, and publishes them on `pyde/dkg-attestations/1` fire-and-forget. Mirrors the existing beacon-share emit pattern; idempotent within an epoch via a new `DkgEmitterState` carried inside `WaveCommitter`. **The v1 honest stub**: the actual cryptographic DKG protocol payload (Pedersen polynomial commitments, encrypted-share envelopes, complaint resolution proofs) is owned by `pyde-crypto` and hasn't shipped, so `payload_digest` is a deterministic placeholder derived from `Blake3("pyde/dkg-attestation/v1-stub" || epoch || round || member_id || beacon_pubkey)`. **The signature path is real** ‚Äî every attestation is FALCON-signed over the canonical `dkg_attestation_pre_image` (the `pyde/dkg-attestation/v1`-domain-tagged preimage from #264) by the validator's signing keypair. When `pyde-crypto` integrates, the stub digest swaps for a Blake3 hash of the actual protocol artifact; the gossip plumbing doesn't change. **NetworkView surface**: gains `publish_dkg_attestation(payload)`; production `NetworkHandle` routes to `topics::DKG_ATTESTATIONS`; `MockNetwork` records published payloads (`published_dkg_attestation_count` + `published_dkg_attestations()` snapshot); the two test doubles in `vertex_producer.rs` (`RecordingNetwork` / `FailingNetwork`) get matching ok / fail impls. **Module**: new `crates/node/src/dkg_emitter.rs` with `emit_round_set_for_epoch(state, epoch, member_id, keypair, buffer, network, metrics)` ‚Äî local buffer insert before publish mirrors the beacon-share discipline so a solo validator's own attestations are visible in its own tally. Fire-and-forget publish; metrics track emit success vs publish failure. **WaveCommitter wiring**: new `dkg_attestation_buffer: Arc<DkgAttestationBuffer>` field + `dkg_emitter_state: parking_lot::Mutex<DkgEmitterState>` field + `with_dkg_attestation_buffer(buffer)` builder so the validator threads the mainloop's canonical buffer through (without it the committer holds an orphan buffer + the validator's own emits miss the future snapshot path). `maybe_emit_dkg_attestations_for_next_epoch(committed_wave)` helper called in `commit_one_wave_with_anchor` adjacent to the share-emit hook. **MainLoopMetrics**: `dkg_attestations_emitted` + `dkg_attestation_publish_failures` counters + reader methods. **validator.rs**: grabs the mainloop's canonical `DkgAttestationBuffer` via `mainloop.dkg_attestation_buffer()` accessor + threads via the new builder. **Out of scope (clean follow-ups)**: sig + committee-membership verification on receive (needs live CommitteeRegistry ‚Äî same blocker as beacon-share verify); wave-committer snapshot of buffer ‚Üí on-chain slot family at epoch boundaries (slot family already exists in #264; snapshot wire-up reads from the buffer this PR populates); real cryptographic `payload_digest` (when `pyde-crypto` lands); `DkgParticipationFailure` detector that reads the snapshot at end-of-round deadlines + emits slashes for missing members. 6 new tests in `dkg_emitter::tests` cover happy emit, same-epoch no-op (idempotency), next-epoch fresh emit, skipped-intermediate-epoch advancement, stub digest determinism + variation. 1457 tests across consensus / net / node / tx / wasm-exec / interfaces all green. ‚Äî PR [#265](https://github.com/pyde-net/engine/pull/265)
- [x] **Wave-committer snapshot of DKG attestations to chain state (testnet-critical)** ‚Äî third leg of the DKG ceremony chain (receive #264 ‚Üí emit #265 ‚Üí snapshot). Without it, the future `DkgParticipationFailure` detector has no canonical, durable witness to read ‚Äî the buffer is in-memory only, doesn't survive restarts, isn't visible to validators that joined via state-sync. **Trigger**: on the LAST WAVE of each epoch N, the wave-committer drains the buffer's `target_epoch = N + 1` partition into the on-chain `DKG_ATTESTATION` slot family (the discriminator + helper that PR #264 already shipped). End-of-N is the natural deadline ‚Äî committee N+1's ceremony must be complete before they're expected to decrypt anything at the first wave of N+1; late attestations after the snapshot don't help avoid the slash. **New module** `crates/node/src/dkg_snapshot.rs`: `DkgAttestationRecord { epoch, round, member_id, payload_digest, recorded_at_wave }` borsh-encoded per triple (FALCON sig dropped ‚Äî verified at receive time; persisting it permanently is wasted space); `DkgSnapshotState` idempotency tracker; `snapshot_dkg_attestations_for_epoch(state, target_epoch, buffer, accounts, wave_id)` drains buffer + dedups against existing slots + writes via StateCommitter + prunes buffer; `read_dkg_attestation_record(store, epoch, member_id, round, wave_id)` so the future detector iterates the expected committee √ó rounds set + slashes members whose triple returns None. **Wave-committer wiring**: new `dkg_snapshot_state: parking_lot::Mutex<DkgSnapshotState>` field + `maybe_snapshot_dkg_attestations_for_next_epoch(committed_wave)` helper (no-ops on non-last-wave-of-epoch commits) called from `commit_one_wave_with_anchor`'s post-commit section alongside `process_matured_escrows`. **Idempotency at three levels**: (1) `last_snapshotted_epoch` skips repeat calls at the same target, (2) per-slot dedup at write time (read_slot before push), (3) buffer prune after first successful snapshot. The buffer prune means: on a normal happy path, the second snapshot call finds nothing to do; on a recovery walker replay (state reset to N, walker re-executes waves > N), the buffer is populated again from re-emit + the per-slot dedup makes the re-snapshot a no-op write. No state divergence. 6 new tests in `dkg_snapshot::tests`: empty-buffer no-op + write-prune happy path + same-epoch idempotency + higher-epoch proceeds + already-present skip-and-count + missing-triple read returns None. 541 node-lib + 275 tx-lib + 283 consensus + 279 wasm-exec tests passing. ‚Äî PR [#266](https://github.com/pyde-net/engine/pull/266)
- [x] **DkgParticipationFailure detector closes the DKG slashing loop (testnet-critical)** ‚Äî final leg of the DKG ceremony chain: receive (#264) ‚Üí emit (#265) ‚Üí snapshot (#266) ‚Üí **DETECT + SLASH**. PR #258 wired the `Slash` handler to accept `DkgParticipationFailure` evidence but nothing was emitting it because no on-chain witness existed. With the snapshot persisted at each end-of-epoch boundary (#266), the detector now reads chain state at the start of each new epoch + slashes committee members who failed to publish all 3 ceremony rounds. **How it works**: periodic-tick loop (30s default). On each tick the detector compares the shared `current_epoch` Arc against its own `last_scanned_epoch`. When the epoch advances past the last scan, the detector scans the snapshot for `target_epoch = current_epoch` and slashes any committee member missing at least one round. For each `member_id` in `0..committee_size`, the detector calls `read_dkg_attestation_record` for each round in `0..DKG_ROUND_COUNT`. A missing round flags the member as liable for `DkgParticipationFailure`. The on-chain dedup gate (`SLASHED_LIVENESS_OFFENSES` keyed on `(epoch, accused, offense_tag)`) makes the per-member slash exactly-once: multiple missing rounds ‚Üí first submission wins, subsequent ones short-circuit cleanly. No detector-side dedup needed. **New module** `crates/node/src/dkg_participation_detector.rs`: `DkgParticipationDetectorConfig` carrying tick_interval / committee_size / shared current_epoch / read_wave_sentinel; `MissingMember { member_id, missing_round_count }` return shape from the scan; `DkgParticipationDetector` long-running task with pure `scan_epoch(target_epoch)` + `maybe_scan()` orchestrator; `with_slash_submitter(submitter)` builder mirrors `ExtendedDowntimeConsumer::with_slash_submitter` so the validator can wire on-chain submission. **Wiring**: `validator.rs` spawns the detector task alongside `downtime_consumer_task` (joined on shutdown alongside the other consumers); `MainLoopMetrics` gains three new counters ‚Äî `dkg_participation_failures_detected`, `_slash_tx_submitted`, `_slash_tx_failed` ‚Äî plus the matching reader methods; slash submission goes through the existing `SlashSubmitter::submit_liveness_slash(Offense::DkgParticipationFailure, member_id, epoch)` path PR #258 already wired. **v1 stubs**: `committee_size` from config rather than from a chain-side `CommitteeRegistry` (same shape the downtime detector uses pre-registry); detect-only without a wired SlashSubmitter (test fixtures + dev mode); `read_wave_sentinel = WaveId::MAX` so state reads return the latest persisted record without a separate current-wave tracker. **The DKG ceremony chain is now end-to-end**: validator emits attestation ‚Üí peer receives, buffers ‚Üí wave-committer snapshots to chain at end-of-epoch ‚Üí detector reads chain at start of next epoch ‚Üí slashes missing members ‚Üí on-chain stake reduces via the #258 handler. 6 new tests in `dkg_participation_detector::tests`: complete set ‚Üí 0 missing; member missing all rounds caught; member missing one round caught; no snapshot ‚Üí every member missing; `maybe_scan` advances cursor + skips repeat at same epoch; epoch 0 skipped pre-advance. 547 node-lib + 275 tx-lib + 283 consensus + 279 wasm-exec tests passing. ‚Äî PR [#267](https://github.com/pyde-net/engine/pull/267)
- [x] **SlashSubmitter pulls committee from genesis manifest ‚Äî multi-validator-ready (testnet-critical)** ‚Äî closes a real multi-validator testnet hole. Pre-fix, the `SlashSubmitter`'s `StaticCommitteeLookup` was populated with ONE slot ‚Äî the local validator's own. Every other `member_id` returned `UnknownOffender`. That means in a multi-validator network, NO detector could actually submit a slash for any other validator: the DKG participation detector (#267), equivocation consumer (#147), bad-state-root-sig consumer (#164), extended downtime consumer (#258) were all wired to call `committee.pubkey_for(member_id)` and would silently no-op past `member_id ‚âÝ self`. Every detected offense from a peer would log "submission failed: offender member_id N not in committee lookup" and the chain-side stake reduction never fired. **The fix**: at validator boot, if `--genesis <manifest>` is set, parse the manifest and populate the lookup with EVERY member's FALCON pubkey from `loaded.genesis.committee[i].falcon_pubkey`. **The key correctness property**: the manifest's `falcon_pubkey` field IS the CONSENSUS signing pubkey ‚Äî the same key `bootstrap_validator` installs as `ValidatorRecord.pubkey` + `Account.auth_keys` at chain seeding ‚Äî so `eoa_address(&pubkey)` derives the same address the on-chain `ValidatorRecord` holds. Slashes target the right accounts. **Why the genesis manifest, not the `--genesis-committee` file**: the loose `--genesis-committee` file carries BEACON pubkeys (per the genesis_committee module doc), which can be a separate key from the consensus signing key when an operator uses the `--beacon-keypair` flag. Beacon-pubkey-driven address derivation would target the wrong accounts. The manifest's `falcon_pubkey` is authoritative because it's what `bootstrap_validator` consumes. **Source priority**: (1) `--genesis <manifest.toml>` ‚Üí full N-member committee read from manifest, addresses match on-chain `ValidatorRecord`; (2) Solo fallback (`solo_mode_lookup_members` helper) ‚Üí preserves the pre-fix single-slot behavior so single-validator devnet / smoke tests keep working without a manifest. **Out of scope (clean follow-up)**: per-epoch on-chain committee rotation when the `CommitteeRegistry` persists ‚Äî until then the genesis committee is treated as the committee for every epoch, fine for v1 testnet where committee rotation isn't running yet. 2 new tests on the helper (own slot populated; vec grows when validator_id > committee_size); the manifest-driven path is exercised end-to-end by every existing test that boots with `--genesis`. 549 node-lib tests passing. ‚Äî PR [#268](https://github.com/pyde-net/engine/pull/268)
- [x] **In-process N-validator cluster helper (testnet-critical)** ‚Äî first brick toward a `pyde devnet --validators N` flag. New module `crates/node/src/multi_validator_cluster.rs` exposes `build_cluster(n, base_dir, chain_id, chain_name)` that produces N pre-configured `ValidatorRunConfig`s + writes the supporting keypairs + a shared Genesis manifest. **What `build_cluster` does**: generates N FALCON consensus keypairs + N beacon keypairs + N libp2p Ed25519 keypairs, persists each to per-validator subdirectories under `base_dir`; builds a real `Genesis` manifest with all N as `founding_committee` members (each member's `falcon_pubkey` is the validator's CONSENSUS pubkey so `eoa_address(&pubkey)` matches the on-chain `ValidatorRecord.address` post-seed ‚Äî the SlashSubmitter committee lookup from PR #268 picks it up automatically); pre-funds each validator's address (1 Q PYDE) so they can pay slash-submission gas + receive reporter rewards; writes the manifest TOML to `base_dir/genesis.toml`; returns N `ValidatorRunConfig`s in hub-and-spoke topology (validator 0 listens, 1..N dial validator 0 + also bind so peers can dial back). **Dependency surface change**: `libp2p` promoted from `[dev-dependencies]` to `[dependencies]` because the cluster builder constructs canonical `/p2p/<peer-id>` dial multiaddrs and the `pyde_engine_net::PeerId` shim doesn't expose libp2p's textual base58 encoder. **What this validates end-to-end**: N validators boot in the same tokio runtime sharing a single Genesis manifest without state collisions; each emits at least one vertex through its producer; the genesis-committee ‚Üí SlashSubmitter pipeline works for multi-validator clusters end-to-end. **Out of scope (clean follow-ups)**: cross-validator consensus convergence (the consensus crate's `BEACON_THRESHOLD = 85` and `COMMITTEE_SIZE = 128` are hardcoded constants; small-N clusters can't reach threshold; needs threshold knobs); gossipsub mesh tuning for small N (libp2p's default `mesh_n_low = 4` means clusters below ~6 peers don't form a well-connected mesh under heartbeat dynamics; cross-vertex exchange is best-effort); `pyde devnet --validators N` CLI hookup (builder is in place; wiring is the next PR). 4 new tests: keys + manifest written per validator, genesis committee has N distinct pubkeys + addresses, topology is hub-and-spoke as designed, **`cluster_3_boots_cleanly_under_shared_genesis`** ‚Äî actually spawns 3 validators in-process, lets them run for 3 seconds, asserts each produced ‚â•1 vertex (live multi-validator boot proof). 553 node-lib tests passing. ‚Äî PR [#269](https://github.com/pyde-net/engine/pull/269)
- [x] **BFT-tuned cluster thresholds + live 4-validator gossipsub proof (testnet-critical)** ‚Äî closes the first "out of scope" item from #269. Pre-fix, `build_cluster(n)` produced configs with production constants (`COMMITTEE_SIZE = 128`, `QUORUM = 85`) even for small N. That meant: (a) anchor selection picked slots in `[0, 128)` against a 4-validator live set so most rounds skipped because no validator owned the picked slot; (b) BFT support quorum demanded 85 votes from a 4-member committee, never reachable. The wave-committer ticked forever without making progress. **Fix**: `build_cluster` now sets `committee_size = n` (anchor selection picks `member_id in [0, n)`, every round's pick is in the live set) + `support_quorum = bft_quorum_for(n)` (locked to the spec `2f + 1` formula with `f = floor((n-1)/3)`). **New helper `bft_quorum_for(n)`** ‚Äî public so the future `pyde devnet --validators N` CLI + other orchestration can derive the same threshold. Table: n=1 ‚Üí q=1; n=4 ‚Üí q=3 (1 byzantine fault); n=7 ‚Üí q=5 (2 byzantine faults); n=128 ‚Üí q=85 (production spec, 42 byzantine faults). Tiny clusters (n < 4) degenerate to q=1 ‚Äî documented as a known limitation; real BFT validation requires n >= 4. **The headline live test `cluster_4_exchanges_vertices_via_gossipsub`** spawns 4 validators in-process under the BFT-tuned config + asserts `vertices_received >= 1` on at least one peer: proof that the gossipsub mesh formed AND vertices crossed the wire. n=4 is the smallest cluster where BFT quorum is non-trivial (q=3 vs q=1 for n<=3) AND where libp2p gossipsub's default `mesh_n_low = 4` JUST meets the well-connected threshold. **Wave commit floor**: still best-effort under this config (mesh formation is timing-dependent at the boundary); a future mesh-tuning PR that overrides `mesh_n_low` for small clusters will lift the assertion to `waves_committed >= 1`. 3 new tests: BFT quorum formula locked against the spec; cluster configs reflect the BFT tuning; live 4-validator gossipsub exchange. 556 node-lib tests passing. ‚Äî PR [#270](https://github.com/pyde-net/engine/pull/270)
- [x] **Small-cluster gossipsub mesh tuning for multi-validator devnet (testnet-critical)** ‚Äî closes the gossipsub-mesh out-of-scope item from #270. Pre-fix, multi-validator devnet at N<6 was effectively running without a converged gossipsub mesh: production libp2p defaults (`mesh_n_low=5`, `mesh_n=6`, `mesh_n_high=12`) assume ‚â•6 peers in the swarm; small clusters can't fill `mesh_n_low=5` against 3 other peers, so the mesh stayed in heartbeat-driven recovery and cross-vertex gossip never converged ‚Äî vertices got published locally but peers didn't pick them up. **Fix**: `build_gossipsub(keypair, small_cluster_mesh: bool)` overrides the mesh parameters to small-cluster-friendly values when `small_cluster_mesh = true` ‚Äî `mesh_n_low = 1`, `mesh_n = 2`, `mesh_n_high = 4`, `mesh_outbound_min = 0`. These satisfy libp2p's inequalities `outbound_min <= n_low <= n <= n_high` AND `outbound_min <= n/2`. **Plumbed end-to-end**: flag flows `ValidatorRunConfig.small_cluster_mesh` ‚Üí `ValidatorRuntimeConfig.small_cluster_mesh` ‚Üí `NetworkRunner::from_keypair` ‚Üí `Network::new` ‚Üí `build_swarm` ‚Üí `build_gossipsub`. Every site documents "Never set true in production." **`MultiValidatorCluster::build_cluster(n, ...)` sets it to `true` automatically** ‚Äî the helper exists exclusively for small clusters, so the tuning is the only sensible default. **Measured impact**: pre-fix 4-validator cluster `vertices_received` ranged 0-1 per validator over an 8s window (best-effort, mesh hadn't formed); post-fix `vertices_received` is 200+ per validator ‚Äî the mesh forms in <1s and cross-validator gossip is steady. New test `cluster_4_steady_vertex_throughput_under_small_cluster_mesh` locks the floor at ‚â•100 vertices_received per validator. **Out of scope (next PR)**: `waves_committed >= 1` doesn't yet fire even with the mesh converged. Root cause is `producer_quorum = 1` (solo-cascade): each validator advances its local rounds independently, so Mysticeti 3-stage commit can't find round-aligned vertices from `support_quorum` distinct producers. Fix is to gate producer vertex production on peer parents (raise `producer_quorum` to match the support quorum for small clusters). 8 cluster tests pass; 557 node-lib + 74 net = 631 tests, 0 failed. ‚Äî PR [#271](https://github.com/pyde-net/engine/pull/271)
- [x] **Receive-side structural quorum matches producer quorum (testnet-critical bug fix)** ‚Äî closes a load-bearing multi-validator devnet bug discovered while investigating "200+ vertices received but 0 waves committed" from #271. Pre-fix, the vertex-receive path in `mainloop::handle_vertex_bytes` checked `detect_slashable_structural_violation(v, QUORUM=85)` against EVERY inbound peer vertex's `parent_vertex_refs.len()`. Small clusters at N<85 had producers emitting vertices with ‚â§N parents ‚Äî every peer vertex was flagged as a slashable `InsufficientParentQuorum` violation and DROPPED pre-insert. The receive-side hardcoded QUORUM meant the local DAG NEVER saw peer vertices on a small cluster, even though the gossip layer was carrying them. The wave-committer's `commit_attempts` metric showed it trying ~195 times in 8 seconds, but every attempt returned `Pending` because Mysticeti's 3-stage rule couldn't be satisfied ‚Äî there were no peer vertices in the local DAG to support the anchor. **Measured impact** on a 4-validator cluster: pre-fix 263 vertices received per validator, **0 inserted**; post-fix 264 received, **264 inserted**. Every peer vertex now makes it into the local DAG. **Fix**: new `ValidatorMainLoop::with_structural_quorum(q)` builder overrides the receive-side quorum used by both `detect_slashable_structural_violation` AND the `AnchorAttestationBuffer`'s per-round majority threshold. `run_validator_with_hooks` passes `config.producer_quorum.unwrap_or(QUORUM)` as the structural quorum ‚Äî that's the minimum parent count actually-honest producers emit on this cluster's wire, so any vertex below that floor genuinely IS a structural violation, but vertices at-or-above the cluster's own producer quorum are valid. Production keeps the spec default (QUORUM=85); cluster builds inherit `producer_quorum=1` so receive-side quorum = 1 + peer vertices accept. **Plumbing**: `mainloop::dispatch(...)` + `handle_vertex_bytes(...)` take a `structural_quorum: usize` parameter; 28 test sites in mainloop pass `pyde_engine_types::consensus::QUORUM` to preserve pre-fix behavior under the production default. **Still out of scope (next PR)**: `waves_committed >= 1` still doesn't fire even with vertices flowing into local DAGs. Root cause is the support-quorum-vs-parent-count handshake at round 1+: each producer's round-1 vertex must reference the anchor's round-0 vertex, which requires the peer round-0 vertex to have ARRIVED before the producer's tick fires. Producers race ahead at 50-200ms tick faster than gossipsub mesh formation (~1s heartbeat). Fix is either a startup grace period that waits for mesh formation OR a producer_quorum >= 2 strategy that doesn't gridlock at boot. **Headline test** `cluster_4_inserts_peer_vertices_after_structural_quorum_fix` spawns 4 validators + asserts `vertices_inserted >= 100` per validator in 10s ‚Äî passes consistently. 558 node-lib + 74 net = 632 tests, 0 failed. ‚Äî PR [#272](https://github.com/pyde-net/engine/pull/272)
- [x] **VertexProducer startup_delay for multi-validator mesh warm-up (testnet investigation continuation)** ‚Äî investigation follow-up to #272. With the receive-side structural quorum fix in place, the next step toward `waves_committed >= 1` in 4-validator clusters was tuning `producer_quorum`. Solo-cascade (`producer_quorum=1`) doesn't produce cross-validator support refs at R+1 (each producer's round-1 vertex references only its own round-0 vertex, never the anchor); `producer_quorum=2` would force round-aligned production but deadlocks at boot because round 0 publishes ONCE before the libp2p gossipsub mesh has formed via heartbeat ‚Äî the message goes to an empty fanout, peers never receive round 0, q=2 at round 1 never satisfies, no further publishes, no traffic to drive mesh formation. Total cluster gridlock. **What this PR adds**: `VertexProducerConfig.startup_delay: Duration` ‚Äî one-shot sleep at the top of `VertexProducer::run` before the first emit. Honours shutdown so quick teardown still exits cleanly. Plumbed through `ValidatorRunConfig.producer_startup_delay_ms: Option<u64>` ‚Üí validator construction. The cluster builder sets `startup_delay = 1500ms` (longer than libp2p gossipsub's ~1s heartbeat) ‚Äî hypothesis: give the mesh time to form before round 0 publishes. **Measured outcome**: with the delay + `producer_quorum=1`, 4-validator cluster sustains **600+ vertices received per validator over 15s** (locked in new test `cluster_4_sustains_high_vertex_throughput_with_startup_delay`). **Wave commit: still pending**. With q=1 producer races, vertices flow, but cross-validator support refs at R+1 are missing ‚Äî waves don't commit. With q=2 + startup_delay=1500ms cluster STILL gridlocks (3-4 vertices received total instead of 660). Heartbeat-only mesh formation isn't reliable enough; the mesh needs ongoing traffic to maintain GRAFT links ‚Äî round-0-only publishing doesn't keep it alive. **Out of scope (next PR)**: a mesh warm-up mechanism that drives GRAFT exchange without relying on the producer's round emits ‚Äî either a faster heartbeat interval for small clusters, explicit `add_explicit_peer` libp2p calls to force mesh membership, or a small "heartbeat ping" topic producers publish to on a faster cadence. Once mesh formation is decoupled from publish traffic, `producer_quorum=2` should work and waves commit. 1 new test; 558 node-lib tests passing; 9 cluster tests pass. ‚Äî PR [#273](https://github.com/pyde-net/engine/pull/273)
- [x] **`pyde validator --state-sync` for soft-testnet onboarding (MC-3.1 first piece)** ‚Äî opens the soft-testnet state-sync surface. Pre-fix, `pyde validator` had only one onboarding path: `--genesis <manifest>` which seeded a fresh chain from genesis. To join an existing chain a new validator had to either (a) get out-of-band copies of the chain's state directory or (b) replay every wave from genesis through gossip ‚Äî neither workable for a real testnet. This PR adds `pyde validator --state-sync <FILE_OR_URL>` mirroring the existing `pyde devnet --fork` flow. File mode reads a local borsh-encoded `SnapshotBundle`; URL mode POSTs `pyde_getSnapshot` against the supplied endpoint + base64-decodes the result. The validator fetches the snapshot, applies it to a freshly-opened state store BEFORE the genesis-seeding gate, skips the genesis gate when state-sync succeeded (state is already populated), and advances `WaveCommitterConfig.initial_wave_id_floor` to `manifest.wave_id` so consensus resumes at the synced wave instead of replaying from 0. **What lands**: new CLI flag `--state-sync <FILE_OR_URL>` on `pyde validator`; new `ValidatorRunConfig.state_sync_source: Option<ForkSource>` field; new `ValidatorRunError::StateSync(String)` variant; `state_sync_source` + `genesis_path` mutually exclusive at CLI dispatch with a clear error; `prefetch_fork_bundle` + `apply_prefetched_bundle` + `ForkSource::display` bumped from private to `pub(crate)` so the validator path can call them; `pub(crate) use` in `devnet/mod.rs` keeps the crate-internal API clean. **What's NOT in scope (next PRs)**: weak-subjectivity checkpoint verification (current path trusts the source URL ‚Äî operators supply a peer they trust like their own bootnode or an audited validator; chunk-by-chunk verification against committee threshold sigs is a follow-up); parallel chunk fetch over libp2p streams (current is one HTTP POST fetching the whole bundle ‚Äî for large state stores this won't scale); `pyde_getSnapshotManifest` lightweight RPC (manifest-only fetch); tail-replay after snapshot apply (current resumes consensus at `manifest.wave_id`; production state sync replays the wave-log tail to catch up to the live chain). **Tests**: 2 new ‚Äî `validator_state_syncs_from_local_snapshot_file` builds a snapshot at wave 7, writes to disk, spawns validator with `--state-sync <path>`, confirms clean boot; `validator_state_sync_and_genesis_combined_is_rejected_at_cli` exercises the mutex check. 560 node-lib + 74 net = 634 tests, 0 failed. ‚Äî PR [#274](https://github.com/pyde-net/engine/pull/274)

**Smoke tests + devnet topology**
- [ ] 1-validator local devnet (parity with the MC-2 spike but now backed by real Œ≤ + Œ≥ ‚Äî replaces `pyde devnet --smoke`)
- [ ] 4-validator local devnet on one machine (real libp2p, real DKG, real beacon)
- [ ] 7-validator local devnet (validates committee selection + Mysticeti 3-stage at small-but-realistic committee size; QUORUM scaled down via `select_anchor_for_testing`)
- [ ] Smoke scenarios: simple transfer, contract deploy, view call (cross_call_static), state-mutating cross-call, event emission, event subscription, sender-key rotation, single-validator slash-evidence dry-run
- [ ] Crash + restart: kill -9 a validator mid-wave, verify state survives + validator rejoins committee on restart (Œ≤.1 PR-5e + Œ≥ chain-halt-recovery cover the primitives ‚Äî this test confirms the integration)

#### Open questions to settle before MC-2 lands

1. ~~**`receipts_cf` + `txs_cf` ownership**~~ ‚Äî **resolved**: landed in state crate via PR [#132](https://github.com/pyde-net/engine/pull/132). Rationale: state already owns every persistent CF; node-owned CFs would mean either (a) two RocksDB instances or (b) a shared registry ‚Äî both add coordination burden.
2. **`consensus_store` schema** ‚Äî Œ≥ has a `consensus_store` trait; what's the persistent layout? Vertex+round indexes, or vertices in RocksDB + indexes in memory?
3. ~~**WAL on the mempool**~~ ‚Äî **resolved: no WAL in v1.** Rationale (capital-allocation lens): the only crash window where a WAL would save a tx is "submitted via RPC + crash before gossip-broadcast." Gossip already provides redundancy ‚Äî if even one peer received the tx pre-crash, it survives (and wallets typically retry on no-receipt anyway). Adding a per-tx WAL trades a small UX edge case (re-submit-after-crash for a small set of solo-validator-RPC users) against write amplification on every admission and bootstrap complexity. v2 reconsiders if operator telemetry shows the crash-window cost is real. The MempoolStats counters (`admitted_local`, `admitted_gossiped`) are the canary ‚Äî if `admitted_local` grossly outpaces `admitted_gossiped` after MC-2 ships, the RPC-direct submission pattern is heavy and the case for WAL strengthens.
4. ~~**Base fee update cadence**~~ ‚Äî **resolved: per-wave update at commit time, EIP-1559 elasticity** (gas target = 50% of `BLOCK_GAS_MAX`). Rationale: Pyde's wave maps to Ethereum's "block" for fee-economics purposes ‚Äî each commit shifts base fee up/down by ‚â§12.5% based on `wave_gas_used / wave_gas_target` (the canonical EIP-1559 formula Œ≤.3 PR-2 already encodes). The node hooks into the consensus commit path: after `commit_with_events` returns, compute the new base_fee + call `WasmExecutorAdapter::update_base_fee(new)` + `PydeMempoolView::update_base_fee(new)` (both now interior-mutable per PR [#133](https://github.com/pyde-net/engine/pull/133) + PR [#129](https://github.com/pyde-net/engine/pull/129)). Two consumers updated in lockstep keep `Receipt::fee_paid` math and mempool `InsufficientBalance` admission threshold consistent. **Gas target choice (50%)** matches Ethereum's tuning since the EIP-1559 paper; v2 may tune up/down if Pyde's elastic-round timing makes 50% mis-targeted (e.g., if waves see consistent under- or over-utilisation).
5. **Light client cutoff** ‚Äî light client lands at MC-3 (state sync). For MC-2, `pyde light` could be a stub that returns "MC-3" rather than building partial.
6. **Two-pass `WaveCommitter.tick_for_testing` reinstatement** ‚Äî Œ≥.15 / Œ≥.16's 2 `#[ignore]`'d validator-integration tests need a multi-validator coordination harness; MC-2's 4+7-validator devnets are the natural test rigs.

**MC-2 BAR:** local devnet running with sub-second commits and successful end-to-end tx flow. Three smoke contracts (one transfer, one storage R/W, one cross_call) deploy and operate correctly. All MC-1 deliverables integrated. `pyde validator --config testnet.toml` runs unattended for ‚â•1 hour without halting on a 7-validator devnet.

---

## MC-3 ‚Äî STATE SYNC + PARACHAIN ACTIVATION `[SEQ] ‚Üí MC-2` ‚Äî Œ≤ + Œ≥ joint

### 3.1 State sync (Œ≥-led, Œ≤ co-owns snapshot generation)

- [ ] Snapshot generation (background on archive nodes + volunteer-served)
  - Walk JMT at target wave version
  - Chunk into ~50MB pieces with range proofs
  - Persist chunks; publish SnapshotManifest
- [ ] `pyde_getSnapshotManifest` RPC handler
- [ ] Snapshot chunk serving over libp2p streams (parallel from multiple peers)
- [ ] Weak-subjectivity checkpoint format (wave_id + dual state_roots + committee threshold sig)
- [ ] WS checkpoint distribution
- [ ] New-validator sync flow (download manifest, parallel chunk fetch, verify, write, replay tail)
- [ ] Sync time target (~40 min for fresh sync)
- [ ] Three-tier node model: archive / pruned / light client

### 3.2 Parachain framework activation (Œ≤ + Œ≥ joint)

- [ ] Parachain account structure (versions, balance, config, state_root, owner deposit, status)
- [ ] Parachain ID derivation (`Poseidon2("pyde-parachain:" || name)`)
- [ ] Deploy flow (owner deposit, WASM validation, registry write)
- [ ] Upgrade flow (proposal, equal-power voting, scheduled activation)
- [ ] Pause / kill (operational lifecycle)
- [ ] State subtree partitioning (`parachain_id[..16]` PIP-2 prefix)
- [ ] Cross-parachain messaging (rate-limited, threshold-signed; Œ≥ networking; Œ≤ host fn)
- [ ] `cross_call` callback mechanism (success / error / timeout flows)
- [ ] Version manifest in wave-commit records (replay correctness)
- [ ] Reference parachains: price-feed oracle + confidential-vote parachain

**MC-3 BAR:** fresh validator can sync to current head in under 1 hour and become committee-eligible. An author deploys a parachain; validators opt in; cross_call from a smart contract to the parachain works with a callback returning a result.

**MC-4 BAR:** performance numbers published per the harness discipline; failure-handling runbooks battle-tested in a controlled environment.

## MC-5 ‚Äî VALIDATION + MAINNET LAUNCH `[SEQ] ‚Üí MC-4`

Spec: Chapter 19 (Launch Strategy).

### 5.1 External audits (5 specialist tracks)

- [ ] Consensus layer (Mysticeti DAG, anchor selection, finality, slashing)
- [ ] WASM execution layer (host functions, fuel-to-gas, validation gate, hybrid scheduler)
- [ ] Cryptography (FALCON, Kyber, Blake3, Poseidon2, threshold, PSS) ‚Äî `pyde-crypto`
- [ ] Networking (libp2p config, gossipsub, peer discovery, sentry pattern, DDoS)
- [ ] `otigen` toolchain (codegen, ABI extraction, deploy flow, wallet)

### 5.2 Incentivized testnet

- [ ] Reference dApps: DEX, lending market, NFT marketplace
- [ ] Funded bug bounty at mainnet tier
- [ ] Multi-month soak with real user traffic
- [ ] Remediate community-found issues before launch

### 5.3 Mainnet candidate

- [ ] Final genesis configuration
- [ ] Initial validator set (‚â•32 validators, geographically distributed)
- [ ] Day-one ecosystem partners (‚â•3-5 parachains/dApps)
- [ ] Token distribution finalized
- [ ] Bug bounty scaled to mainnet tier
- [ ] Mainnet launch

**MC-5 BAR:** mainnet live. All MC-0 through MC-4 work integrated, audited, stress-tested, soak-passed.

---

## Beyond V1 `[PAR]` ‚Äî post-mainnet research/dev directions

- ZK-aggregated FALCON signatures (the path to dramatic signature-verification throughput gains)
- zk-WASM proven execution
- Cross-chain bridges (Ethereum, Bitcoin, others) with proven-security mechanisms
- **Programmable accounts + native session keys** ‚Äî scoped, bounded, revocable dApp delegation. Native at the protocol (vs Ethereum's ERC-4337 retrofit). See Chapter 11 *Session keys (v2)* and `companion/DESIGN.md` for the design + v1 reservations the surfaces depend on.
- State-expiration policy
- Tier 2/3 wallet preview (heuristics + LLM analysis) per [[ai-wallet-preview-direction]]

### V1 reservations that create room for v2 features

V1 ships *interfaces*; v2 ships *implementations*. Discipline: don't reach into v2 while v1 is shipping, but reserve the protocol surfaces v2 needs so contracts written today survive the upgrade unchanged.

| v2 feature | v1 reservation | Cost at v1 |
| --- | --- | --- |
| Programmable accounts | `AuthKeys::Programmable` enum tag `0x03` | Enum variant, unused ‚Äî ~zero |
| Programmable accounts | Account `code_hash` + `storage_root` (unified with contracts) | Already shipped (account/contract account shape unified) |
| Session keys | WASM "policy mode" execution flag | Reserved-but-not-implemented ‚Äî ~zero |
| Session keys | Multisig signature pipeline | Already shipped (serves multisig + future session-key flows) |
| ZK light clients | Poseidon2 state root + ZK-friendly primitives | Already shipped (dual-hash JMT, no Blake3 in proof-bearing paths) |
| Parachains (further depth) | `cross_call` host fn, `HardFinalityCert` primitive, async callback slots | Already shipped (Chapter 13, `companion/PARACHAIN_DESIGN.md`) |

The discipline: every entry above is something the v1 protocol can ship for ~zero marginal cost, but skipping any one of them would force a hard-fork rewrite when v2 lands. Reserving them now is cheap insurance.

---

## End-to-end flow: user ‚Üí execution ‚Üí user

For context on what all this protocol work enables, here's the full E2E flow once all chunks are landed:

```text
1. USER: opens wallet, builds tx (function call, args, gas budget)
2. WALLET: runs local wasmtime preview ‚Üí shows state changes, gas estimate, events
3. USER: reviews preview, signs (FALCON-512)
4. WALLET: optionally encrypts under committee threshold key (Kyber-768)
5. WALLET ‚Üí RPC: pyde_sendRawTransaction(signed_tx)
6. RPC: validates ingress (sig, balance, nonce, gas, chain_id)
7. RPC ‚Üí MEMPOOL WORKER: forwards via libp2p
8. WORKER: adds to pending batch
9. WORKER: seals batch, gossipps to other workers, collects ‚â•85 certifications
10. WORKER ‚Üí PRIMARY: certified batch_hash available for inclusion
11. PRIMARY: produces vertex with batch_hash in batch_refs (+ decryption shares if applicable)
12. VERTEX: gossipped via libp2p/gossipsub on pyde/vertices/1 topic
13. DAG: grows; each round adds 128 vertices
14. ANCHOR: deterministically selected via Hash(beacon, round, prev_root) mod 128
15. SUPPORT: round R+2's 85+ vertices transitively reference anchor ‚Üí 3-stage support
16. COMMIT: subdag walk (BFS-for-set + canonical sort)
17. DECRYPT: batch threshold-decrypt all encrypted txs in subdag (shares already piggybacked)
18. SCHEDULE: hybrid scheduler (static access + Block-STM) partitions for parallel execution
19. EXECUTE: wasmtime runs each tx (per-tx overlays for isolation; success ‚Üí merge, trap ‚Üí discard)
20. STATE: changes accumulate in DashMap ‚Üí JMT update ‚Üí new state_root
21. SIGN: committee FALCON-signs (wave_id, blake3_root, poseidon2_root)
22. PERSIST: WaveCommitRecord synchronously to disk; vertices/batches/receipts lazily
23. FINALITY: 85+ sigs collected ‚Üí HardFinalityCert formed
24. USER ‚Üê RPC: pyde_getTransactionReceipt(tx_hash) returns success/revert + state changes + gas used
25. USER: sees confirmation in wallet UI

Total wall-clock from step 5 (submit) to step 25 (confirmation visible): ~500ms-1s under normal conditions.
```

Each step maps to specific chunks in the roadmap. The full path traverses MC-2 (consensus, execution, state, crypto, network, accounts, slashing) end-to-end, with MC-3 (otigen, SDKs, wallet) at the boundaries.

---

## Stream dependency matrix (cross-MC view)

| Item | Owning stream | Depends on | Used by |
|------|---------------|------------|---------|
| MC-0 Interface foundation | main session | (none) | All MC-1 streams |
| MC-1 Œ± Toolchain | Œ± | MC-0 + `HOST_FN_ABI_SPEC` | Contract authors; MC-2 deploy testing |
| MC-1 Œ≤.1 State | Œ≤ | MC-0 | Œ≤.4 (wasm-exec); Œ≥.1 (consensus reads state_root); MC-3 state sync |
| MC-1 Œ≤.2 Account | Œ≤ | MC-0 + `pyde-crypto` | Œ≤.3 (tx sender validation); Œ≤.4 (host context); Œ≥.4 (validator txs) |
| MC-1 Œ≤.3 Tx | Œ≤ | MC-0 + Œ≤.2 + `pyde-crypto` | Œ≤.4 (tx dispatch); Œ≤.5 (mempool); Œ≥ (consensus orderable items) |
| MC-1 Œ≤.4 WASM Execution | Œ≤ | MC-0 + Œ≤.1 + Œ≤.2 + Œ≤.3 | MC-1 Œ± (`pyde.abi` consumers); Œ≥ (consensus invokes via `Executor`); MC-3 parachain runtime |
| MC-1 Œ≤.5 Mempool | Œ≤ | MC-0 + Œ≤.3 | Œ≥.1 (reads via `MempoolView`); Œ≥.2 (gossip submission) |
| MC-1 Œ≥.1 Consensus | Œ≥ | MC-0 + `pyde-crypto` | Œ≥.5 (node binary drives consensus); MC-2 integration |
| MC-1 Œ≥.2 Net | Œ≥ | MC-0 | Œ≥.1 (gossip transport); Œ≤.5 (tx propagation) |
| MC-1 Œ≥.3 DKG | Œ≥ | MC-0 + `pyde-crypto` | Œ≥.1 (threshold decryption keys); Œ≤.4 (threshold_encrypt/decrypt) |
| MC-1 Œ≥.4 Slashing + Validator Lifecycle | Œ≥ | MC-0 + Œ≥.1 + Œ≤.3 | Œ≥.5 (RPC validator endpoints); consensus integrity |
| MC-1 Œ≥.5 Node binary | Œ≥ | All Œ≤ + Œ≥ crates via traits | The deployable artifact |
| MC-2 Integration | Œ≥-led | All MC-1 streams done | Devnet & all of MC-3-5 |
| MC-3 State Sync + Parachain | Œ≤ + Œ≥ joint | MC-2 | New validators (sync); parachain authors |
| MC-4 Performance + Failure | shared | MC-2 + MC-3 functional | Mainnet readiness |
| MC-5 Validation + Launch | main | All preceding | Mainnet live |

---

## Operating principle

The bias of this roadmap is **honesty over optimism**. No chunk ships before its bar is met. No item is checked off until the work behind it is actually done. If something turns out to be wrong, it gets honestly rewritten ‚Äî including this roadmap.

The work is the work. It ships when it is ready.
